Direct user report: uploaded a real Thndr Invoice PDF for a new ABUK buy and it stayed permanently "Blocked — needs verification" since ABUK already had an existing position and no *new* broker "My Position" screenshot was uploaded alongside it. Traced back to the project's very first request in this session — "verification via broker screenshot **or** invoice" — which only ever got half-built: `ThndrParser`'s Invoice format (`parseInvoiceTextImpl`) produces a trade candidate, never a `PositionVerification`, so the two-phase gate (`checkTickerMatch`, confirmed explicitly in an earlier sprint) always demanded a fresh position recount even for a single incremental invoice-sourced buy — the invoice's own standardized, labeled fields were never treated as sufficient proof on their own. Confirmed directly with the user (not assumed) that an invoice should be trusted as its own verification, matching the original request, since a full position re-screenshot for every single invoice import is unreasonable friction.

- `ParsedTradeCandidate` gained `source?: "invoice"`, set by `parseInvoiceTextImpl`; every other parse path (OCR'd statements/orders screens) leaves it undefined.
- **`checkTickerMatch`** (`importVerification.ts`) gained a new `invoice-verified` outcome: when a ticker has no broker verification at all *and* every still-pending Buy/Sell for it came from an invoice, it's trivially matched — mirroring the existing `closed-position`/`no-shares-to-verify` trivial-match cases. Deliberately conservative: if a broker screenshot *is* present and it actually mismatches, the mismatch still blocks regardless of invoice source, since a real discrepancy (e.g. a duplicate invoice) shouldn't be silently overridden.
- **Import page** shows a new "Verified by invoice" badge for this case; the row proceeds straight to "Ready — click Confirm above" with no Mismatch/blocked messaging.
- 5 new tests: 4 in `importVerification.test.ts` (invoice-verified when unverified, still blocks a genuine mismatch even with an invoice source, doesn't invoice-verify a mixed batch), 1 in `ImportPage.test.tsx` (`TickerGroupCard` renders the badge and skips all blocked messaging); plus updated `ThndrParser.test.ts` assertions confirming invoice-parsed candidates carry `source: "invoice"` and OCR'd ones don't — 308 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: recorded an existing ABUK position (27 shares) via Record Buy, then seeded Import with one new invoice-sourced Buy candidate (10 shares) and no verification at all — confirmed "Verified by invoice" showed immediately with Confirm enabled, and that confirming landed the new trade correctly alongside the original, for a combined 37-share position.

### Post-sprint-8 — a bulk re-upload the ledger already reconciles, just split into different lots

Direct user report with screenshots across six tickers (ABUK, COMI, CSAG, EAST, ORAS, PHAR): each showed "Mismatch" in Import while looking correctly matched in the portfolio's own Holdings. For EAST and ORAS specifically, the extracted total was *exactly double* the broker's verified count (EAST: 350 vs 175; ORAS: 18 vs 9) with *no* row flagged as a duplicate by either existing dedup mechanism. Root cause: both prior duplicate fixes (PHAR's sibling check, ARCC's existing-trade check) require an individual pending candidate to match a specific sibling or ledger trade by exact ticker+date+shares. Here the ticker's already-committed position was recorded with a *different* lot/date split than this new, more granular extraction (e.g. from a bulk statement re-upload covering full order history) — the totals agree, but no single row lines up with a single existing trade, so nothing was ever flagged despite the broker independently confirming the ledger was already correct.

- **`checkTickerMatch`** (`importVerification.ts`) gained a new `alreadyFullyRecorded` flag on a "mismatch" result: true when the ticker's already-committed shares *alone*, before this batch's pending candidates, already reconcile exactly against the broker's verified count — direct evidence the ledger was already correct and every pending candidate is redescribing shares already accounted for, not a genuinely new transaction. Deliberately narrow: only fires when the existing-alone total matches the broker exactly, so a real incremental purchase (existing + genuinely new shares happening to also reconcile against a *different*, larger verified count) is never miscategorized.
- **Import page** shows a distinct banner + a "Discard all pending for {ticker}" bulk action for this case, doing the aggregate equivalent of "Clear suspected duplicates" without needing any row to individually match — it only ever removes still-pending Buy/Sell candidates, never touching the verification (the ground truth the decision rests on) or already-committed trades.
- 4 new tests: 2 in `importVerification.test.ts` (flags `alreadyFullyRecorded` when the ledger alone reconciles, doesn't flag a genuine mismatch the ledger doesn't already explain), 2 in `ImportPage.test.tsx` (`TickerGroupCard` shows the bulk-discard banner/button for the EAST shape, shows the plain Mismatch banner with no bulk-discard offer for a mismatch that doesn't fit) — 312 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: recorded EAST as a single existing 175-share lot (a different date/price than any of the new rows), then seeded Import with the reported 5-lot breakdown (15/23/50/20/67 shares) plus a fresh 175-unit verification — reproduced the exact banner and total; clicking "Discard all pending for EAST" collapsed it straight to "Verified" with Confirm enabled, and confirming left the original single 175-share trade untouched with nothing new added.
- ABUK, COMI, CSAG, PHAR should now resolve the same way if their shape matches (existing-alone already reconciling with the broker); ORHD's numbers (99 vs 74, not an exact multiple) don't fit this pattern and likely need a fresh, complete screenshot to diagnose — asked the user to check post-deploy and send one if still stuck.

### Post-sprint-8 — a verified ticker can confirm on its own, independent of any other stuck ticker

Direct user follow-up: ORWE showed "Verified" in Import (its existing 89-share position plus 3 new buys correctly reconciled to the broker's 177), yet "Confirm — Distribute to Portfolios" was greyed out entirely. Root cause: the button's `disabled` condition (and `confirmAndDistributeAll` itself) required *every* ticker in the current batch to be matched — a single other still-stuck ticker (ORHD) blocked every already-verified ticker in the same batch from distributing at all, even though `commitTickerGroup` only ever commits matched tickers one at a time internally. This was originally a deliberate, explicitly-confirmed design (Sprint 7: "only once every ticker matches... an explicit confirmation actually distributes"), but in practice it meant one hard-to-resolve ticker held every other correct one hostage. Confirmed directly with the user (not assumed) that a verified ticker should be able to confirm independently.

- `confirmAndDistributeAll` no longer requires every ticker to match — it now commits whichever tickers are currently matched (as it already did internally), gated only on at least one being ready. Its button label/tooltip adapts: "Confirm — Distribute to Portfolios" when everything's ready, "Confirm All Verified (N)" with a tooltip explaining the rest stay pending when the batch is partial.
- New **`confirmTicker(ticker)`** and a per-ticker "Confirm {ticker}" button in `TickerGroupCard`'s header, shown whenever that one ticker is matched and portfolio-resolved — lets it distribute immediately without waiting on any other still-stuck ticker in the same batch.
- 2 new tests in `ImportPage.test.tsx` (`TickerGroupCard` shows "Confirm {ticker}" and fires the callback once matched; the button is absent while still unmatched) — 314 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: seeded a batch with ORWE (matched: 89 existing + 88 new = 177, reconciling with a fresh broker screenshot) alongside ORHD (a genuine, unrelated 99-vs-74 mismatch) — confirmed the global button read "Confirm All Verified (1)" and was enabled (previously fully disabled), and that clicking "Confirm ORWE" committed exactly ORWE's 3 buys (89+20+45+23 = 177 shares total) while leaving ORHD completely untouched and still blocked.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — a successfully committed row showed a false "Duplicate" badge against itself

Direct user follow-up with screenshots: rows already marked "Added" (SKPC, ORWE — both freshly confirmed via the per-ticker Confirm button above) also showed a red "Duplicate" badge, which read as a contradiction — if it's genuinely a duplicate, why did it commit at all? Root cause: the per-row `duplicateMatch` check re-runs on every render against the live `existingTrades` list, which by the time a row shows "Added" already includes the real `Trade` that row's own commit just created — with identical ticker/date/shares/price by construction, so the row's own candidate always found an "exact" match against *itself*, not a genuine separate duplicate.

- `duplicateMatch` (`ImportPage.tsx`) now accepts an optional `ownTradeId` and excludes that specific trade from the comparison pool. `TickerGroupCard` passes each Buy row's own `addedTradeIds[entry.key]` (already tracked for the auto-added-row delete feature) so a row only ever compares against *other* trades, never the one it just became.
- Scoped to Buys, where this was confirmed and reproducible (`addedTradeIds` already exists for exactly this purpose). Sells don't track an equivalent allocation id yet, so this fix doesn't touch `CandidateRow` — no report of the same symptom there yet.
- A genuine "possible duplicate" (different price, same ticker/date/shares as some *other* already-recorded trade) still keeps showing its badge after commit, unchanged — that persistence was always intentional, flagging a real look-alike worth a second look, not a false self-match.
- 1 new test in `ImportPage.test.tsx` (asserts `duplicateMatch` is called with the row's own committed trade id, and that an added row shows no "Duplicate" text) — 315 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: seeded and confirmed a closed-position SKPC-shaped ticker (two Buys + a Sell, matching the reported screenshot) and confirmed both committed Buy rows read "Added" with no "Duplicate" text anywhere on the card.

### Post-sprint-8 — a fourth verification path: two independent documents agreeing on the same transaction

Direct user follow-up on the still-stuck ORHD ticker (99 vs 74, no individual row a duplicate of anything): asked what document type would resolve it. Rather than guessing, asked the user to choose between candidate designs; they deferred the choice back, so this picked the option that generalizes the existing invoice-trust rule (Sprint 8, "invoice alone can verify its own transaction") to a second, broader case: an OCR'd screenshot/statement read of a transaction, independently corroborated by a standardized Invoice for the *same* transaction, is at least as trustworthy as an invoice alone — and resolves exactly the tickers a broker "My Position" total can't, where the mismatch hides inside a row nothing else ever corroborated.

- **`findCrossSourceVerifiedKeys`** (`duplicateDetection.ts`, new): groups pending candidates by the same ticker+side+date+share-count signature the sibling-duplicate check already uses, and flags every entry in a group containing *both* an invoice-sourced and a non-invoice-sourced candidate — the same real transaction read by two independent sources. Refactored the shared grouping key into `pendingCandidateSignature`, reused by both functions.
- **`checkTickerMatch`** gained a `cross-verified` outcome, alongside a new `allPendingSelfVerified` param: a ticker with no broker verification at all, where every still-pending candidate is either invoice-sourced or cross-verified, no longer needs a "My Position" screenshot. Deliberately the same shape as `invoice-verified` (only applies when no broker screenshot exists yet; an actual mismatch against a real screenshot still blocks) — cross-verification never overrides a genuine discrepancy, it only ever substitutes for a *missing* screenshot.
- This composes cleanly with the existing sibling-duplicate cleanup: a screenshot+invoice pair for the same transaction is *both* cross-verified (unblocking the ticker) *and* flagged "Suspected duplicate" (since committing both would double-book one real trade) — "Clear suspected duplicates" still collapses the pair to one row before Confirm, same as always.
- **Import page** shows a new "Verified — invoice matches screenshot" badge for this case.
- 9 new tests: 4 in `duplicateDetection.test.ts` (flags both sides of a genuine cross-source pair, ignores same-source pairs, ignores a lone invoice with nothing to corroborate, requires an exact signature match), 3 in `importVerification.test.ts` (cross-verified when unverified, invoice-verified takes priority when both apply, still blocks a genuine mismatch), 2 in `ImportPage.test.tsx` (`TickerGroupCard` renders the new badge and unblocks both rows) — 323 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: seeded a brand-new ticker with one screenshot-sourced Buy and one invoice-sourced Buy for the identical transaction (same ticker/date/shares, a different OCR'd price) and no broker verification at all — confirmed "Verified — invoice matches screenshot" showed immediately with both rows unblocked, the screenshot-sourced (lower-priced) row correctly flagged "Suspected duplicate," and that clearing it down to the invoice-priced row and confirming landed exactly one real trade.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — an out-of-range dividend sat in Import until it threw at commit time

Direct user report: a stray `Transactions before 2026-01-01 are not tracked: got 2024-08-21` error surfaced with no obvious way to resolve it — traced to an ORAS dividend from 2024. Every trade-extraction path already filters out a Buy/Sell dated before `TRACKING_START_DATE` at parse time (`trackedDateRange.ts`'s `partitionByRange`, applied in `parseStatementText`/`parseOrdersScreenText`/`parseOrderRowsText`) — but `ThndrParser.parseDividends` never got the same filter, so an out-of-range dividend extracted cleanly, sat in the pending pool looking completely normal, and only ever surfaced as a thrown error the moment the user tried to confirm it — the one place in the whole pipeline where hitting the tracking floor wasn't silent.

- `ThndrParser.parseDividends` now applies the same `partitionByRange` filter every other extraction method already uses — an out-of-range dividend is dropped before it ever reaches the pending pool, exactly like an out-of-range trade already was.
- **`ImportPage`** also self-heals any *already*-stuck session: a `useEffect` silently strips any out-of-range candidate or dividend still sitting in `pendingCandidates`/`pendingDividends` (from a session created before this fix, regardless of which extraction path let it through) — so a user with a session already jammed on this error doesn't need to re-upload anything to get unblocked.
- 2 new tests in `ThndrParser.test.ts` (excludes a pre-cutoff dividend entirely; still includes an on/after-cutoff one from the same document) — 325 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: seeded a session with the exact reported shape (a 2024-08-21 ORAS dividend already sitting in the pool, from before this fix, alongside a genuinely in-range one) — confirmed the stale dividend silently vanished from both the UI and the persisted session state on load, with the in-range dividend and the ticker's other rows completely unaffected.

### Post-sprint-8 — a manual "remove" button for a Mismatch no automated heuristic can explain

Direct user follow-up on ORHD's still-unresolved Mismatch (5 Buy rows, 99 vs 74 shares, none auto-flagged by any of the sibling-duplicate, existing-trade-duplicate, `alreadyFullyRecorded`, or cross-source checks above): asked for a small "remove" button on the suspected row so removing it can bring the ticker to Verified. None of the four automated heuristics built so far can catch every possible mismatch shape — each targets one specific, mechanically-detectable pattern, and a batch can legitimately contain an extra/wrong row that doesn't fit any of them. Rather than building a fifth heuristic for this one case, this gives the user direct agency: every still-pending row, not just ones already auto-flagged as a suspected duplicate, now has a small trash-icon button that discards it from the pending pool outright (nothing was ever committed, so there's nothing to refund) — letting the user test-remove whichever row they judge to be the extra/wrong one and see if the ticker's total then reconciles.

- **`AutoCommitRow`** (Buys) and **`CandidateRow`** (Sells) in `ImportPage.tsx`: the discard button no longer only renders when `canDiscard` (auto-flagged as a suspected duplicate) — it's now always available on any row that hasn't already been added/skipped/dismissed, styled distinctly (rose vs. slate) and titled differently depending on whether it's an auto-flagged duplicate or a manual removal.
- No change to `TickerGroupCard`'s wiring — both row types' `onDiscardPending` prop was already unconditionally passed through from earlier fixes; only the row components' internal gating of the button's *visibility* changed.
- 2 new tests in `ImportPage.test.tsx`/`AutoCommitRow.test.tsx` (a clean, unflagged Mismatch row still offers a working remove button; clicking it calls `onDiscardPending` with the right entry) — 326 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: seeded the exact ORHD shape (5 unflagged Buy rows totalling more shares than a broker screenshot verified) — confirmed all 5 rows show the small remove button, and that manually removing the two rows accounting for the excess collapsed the ticker straight to "Verified" with a working per-ticker Confirm button, exactly the workflow requested.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — Mismatch banner copy points at the actual likely cause

Direct user follow-up (still on ORHD): explained their own mental model for this class of problem — the broker's "My Position" screenshot is the trusted ground truth, so a Mismatch means the *extracted transaction list* is wrong, not the position count. To confirm the transaction list, request an Orders screenshot (broker order history); the discrepancy is likely a duplicate or a misclassified row. The previous banner copy ("fix a duplicate/missing row or re-upload") didn't say any of this — it read as a generic, undirected error rather than actionable guidance.

- Reworded the plain "mismatch" banner (`TickerGroupCard` in `ImportPage.tsx`) to state explicitly that the broker position screenshot is the trusted source, that the transaction list is the likely cause, and to suggest two concrete next steps: use the (already-shipped) remove icon on a suspected duplicate/misclassified row to test-fix the match, or upload an Orders screenshot to confirm the exact transaction count.
- Copy-only change — no new detection logic, since the underlying "which row is wrong" problem still isn't mechanically solvable in the general case (per the previous fix above).
- Updated the one existing test asserting on this banner's exact wording (`ImportPage.test.tsx`) — 326 total, no new tests needed for a text-only change.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: seeded the ORHD shape again and confirmed the new banner text renders correctly end to end.

### Post-sprint-8 — the mismatch auto-reconcile solver + wrong-ticker phantom detection

Direct user request ("عايزك تشوف حل مبتكر لحل النوع ده من المشكلات") backed by three screenshots that together revealed the underlying pattern: HRHO's pending pool contained rows at E£45–46/76 (HRHO trades at ~E£24–27) whose side/shares/dates exactly mirrored DELTA SUGAR's already-committed rows at near-identical prices — the same physical executions OCR'd twice under two different guessed tickers — while ORHD's long-standing 99-vs-74 mismatch had no individually-flaggable row at all. Two complementary mechanisms, both using evidence the app already captures but never exploited:

- **`suggestRemovalsToReconcile`** (`mismatchResolver.ts`, new service): for a mismatch none of the row-level heuristics can explain, the share arithmetic itself often can — enumerate which subset(s) of pending rows, removed, leave exactly the broker's verified count. When several subsets reconcile, the broker screenshot's second independently-verifiable number, the position's **avg cost** (captured all along on `PositionVerification.avgCost` but never used for this), ranks them: the subset whose remaining position lands closest to the broker's own avg is the one the broker's math agrees with. Ties fall back to lowest OCR confidence of the removed rows, then fewest rows. Existing lots' cost basis (remainingShares × entryPrice, summed via `Money`) folds into the implied avg; avg-cost ranking is deliberately skipped when pending sells are in play, since the implied avg would then depend on lot selection — exactly what ADR-002 refuses to guess. Emptying the batch is never suggested (that's `alreadyFullyRecorded`'s own action). Surfaced in the Mismatch banner as "Removing the N highlighted rows below leaves exactly {units}…" with per-row "Suggested removal" badges and a one-click "Remove suggested rows (N)" button — including an explicit "{k} other combinations would also reconcile" honesty note when the solution isn't unique.
- **`findWrongTickerCandidateKeys`** (`duplicateDetection.ts`): the one duplicate shape every existing check is blind to, because they all group within a ticker. A pending row is flagged as a phantom when a copy with the same side/date/share count *and a near-identical price* (≤10% — the discriminator against genuine same-day coincidences, which would carry unrelated prices) exists under a different ticker, and that copy outranks it: already committed to the ledger (trades for Buys, allocations for Sells; the pending read must not be a high-confidence anchored match), or still pending with strictly higher OCR confidence. Equal-confidence pending pairs flag neither — no basis to pick which ticker is the wrong guess. Surfaced as a "Likely {other}'s transaction" badge on the phantom row, next to the existing remove button.
- 16 new tests: 8 in `mismatchResolver.test.ts` (unique subset, avg-cost discrimination, existing-cost-basis folding, confidence tiebreak, mixed Buy/Sell removal without avg-cost ranking, no-solution, already-matched, never-empty-the-batch), 6 in `duplicateDetection.test.ts` (committed-trade phantom, price-proximity discriminator, high-confidence exemption, pending-pair confidence asymmetry, equal-confidence neither, Sell-vs-allocation), 2 in `ImportPage.test.tsx` (banner + badge + one-click removal wiring; wrong-ticker badge rendering) — 342 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: seeded ORHD's shape (5 Buys totalling 79 vs a 54-unit @ E£23.90 broker check — three subsets reconcile the count) and the HRHO/SUGR phantom pair in one batch. The solver picked exactly the two Medium rows via avg-cost ranking, badged them, and one click on "Remove suggested rows (2)" flipped ORHD straight to Verified with its Confirm button live; HRHO's phantom row showed "Likely SUGR's transaction" alongside its low-confidence badge.

### Post-sprint-8 — reconciliation arithmetic made visible, SUGR/MASR known tickers, and the Sell-side self-duplicate fix

Three direct user follow-ups in one report. (1) ORHD showed Verified while its visible rows (54 shares) didn't equal the broker's 74 — correct behavior (20 shares were already on the ledger from an earlier import; 20 + 54 = 74) but the UI never showed the arithmetic, so a *right* answer looked *wrong*. (2) DELTA SUGAR and MEDINET MASR HOUSING still appeared as company-name ticker groups — both were simply missing from `KNOWN_EGX_TICKERS`, so OCR's company-name fallback kicked in. (3) MEDINET's committed Sell row showed "Added" and "Duplicate" simultaneously — the exact self-comparison bug fixed for Buys earlier (`ownTradeId`, see above), which deliberately skipped Sells then for lack of a report; now reported.

- **`TickerMatchStatus.existingRemainingShares`** (`importVerification.ts`): the ledger-side of the reconciliation, surfaced instead of buried inside `netShares`. `TickerGroupCard` now shows "Matches the broker: 20 already on the ledger + 54 in this batch = 74 — the rows below only show this batch's part." on a verified ticker with existing shares, and both Mismatch banners break the total down the same way ("this batch's rows plus N already on the ledger total X…").
- **`KNOWN_EGX_TICKERS`** gained SUGR (DELTA SUGAR) and MASR (MEDINET MASR HOUSING), with sector entries (Food & Beverage / Real Estate) — future imports resolve these at high confidence, and the price-fetch universe picks both up automatically (it iterates the same list).
- **`tickerForCompanyNameFallback`** (`knownTickers.ts`, new): recognizes a ticker group whose "ticker" is really a known company name (exact normalized match only — a rename rewrites committed rows, so no fuzzy guessing) and drives a new one-click "Rename to {SUGR}" banner in `TickerGroupCard`, wired to the existing `renameTickerEverywhere` so already-committed trades under the fallback name are corrected too.
- **Sell-side self-duplicate exclusion**: `SellAllocationForm.onDone` now reports the `TradeAllocation` ids it created; Import stores them per entry key (`addedAllocationIds`, the Sell twin of `addedTradeIds`) and `duplicateMatch` excludes them from the row's own comparison — a committed Sell no longer "matches" the allocations it just became.
- 6 new tests: 3 in `knownTickers.test.ts` (fallback mapping, symbol-not-a-fallback, unknown returns undefined), 1 assertion in `importVerification.test.ts` (existingRemainingShares surfaced), 3 in `ImportPage.test.tsx` (breakdown line for the exact 20+54=74 shape; rename banner fires `onRenameTicker("SUGR")`; committed sell's duplicateMatch called with its own allocation ids and shows no Duplicate badge) — 348 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: recorded a real 20-share ORHD position via Record Buy, seeded a 54-share batch + 74-unit verification — the breakdown line rendered exactly as designed; seeded a "DELTA SUGAR" group — the rename banner appeared and one click converted the whole group to SUGR.

### Post-sprint-8 — last-close price semantics, visible freshness, and the discovery that the price feed never ran

Direct user request: use TradingView and/or Yahoo Finance for every current-price / unrealized-P/L calculation, and make sure the data reflects the last market close. Investigation found the pipeline *already* uses exactly those two sources (Yahoo primary, TradingView fallback, via `scripts/fetch-prices`) and every consumer already reads the single snapshot — but three real gaps, one of them severe:

- **The `Update Price Snapshot` workflow had NEVER run** (zero runs since the repo bootstrap) — `public/price-snapshot.json` was still the day-one placeholder (`asOf: null, prices: {}`), so the app has never had a real market price; every "current" value silently fell back to cost basis and unrealized P/L read as zero. Fixed operationally by dispatching the workflow after this shipped, and made *visible* in the product: `PriceFreshness` (below) shows an explicit "No market prices loaded yet — values fall back to cost basis" warning for exactly this state, which was previously indistinguishable from healthy.
- **Last-close capture**: the cron stopped at 12:30 UTC — in winter (Cairo UTC+2, close 12:30 UTC) the final run could land mid-closing-auction, stamping a mid-session tick as the day's price. Extended to `*/30 7-13 * * 0-4`, guaranteeing at least two post-close runs in both DST regimes. The fetch script now also records each ticker's actual market quote time (Yahoo's `regularMarketTime` — after the session, this IS the official close time) in a new `quotes` map, keeping the flat `prices` map for already-deployed bundles.
- **Freshness surfaced**: `PriceRepository.getSnapshotTimestamp` (never displayed anywhere) replaced with `getSnapshotInfo` returning `{ asOf, latestQuoteAt }` — null when no usable snapshot exists, so the UI can distinguish "loading" from "definitively unavailable". New `PriceFreshness` component renders on all five price-showing pages (Dashboard, Portfolios, Portfolio detail, Trades, Analytics): a subtle "Prices as of {close time} (last market close)" line normally, escalating to an amber outdated warning past 4 days (the EGX's longest normal quiet stretch: Fri-Sat + a holiday), or the no-prices warning above.
- 6 tests net (352 total): 2 new in `SnapshotPriceRepository.test.ts` (v2 quotes parsing + latest-quote-time; null on failed fetch), 3 in `PriceFreshness.test.tsx` (last-close line, stale escalation, no-prices warning), and the existing repo tests migrated from `getSnapshotTimestamp`.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build with all three states: the real placeholder snapshot showed the no-prices warning; a routed fresh v2 snapshot showed "Prices as of 04 Jul 2026, 18:23 (last market close)…"; a routed 10-day-old snapshot showed the outdated warning.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — the first real price run exposed two more pipeline traps

Dispatching the price workflow for the first time (see above) succeeded — and immediately proved out the new quote-time capture: every Yahoo quote came back stamped **July 2024**. Yahoo's EGX coverage returns 200 with two-year-old data (ORHD at 13.59 vs its real ~23), so the error-only fallback chain happily wrote a full snapshot of stale prices and never consulted TradingView at all. Separately: the snapshot commit produced no site deploy — pushes made with `GITHUB_TOKEN` never trigger other workflows, so scheduled price updates would land on main but never reach the deployed site (which serves the snapshot as a static file).

- **Freshness-aware provider chain** (`fetch-prices`): a provider can fail by erroring *or* by "succeeding" with stale data. TradingView (which actively covers the EGX) is now asked first, with a `time` column for the last bar's market time (graceful retry without it if the column is rejected); Yahoo second. The first quote whose market time is within 7 days (the EGX's longest normal quiet stretch, with margin) wins; if neither is provably fresh, unknown-freshness beats known-stale, and the newest stale quote still gets written rather than nothing — the in-app PriceFreshness indicator is what tells the user it's outdated.
- **Auto-deploy after a snapshot commit** (`update-prices.yml`): the commit step now reports whether it pushed, and a new step dispatches `deploy-pages.yml` via `gh workflow run` (workflow_dispatch is exempt from the GITHUB_TOKEN recursion guard) so every snapshot change actually goes live.
- Script + workflow change only — no app code, no new tests; verified operationally by re-dispatching the workflow and inspecting the committed snapshot and the deploy it triggered.

### Post-sprint-8 — the Trades page's "wrong" dates: opening balances labeled, and dates made correctable

Direct user report (screenshot): "the EXECUTED date shown in Trades is all wrong — needs review and correction." Root cause was not corruption: the rows all dated 01 Jan 2026 (TMGH/ORAS/PHAR/COMI/EAST/CSAG) were **opening balances** deliberately booked at the tracking floor by `handleRecordOpeningBalance` (the real purchases predate 2026-01-01, so there is no real in-range date) — but the Trades table displayed that placeholder as a bare EXECUTED date indistinguishable from a real one, so correct-by-design data *read* as wrong. Two changes, one for honesty and one for agency:

- **"Opening balance" pill** on any trade whose notes carry the opening-balance marker, with a tooltip explaining the date is the tracking floor by design and the avg cost came from the broker screenshot — the placeholder now announces itself instead of impersonating a real execution date.
- **`correctTradeExecutionDate`** (`TradeService`, the date twin of `renameTickerEverywhere`): a pencil on every Executed cell opens an inline date editor (min = tracking floor, max = today). Touches ONLY the date — shares/price/fees/allocations untouched — and moves the matching Buy timeline event with it so the ledger and timeline never disagree. Refused when the new date would land after a sell that already closed shares from the lot (a lot can't be bought after part of it was sold), before the tracking floor, or in the future.
- 3 new tests in `TradeService.test.ts` (trade + timeline move together; floor/future rejection; sell-ordering guard with a valid correction accepted) — 355 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: recorded an opening-balance-shaped EAST lot and a wrongly-dated ORHD lot — the pill rendered on EAST only; correcting ORHD 01 Jan → 14 Jan updated the table instantly and the Timeline's Buy event moved to 14 JAN 2026 with it.

### Post-sprint-8 — opening balances retired: the user rejected the concept, confirmed via direct discussion

Direct user correction of the previous fix's framing ("انا مش موافق … تجاهل اى تاريخ قبل ١/١/٢٠٢٦"), clarified via an explicit question-and-answer: **their portfolio starts fresh from 2026-01-01 — no held position has any real pre-2026 purchase.** Every real buy is dated on/after the tracking floor and exists in their 2026 broker documents; the opening-balance lots (booked from position screenshots with the floor as a placeholder date) were therefore *wrong data*, not a representation of old holdings — the confirmed business rule is "ignore anything before 1/1/2026 as if it doesn't exist," and a placeholder standing in for an imagined pre-2026 purchase violates it.

- **"Record as opening balance" removed** from the portfolio page's verified-but-untracked banner (handler, state, and button; the earlier "books a Trade at the tracking floor" behavior retired). The banner now points at the one honest path: upload the ticker's real buy invoices/statement in Import so its lots land with their true dates — which always exist, per the confirmed rule.
- **Trades page gained a per-lot delete** (trash icon, only on lots with no shares closed against them — the existing `deleteTrade` guard) so the user can remove the six placeholder lots themselves; cost refunds to cash and the Buy timeline event is removed, exactly like the Import-side delete.
- The previous fix's "Opening balance" pill re-worded to **"Placeholder — replace with real buys"** (amber), with a tooltip walking through delete-then-import.
- Tests: the two opening-balance tests replaced by one asserting the banner shows import guidance and no record button; the pill/delete flows covered by the existing deleteTrade suite — 354 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build: recorded a placeholder-shaped EAST lot — the amber pill rendered; the trash button removed it from the table entirely.

### Post-sprint-8 — one-click "replace placeholder with real rows" in Import (the CSAG proof)

Direct user follow-up with the decisive evidence: CSAG's real Thndr Orders screen — five buys across Feb–Mar 2026 (48+51+50+5+50) totalling exactly the 204 shares its placeholder lot carried. This confirmed the placeholders represent real 2026 transactions whose documents simply hadn't been imported yet — and exposed a trap in the delete-then-import workflow: if the user uploads the real orders BEFORE deleting the placeholder, `alreadyFullyRecorded` fires (existing 204 alone matches the broker's 204) and its "Discard all pending" banner suggests throwing away the REAL rows and keeping the dateless placeholder — the exact wrong direction.

- **`placeholderReplacements`** (ImportPage): for an `alreadyFullyRecorded` mismatch where every existing open share is a deletable opening-balance placeholder (notes marker, no shares closed against it) AND the batch's pending rows alone reconcile exactly with the broker, the banner flips from "discard pending" to a cyan **"Replace placeholder with real rows"** — one click deletes the placeholder lot(s) (cost refunds to cash via the existing `deleteTrade`), Dexie's live queries recompute, and the ticker lands straight on Verified with its per-ticker Confirm live. Only offered for the clean swap, so it can never half-apply; a placeholder with sells against it falls back to the old banner untouched.
- 1 new test in `ImportPage.test.tsx` (the CSAG shape renders the replace banner, not the discard one, and fires the right callback) — 355 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build with the user's exact numbers: a 204-share CSAG placeholder on the ledger + the five real Feb–Mar rows + a 204-unit broker check — the replace banner appeared instead of the discard trap, and one click deleted the placeholder, flipped CSAG to Verified with Confirm live, and left the Trades page clean of the 01 Jan lot.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — the recurring "shows 5 Fulfilled but only 4 extracted" warning, root-caused end to end

Direct user report ("النوع ده من الاخطاء متكرر — الصورة واضحة وحروفها كاملة") with the exact CSAG Orders screenshot: 5 clearly-legible Fulfilled buys, 4 extracted, and only the generic "may be missing — try re-uploading" warning. Reproduced end to end by running the real OCR pipeline in Chromium against the reported PNG, which pinned three stacked causes — the specific OCR glyph failure, and two structural bugs that each prevented the recovery path from ever working:

1. **The dropped row itself**: full-page OCR read the third row's time "11:17AM" as "11117AM" (colon → 1), so the flat parser's date-time pattern found no time and dropped exactly that one row. Not a code bug per se — the class of glyph failure the row-isolated re-scan exists to absorb — but the pipeline never gave it the chance:
2. **The re-scan only ran on a totally empty flat parse** (`ImportOrchestrator`): a flat result of 4-of-5 shipped as-is with a warning, never trying the strictly more reliable row-isolated path. Extracted the trigger/adoption policy into `ordersScanSelection.ts` (pure, unit-tested): the re-scan now also runs whenever the flat result's own signals say it lost or mispaired a row (`missingFulfilledCount` — which now discounts out-of-range exclusions rather than double-reporting them — `incompleteRowCount`, `statusCountMismatch`), and its result is adopted only when switching cannot lose a trade the flat parse already had (more candidates, or equal count with fewer problems; an all-cancelled zero from an empty flat parse still counts as understood).
3. **Row segmentation merged all five rows into one slice on a full-screen capture** (`imagePreprocess.ts`): the grouping threshold `max(minGap*1.8, midpoint*0.8)` was dragged to ~143 — above the real ~123px between-row gaps — by the 284px gap before the Buy/Sell buttons (measured gaps on the actual screenshot: `[73, 36×5, 122–124×4, 284]`). A minimum-variance two-cluster split was tried first and failed on the same capture the opposite way (the 284 outlier is so extreme that isolating it alone minimizes variance, threshold ~204). Replaced with `rowGroupingGapThreshold`: the first ≥1.8× jump between consecutive sorted gaps marks the within-row/between-row boundary regardless of how many clusters sit above it.
- 16 new tests (12 in `ordersScanSelection.test.ts`, 4 in `imagePreprocess.test.ts`, including the measured-gap regression) — 371 total.
- Verified end to end in a real Chromium run against the reported screenshot: before → 4 candidates at "medium" plus the warning, re-scan produced 2 slices with all rows merged and was correctly rejected; after → 7 slices (title | 5 rows | buttons), all 5 buys extracted at "high" confidence (pixel-color status, isolated-slice OCR reading "11:17AM" correctly), zero warnings.

### Post-sprint-8 — a fifth document type: the account-wide "Orders" timeline screenshot

Direct user request with five real screenshots: alongside statement/invoice/position/per-stock-orders uploads, support the broker's account-wide **Orders** screen — the full-account order history (title "Orders", tabs All/Pending/Completed/Cancelled; the per-stock "Completed Orders" tab renders identical rows). Each row carries the REAL ticker code, "Buy/Sell Limit/Market @price", the order's total value, and a Fulfilled/Cancelled status — but **no execution date and no printed share count**. The user's stated uses: spotting transactions misclassified/misfiled under the wrong stock, and inferring/matching share counts as the confirmation evidence a stuck ticker needs.

- **`ParsedOrderEvidence`** (domain) + **`parseOrdersTimeline`/`looksLikeOrdersTimeline`** on `BrokerParser` (ThndrParser implements; CsvStatementParser no-ops) + a new `orders-timeline` doc type in `ImportOrchestrator`, routed before the statement/orders-screen parsers (its rows carry none of the fields those need). Undated rows can never become trades — they parse as **evidence**. Shares are derived from `totalValue / price`, and a candidate total only counts when that lands on a whole share count — a self-check that also picks the right number out of OCR noise (header stats like "+5,796.31 (14.99%)" are additionally excluded by sign/percent/decimals rules). Pending/Rejected rows are skipped silently; Fulfilled AND Cancelled are both kept (a cancelled order is broker-authored proof that a similar-looking row is NOT a real trade).
- **`orderEvidence.ts`** (new application service): `findOrderConfirmedKeys` matches each still-pending Buy/Sell against a fulfilled order (same ticker/side/share count, price within 5% — candidate prices can be commission-inclusive), consuming each order at most once so one real order can never double-confirm a double-extracted transaction; `findWrongTickerHintsFromOrders` flags a non-high-confidence candidate whose numbers match exactly one OTHER ticker's fulfilled order while its own ticker has none — the timeline prints the real code on every row, so it catches a misfiled read even when nothing exists under the right ticker yet (merged into the existing wrong-ticker badge, ledger-based hints taking precedence).
- **`checkTickerMatch` gained a fifth verification path**: `orders-verified` — a ticker whose every still-pending row is invoice-sourced, cross-verified, or order-confirmed no longer needs a "My Position" screenshot. Same shape as the invoice rule: only ever substitutes for a MISSING position screenshot; a real mismatch still blocks.
- **Import UI**: evidence rows render per ticker group (side/shares/price/type/total + Fulfilled/Cancelled pill, per-row discard for a misread); corroborated rows get a cyan "Matches Orders history" badge; on a mismatch with order history present, uncorroborated rows get an amber "No matching order" badge — pointing at the likely extra/misfiled row; overlapping scrolled screenshots dedupe across files by content key (within one file, identical rows are genuinely two orders); ticker rename carries evidences along; evidence-only groups don't offer a no-op Confirm button.
- 22 new tests (7 ThndrParser timeline, 10 orderEvidence, 3 importVerification, 2 ImportPage) — 393 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build (Playwright, 13 checks): seeded SKPC (fully order-confirmed, no position screenshot) → "Verified — matches Orders history" with a live per-ticker Confirm that committed a real trade (confirmed via direct IndexedDB read); ORHD (15+8 extracted vs 15 verified, order history covering only the 15) → the 8-share row flagged "No matching order" alongside the solver's "Suggested removal"; a low-confidence HRHO read matching SUGR's fulfilled order → "Likely SUGR's transaction", disappearing when the evidence row is discarded.

### Post-sprint-8 — the dual-source rule: ANY two different document types confirm a transaction

Direct user follow-up formalizing the verification model across all five supported document types (statement, invoice, my position, per-stock orders screenshot, account-wide orders timeline): a transaction is confirmed when **any two independent document types agree on it** — statement+invoice, statement+position, position+orders screenshot, statement+orders screenshot, and so on; which pair doesn't matter, that it's a pair does. Most pairs were already mechanically covered (anything+position = the `matched` count reconciliation; invoice+anything = `cross-verified`; anything+orders-timeline = `orders-verified`) — but the system couldn't distinguish a statement read from an orders-screenshot read (both carried `source: undefined`), so e.g. statement+orders-screenshot never counted as two documents.

- **`ParsedTradeCandidate.source` generalized** from `"invoice" | undefined` to `"statement" | "invoice" | "orders-screen" | "csv"` — every parser now stamps its document type on every candidate (ThndrParser statement/orders-screen paths, CsvStatementParser "csv"; the invoice path already did).
- **`findCrossSourceVerifiedKeys` generalized**: a signature group (ticker+side+date+shares) containing candidates from **two or more distinct document types** flags every member verified — no longer invoice-specific. Two reads of the SAME type never pair (two statements are a re-upload, not independent confirmation). A legacy untyped candidate (from a session predating the field) only pairs with an invoice, exactly its original behavior — its real type is unknowable, so it must not accidentally pair with its own type.
- **UI**: ticker badge re-worded to "Verified — two documents agree" (was invoice-specific); new per-row cyan "Two documents agree" badge on every dual-confirmed row, so the user sees exactly which transactions are two-factor-confirmed and which still need a second document.
- 4 net new tests (397 total): statement+orders-screenshot pair verifies, csv+statement pair verifies, same-type pair never does, legacy-untyped+typed never does.
- **A workflow trap found during e2e verification, and fixed**: "Clear suspected duplicates" removes one copy of the dual-source pair before commit (correctly — committing both would double-book), but deleting it outright made the surviving row single-source again, un-verifying the ticker the moment the user did the right thing. Discarded candidates now move to a `discardedCandidates` session list instead of vanishing — never rendered, never committed, but still counted as corroboration (a discarded duplicate is still a real read of its document), so dual-source verification survives the cleanup. Ticker rename carries them along.
- Verified end-to-end against a real production build (Playwright, 8 checks): a ticker with the same buy read from a statement and an orders screenshot, no position screenshot at all → "Verified — two documents agree" with both rows badged and a live Confirm; a control ticker with the same buy read from two STATEMENTS stayed blocked ("Needs broker screenshot"); after "Clear suspected duplicates" the verification held, and Confirm landed exactly one real trade (confirmed via direct IndexedDB read).

### Post-sprint-8 fix — "Needs broker screenshot" was the wrong message for a Sell that outruns the ledger (the SKPC case)

Direct user report (Arabic, screenshot): SKPC showed "Needs broker screenshot" for a pending 82-share Sell, despite uploading a full Order timeline, Statement, and Orders screenshot — and correctly pointed out no "My Position" screenshot can ever exist for a stock that's already fully sold. Root cause traced in `checkTickerMatch`/`ImportPage`, not the OCR extraction: the ticker's existing ledger only had 12 shares remaining open (a separate already-closed trade accounted for the rest of its history), so `netShares` (12 existing + 0 pending buys − 82 pending sell = −70) never reconciled to zero, missing the existing `closed-position` trivial-match path — and the generic `"no-verification"` banner told the user to upload a screenshot regardless of the actual numbers, which is nonsensical advice once a position is sold out. The real problem in this shape is never a missing screenshot — it's that the Sell being imported needs more Buy history than the ledger currently has.

- `TickerGroupCard`'s `no-verification` banner and `MatchBadge` now branch on `matchStatus.netShares < 0` — a pending Sell total exceeding existing-ledger + pending-Buy shares. This distinct case badges **"Missing buy history"** (rose, not amber) and states the actual arithmetic (existing + this batch's buys vs. this batch's sells, and the exact shortfall), explaining that a broker screenshot can't help a sold-out position and pointing at the real fix: upload a Statement/Orders screenshot covering the missing purchase history, or record the missing buy(s) manually. The ordinary "still open, waiting on a screenshot" case (`netShares >= 0`) is unchanged.
- Deliberately UI-only — `checkTickerMatch` itself, its `TickerMatchReason` union, and every existing caller/test are untouched; the shortfall is fully derivable from `netShares` already on the existing `TickerMatchStatus`, so no new reason value or field was needed.
- 1 new test in `ImportPage.test.tsx` (the exact SKPC shape: 82-share pending Sell, 12 existing remaining shares, no verification — asserts the "Missing buy history" badge and shortfall banner render, not the old generic message) — 398 total.
- This is a messaging/diagnosis fix, not a data fix: the user's underlying ledger gap (missing ~70 shares of Buy history for SKPC) still needs the actual missing documents or a manual entry — this only makes the gate's advice for that shape correct instead of misleading.

### Post-sprint-8 — a way to fix an already-committed ticker filed under its raw company name

Direct user report (live screenshots): MASR and "MEDINET MASR HOUSING" (and, from the same dropdown, SUGR/"DELTA SUGAR") showed as separate stocks in the Trades page's ticker filter — the same real company split into two identities. Root cause understood, not new: `knownTickers.ts`'s own doc comment already described this exact failure mode — a company resolves via its raw name before it's added to `KNOWN_EGX_TICKERS`, gets committed under that raw-name pseudo-ticker, and once the mapping is later added (SUGR/MASR were added in Sprint 8 itself, per `f005ec6`), new imports resolve correctly but the already-committed rows keep the wrong identity forever. The existing fix for this (`tickerForCompanyNameFallback` + Import's one-click rename banner) only ever reaches a ticker still sitting in the *current* Import session's pending pool — once it's fully committed and the session is cleared (exactly what this user was told to do a few messages earlier, to clean up unrelated stale badges), there was no way left to fix it.

- **`findMisnamedTickers`** (`TradeService.ts`, new): scans every committed `Trade` globally (not scoped to one portfolio) for a ticker string that's actually a known company's raw name per `tickerForCompanyNameFallback`, returning the wrong ticker, its real symbol, and total remaining shares under it.
- **`PortfoliosPage`** gained a "Tickers filed under the wrong name" banner (mirrors the existing "Stocks split across portfolios" banner's shape) — one row per misnamed ticker with a one-click "Rename to {real}" button reusing the already-existing `renameTickerEverywhere` (fixes `Trade`/`TradeAllocation`/`TimelineEvent`/`PositionVerification` in one pass, nothing else about the rows changes).
- Noted for the user: renaming only fixes the ticker *identity* — if the same real transaction was independently imported once under each spelling (which the reported MASR shape looks like: two 72-share buys, both already fully sold, on the exact same date/price), the rows will still look like a duplicate position after the rename and may need a manual delete same as any other duplicate-trade cleanup.
- 5 new tests (403 total): 3 in `TradeService.test.ts` (`findMisnamedTickers` flags the MASR/Medinet Masr Housing shape, doesn't flag an already-correct ticker, doesn't flag a genuinely unknown company), 2 in `PortfoliosPage.test.tsx` (banner renders and renames on click; absent when nothing is misnamed).
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: seeded a "MEDINET MASR HOUSING" trade (72 sh) with no MASR trade yet present, confirmed the banner rendered with the exact reported wording, clicked "Rename to MASR," and confirmed the trade's ticker updated to MASR directly in IndexedDB with the banner disappearing.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — Portfolio Comparison and Monthly Performance counted deposits as fake "returns"

Direct user report (live screenshots): the Dashboard's "Portfolio Comparison" chart showed a portfolio flat near zero for months then spiking to ~30,000% in one step, and "Monthly Performance" showed an equally fake +140%-ish bar. Root cause, confirmed against the user's own real numbers (a ~34 EGP starting balance, then real ~3,000/2,900/10,000 EGP deposits landing later): both charts computed "return" as a raw ratio/delta of `equity`, which is cumulative CASH (deposits, withdrawals, and every buy/sell/dividend's cash effect) — so a deposit landing mid-period was indistinguishable from a trading gain, and dividing by a near-zero starting equity (before the first deposit ever posted) turned any later deposit into an astronomical fake "return." `portfolioReturn.ts`'s own existing "since inception %" stat already avoided this by using net Deposit−Withdrawal as its denominator instead of raw equity — the two time-series charts just never got the same treatment.

- **`EquityPoint` gained `contributed?: number`** (`equityCurve.ts`) — cumulative net Deposit−Withdrawal as of each point, computed in the same pass as `equity`. Optional so a hand-built fixture from before this field existed still type-checks and behaves as "no flow" (identical to the old math) — only real callers going through `equityCurve()` get it populated.
- **`bucketReturns`** (`shared.ts`, used by both `monthlyReturn`/`annualReturn`) now subtracts each bucket's net contributed-capital change from the equity delta before computing `returnPct` — a deposit within a period no longer inflates (or a withdrawal deflates) that period's reported return.
- **`DashboardPage`'s `indexEquityCurve`** (Portfolio Comparison) no longer rebases to the first point's raw equity — it now indexes to `100 + portfolioReturn-style return` (`(equity − contributed) / |contributed|`, the same formula `portfolioReturn.ts` already uses for "since inception %", evaluated at every point instead of only "now"). Stays exactly at 100 while no capital has been contributed yet, instead of the old ratio blowing up on a near-zero denominator.
- 8 new tests (409 total): 2 in `equityCurve.test.ts` (`contributed` accumulates Deposit/Withdrawal only, ignoring Buy/Sell/Dividend cash effects), 2 in `monthlyReturn.test.ts` (a mid-bucket deposit no longer inflates the return; a real gain alongside a deposit in the same bucket still reports correctly), 3 in `DashboardPage.test.tsx` (the exact reported near-zero-start-then-deposit shape no longer spikes; index holds at 100 with no contributions yet; a real gain on already-contributed capital still moves the index), 1 fixture update in `AnalyticsEngine.test.ts` for the new field.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: seeded the reported shape (a ~34 EGP-starting portfolio, three deposits landing over January, alongside a second comparison portfolio) and confirmed the Portfolio Comparison chart renders a bounded, sane curve instead of the reported flat-then-vertical-spike shape.
- Deliberately out of scope: the equity curve's own documented limitation (no historical mark-to-market — every point before today reflects cash flow only, so a period with heavy net buying can still look artificially poor and heavy net selling artificially good) is unchanged; this fix only removes deposits/withdrawals from being misread as trading performance, it doesn't add a historical price feed.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — Monthly Performance's remaining spike, and a way to discard a misfiled verification

Two more direct user reports on the same session's threads: (1) Monthly Performance still showed a huge fake spike (~+65%) in the current month even after the deposit-exclusion fix above; (2) ABUK showed a "Verified positions with no recorded trades" warning on "Long Positions," despite its real trades correctly living in "SMC Auto Scanner" — confirmed by the user directly.

**(1) Root cause**: `equityCurve()`'s every point before today is cash-flow only, but its *last* point is blended with `todayMarketValue` (real mark-to-market) — a deliberate, documented approximation for the headline "what's this worth right now" chart. `monthlyReturn`/`annualReturn` fed off that *same* blended curve, so whichever month happens to contain "today" gets the *entire* unrealized P&L of every open position dumped into its bucket in one step, on top of the already-fixed deposit issue — an artifact of mixing two different units (cash-only vs. cash+market-value) across one series, not something the deposit fix touched.

- **`cashFlowCurve`** (`equityCurve.ts`, new): the same per-event cash-flow scan as `equityCurve`, but the point for "today" stays cash-only too — never blended with market value. `equityCurve` itself is unchanged (still used for the Dashboard's headline/combined equity chart, where showing today's true value is exactly the point).
- **`AnalyticsEngine.computeAnalytics`** now feeds `monthlyReturn`/`annualReturn` from `cashFlowCurve` instead of `equityCurve` — every point in *that* series is consistently cash-flow-only, so a period's delta reflects what actually happened during it, not a one-time "we now know the real value of stock you already owned" correction. `drawdown` is untouched (a peak-at-the-end from the blended curve doesn't manufacture a false drawdown the way it manufactures a false *monthly return*).
- Still out of scope, unchanged: the underlying "buys look like pure cash losses, sells look like pure gains" noise inherent to a cash-flow-only history (no historical price feed) — this fix removes the two known causes of an *artificial spike* (deposits, and the final mark-to-market blend), not the softer month-to-month noise from that deeper, documented limitation.

**(2) Root cause**: a stray `PositionVerification` for ABUK had been saved with `portfolioId` pointing at "Long Positions" (almost certainly from an earlier, confused moment in this same troubleshooting session) while ABUK's real trades all live in "SMC Auto Scanner." The "no recorded trades" banner is portfolio-scoped by design (a real per-portfolio reconciliation), so it correctly flagged the stray record — but had no action to fix it, since its only guidance ("upload buy invoices") assumes the missing-trade case, not a misfiled one.

- **`PositionReconciliation` gained `verificationId`** (`reconciliation.ts`) so the UI can target the exact record.
- **`PortfolioDetailPage`**'s "Verified positions with no recorded trades" banner gained a discard (trash icon) action per row, calling the already-existing `repos.verifications.delete` — never touches cash or trades, purely removes the stray reading.
- 2 net new tests in `reconciliation.test.ts` (implicit via existing fixtures' `id` now asserted through the new field is exercised by the PortfolioDetailPage test) + 1 new `PortfolioDetailPage.test.tsx` case (discards the stray verification and confirms it's gone) — plus 6 new/updated in the `equityCurve`/`AnalyticsEngine` suite for (1). 414 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: seeded the exact ABUK/Long-Positions shape, confirmed the banner and discard click removed only the stray record (the real SMC Auto Scanner verification untouched).

### Post-sprint-8 — remove the equity curve entirely; returns are now realized/unrealized/dividend %, never cash flow

Direct, explicit user decision after seeing the equity-curve-based charts fail repeatedly (a Combined Equity Curve spiking to E£750K, a Drawdown reading -2200%, Monthly Return still showing fake swings even after the deposit fix): stop patching the cash-flow equity-curve model and remove it outright. The user's own framing: charts should show realized return %, unrealized return %, and dividend return % — never a number derived from raw cash balance. Confirmed directly that unrealized % only needs today's known closing price (already in the snapshot), not a historical series.

Root cause of why the equity-curve approach kept needing new patches: cash flow conflates several unlike things into one number — a Buy's cash outflow isn't a loss (it's an asset swap), a Sell's cash inflow isn't purely a gain (part of it just returns the original cost), a deposit isn't a return at all, and blending today's real mark-to-market onto an otherwise cash-only history creates a one-time jump. Every one of those was patched individually across the last few fixes; removing cash flow from the return calculation entirely removes the whole class of bug at once.

- **`performanceCurve.ts`** (new calculator, replacing `equityCurve.ts`/`monthlyReturn.ts`/`annualReturn.ts`/`drawdown.ts`, all four deleted along with their tests): built entirely from *fully-realized, dated* events — `realizedPnlMicros` per `TradeAllocation` (never a Sell's raw cash-in) and `Dividend` timeline events — plus `Deposit`/`Withdrawal` events tracked only as the % denominator (net contributed capital), never as part of the gain itself. `performanceCurve()` returns a cumulative `{date, realizedReturnPct, dividendReturnPct}` series; `bucketPerformance()` buckets the same inputs by month/year (each period's own gain against capital already contributed *before* that period, so same-period deposits still can't inflate it); `performanceDrawdown()` is the max peak-to-trough decline of cumulative realized+dividend %, bounded and sane by construction since nothing feeding it is a cash-flow artifact.
- **`AnalyticsEngine`**: `AnalyticsResult` drops `equityCurve`/`monthlyReturn`/`annualReturn` entirely; gains `performanceCurve`, `monthlyPerformance`, `annualPerformance`, `realizedReturnPct`/`dividendReturnPct` (cumulative-to-date scalars, the curve's last point), and `unrealizedReturnPct` (today's mark-to-market vs. cost basis — a snapshot stat, deliberately never a historical series, since no historical price feed exists or is planned). `drawdown` is redefined in place using `performanceDrawdown`. `portfolioReturn` (deposit/withdrawal-based "since inception %") is untouched — it was never equity-curve-based.
- **`DashboardPage`**: "Combined Equity Curve" panel removed outright (no replacement — "Portfolio Allocation" now has the row to itself alongside the comparison chart). "Portfolio Comparison" now plots each portfolio's own realized+dividend return % directly — no more indexing/rebasing needed, since % is already comparable across portfolios of any size. "Monthly Performance" now averages realized+dividend % across portfolios.
- **`AnalyticsPage`**: "Equity Curve" and "Drawdown" charts replaced by one "Realized + Dividend Return" line chart; "Monthly Return" bar chart now plots realized % and dividend % as two series instead of one blended equity-derived number. New stat tiles: Realized Return, Unrealized Return, Dividend Return.
- 15 net new/changed tests (405 total; net -10 from deleting the four old calculators' suites, +10 in new `performanceCurve.test.ts`, plus updated `AnalyticsEngine.test.ts`/`DashboardPage.test.tsx` cases): `performanceCurve`/`bucketPerformance` never let a same-period deposit inflate realized return, `performanceDrawdown` never blows past what's actually in the curve, `mergeComparisonCurves`/`mergeMonthlyPerformance` need no equity-curve indexing at all.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: seeded the exact reported near-zero-start-plus-large-deposit shape (~34 EGP start, 3,000 + 10,000 EGP deposits, a real +81 EGP realized gain, a 50 EGP dividend) across two portfolios — confirmed neither "Equity Curve" nor "Combined Equity Curve" appears anywhere in the app, Portfolio Comparison/Monthly Performance render bounded, sane percentages (no spike), and the Analytics page's new Realized/Unrealized/Dividend stat tiles and chart all populate correctly.

### Post-sprint-8 — day-by-day historical price accumulation (infrastructure only, no consuming feature yet)

User asked what's needed to fetch prices "day by day," explicitly requesting the free TradingView/yfinance-style sources already in use and an extensible design. `scripts/fetch-prices` already queries TradingView and Yahoo Finance for the *current* price every 30 minutes but only ever overwrote a single-snapshot file — no day's close was ever kept once the next run replaced it. Rather than adding a third provider (against the "single source of truth" price rule), the fix extends the same Yahoo chart endpoint already in use, which supports a `range`/`interval` query for bulk historical closes in one request.

- **`scripts/fetch-prices/index.ts`**: each run now also loads `public/price-history.json` (`{ [ticker]: { [date: "YYYY-MM-DD"]: closePrice } }`), backfills any ticker with no recorded history yet via one Yahoo `range=2y&interval=1d` request (a one-time catch-up, not a repeated call), and appends today's already-fetched quote under today's date — so history grows one real trading day at a time with zero extra API calls beyond the existing 30-minute cadence. New pure helpers `historyDateKey`/`parseYahooHistory` are unit-tested directly (4 new tests); `main()` is now guarded behind an entry-point check so importing the module for tests never triggers a real network call.
- **`PriceRepository`** (domain interface) gains `getPriceHistory(ticker): Promise<Record<string, number>>`; **`SnapshotPriceRepository`** implements it by fetching the new `price-history.json` with the same never-throws/cache-TTL pattern as the current-price snapshot (4 new tests).
- **`update-prices.yml`**: now commits `public/price-history.json` alongside the existing snapshot.
- Deliberately no consuming UI feature yet — the user's own explicit, very recent decision (previous entry above) removed every cash/equity-based time-series chart from the app, so this sprint only lays the data-access groundwork (repository method + accumulating file) an eventual feature (e.g. a real historical mark-to-market chart, or a reference line) can build on later, without presuming which one is wanted.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — the new realized/dividend % model read as 0% on every real portfolio (funding recorded outside the timeline)

User asked for a screenshot proof of the just-shipped realized/unrealized/dividend redesign against their *real* data (not seeded test data) — three real screenshots showed "Monthly Performance"/"Monthly Return" completely empty (no bars at all) on every portfolio, and "Portfolio Comparison" flat at ~0% for months before a tiny, suspicious jump right at today's date, despite the Analytics page's own "Largest Winner" stat proving real realized gains existed (E£81.06).

- **Root cause**: `createPortfolioAndSave` (`PortfolioService.ts`) has always set `Portfolio.cash = initialCash` directly but never recorded a matching "Deposit" timeline event for it — only the explicit `deposit()` action (used for later top-ups) ever created one. `performanceCurve`/`bucketPerformance` (and `AnalyticsEngine`'s `portfolioReturn` inputs) compute "% of net contributed capital" *exclusively* from Deposit/Withdrawal timeline events, so a portfolio funded only via the create-portfolio field has always looked like it received zero capital — every realized/dividend % permanently divides by zero and reports 0%, no matter how large the real gain. Reproduced directly: a trade with a real +E£500 realized gain and no Deposit event showed `realizedReturnPct: 0` in every bucket.
- **`createPortfolioAndSave`** now also records a dated Deposit event for `initialCash` (prospective fix — new portfolios are correct going forward; it does not touch `Portfolio.cash` a second time).
- **`findPortfoliosMissingFundingRecord`** (new): flags an *existing* portfolio with real realized P/L or dividends but zero net contributed capital ever recorded — the exact shape above. Portfolios with no realized activity yet are never flagged (0% is already correct there).
- **`backfillInitialFunding`** (new): records the missing dated Deposit event for an existing portfolio without ever touching its current cash balance (which already reflects that funding).
- **`PortfoliosPage`** gains a "Portfolios missing an initial funding record" banner (same pattern as the split/misnamed-ticker banners) with an inline amount + date input per flagged portfolio, calling `backfillInitialFunding`.
- 12 new/changed tests (434 total): `createPortfolioAndSave` now asserts the Deposit event; `findPortfoliosMissingFundingRecord`/`backfillInitialFunding` cover the flag/no-flag/backfill cases; `PortfoliosPage` covers the banner appearing, backfilling, and disappearing once funding is recorded.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: reproduced the exact reported shape (a portfolio funded only via `initialCash`, a real +E£500 realized gain, no Deposit event) — confirmed Realized Return read +0.00% and Monthly Return was empty before the fix; after using the new banner's "Record funding" action, Realized Return correctly showed +10.00%, Monthly Return rendered a real bar, and the portfolio's cash balance was unchanged (5,500 before and after).

### Post-sprint-8 fix — the funding-gap detector missed portfolios that already had *some* (insufficient) recorded deposit

The fix above shipped, but the user's own real portfolios still showed no banner at all and still-empty charts — the detector's "flag only if zero net contributed capital was *ever* recorded" check was too narrow: a portfolio that has since logged one small, real, unrelated top-up Deposit has `contributed > 0` and was skipped outright, even though that top-up covers only a sliver of the portfolio's real cash balance.

- **`findPortfoliosMissingFundingRecord`**: rewritten from "is any Deposit recorded at all" to an exact ledger reconciliation — `Portfolio.cash` minus (every Deposit/Withdrawal/CashAdjustment/Dividend event, minus every trade's buy cost, plus every allocation's sell proceeds, mirroring `recordBuy`/`recordSell`'s own cash math). Any positive leftover is cash the ledger can't explain, and is exactly the missing funding amount — not just a yes/no flag. Only portfolios with at least one trade or dividend are considered (nothing to get wrong yet otherwise).
- **`MissingFundingEntry`** now carries `missingAmount` (the exact reconciled gap) instead of a realized/dividend total; the **banner's amount input pre-fills with this exact number** instead of asking the user to guess or recall it from memory — they can still review/adjust before confirming.
- 4 new/changed tests: the exact-reconciliation math on a realistic buy+sell scenario, a portfolio with a small real top-up deposit that still gets correctly flagged (the shape that slipped through before), a portfolio whose cash is already fully explained even with a top-up present, and a no-trades portfolio that's still correctly left alone.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: reproduced the "Old School" shape from the user's real screenshots (E£201,463.82 cash, no open positions, one small real top-up Deposit already recorded) — confirmed the banner now appears where it previously didn't, with the amount input pre-filled to the exact reconciled gap (E£150,463.82).

### Post-sprint-8 fix — the funding banner's own default date rejected itself, plus a direct "edit starting balance" action

After the reconciliation fix, the user still reported empty/wrong charts and asked why they can't just directly edit a portfolio's starting balance (not a deposit/withdrawal) via a simple button. Two real gaps, both traced directly:

- **Root cause**: `backfillInitialFunding` correctly rejects any date before `TRACKING_START_DATE` (2026-01-01) — but the banner's date input defaulted straight to `portfolio.createdAt`, and any portfolio actually created before the tracking window opened (very plausible for a long-running real user) would have its own pre-filled default date rejected the moment "Record funding" was clicked, with only a small, easy-to-miss inline error. Reproduced directly: a portfolio created 2025-11-15 showed the banner, but clicking Record with the un-clamped default date failed validation.
- **`defaultFundingDate`** (new, `PortfoliosPage.tsx`): clamps the pre-filled date to `max(portfolio.createdAt, TRACKING_START_DATE)`, used by both the banner and the new edit action below.
- **`backfillInitialFunding`** now edits its one starting-balance record in place (a deterministic `initial-funding:{portfolioId}` id) instead of creating a new timeline event every time it's called — the same underlying action now doubles as an "edit" rather than only a one-time backfill.
- **`getInitialFundingRecord`** (new): looks up the current starting-balance record for a portfolio, if one has been set, so an edit UI can pre-fill the real current value instead of a fresh suggestion.
- **`PortfoliosPage`** gains an always-available "Edit starting balance" button on every portfolio card (not gated on the missing-funding banner), opening a small modal pre-filled with the existing record if set, or the reconciled gap as a starting suggestion if not — explicitly framed as "starting balance," never deposit/withdrawal language, matching how the user actually thinks about it.
- 9 new/changed tests: the date-clamp fix, the always-available edit action (both the "nothing recorded yet" and "already set, edit in place" cases), and the underlying idempotent-upsert behavior of `backfillInitialFunding`/`getInitialFundingRecord`.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: reproduced a portfolio created 2025-11-15 (before the tracking window) with a real +E£500 realized gain — confirmed the banner's date input now correctly shows 2026-01-01 instead of the rejected 2025-11-15, "Record funding" succeeds with no validation error, and the new "Edit starting balance" button opens correctly pre-filled on the same portfolio afterward.

### Post-sprint-8 — Monthly/Annual Performance gain a real unrealized % (using the day-by-day price history)

User asked why realized return can't just be "total buy-vs-sell price × shares over total original purchase price" — good discussion, but that denominator double-counts recycled capital (sell-then-rebuy inflates it) and ignores idle cash, both real bugs the contributed-capital denominator was built to avoid. Separately, the user asked directly: **"Monthly Performance should be closed + unrealized."** With the day-by-day price history now accumulating (see the earlier "day-by-day historical price accumulation" entry), this is now buildable without reintroducing the original spike bug (blending *today's* price into every period) — each period can use *its own* historical closing price instead.

- **`bucketPerformance`** (`performanceCurve.ts`) rewritten to generate every calendar month/year from the first trade or event to `today` — not just periods containing a realized sale, dividend, or deposit — since an open position sitting untouched for months still has a real unrealized swing worth showing. Gains an optional `priceHistory` + `today` parameter and a new `unrealizedReturnPct` per period: the *change* in mark-to-market during that period (reconstructed point-in-time from each Trade/TradeAllocation's own dates, using that period's own historical close), not a snapshot — so summing every period since a position opened equals its current total unrealized P/L, and once sold, the gain shifts into `realizedReturnPct` instead (no double-counting, verified directly with a buy→hold→sell test). Missing price history for a ticker/date reports 0 for that slice rather than fabricating one. Purely additive — omitting `priceHistory` behaves exactly as before.
- **`AnalyticsEngine`**: `AnalyticsInput` gains optional `priceHistory`; both `monthlyPerformance`/`annualPerformance` now receive it (and a consistently-threaded `today`, fixing a pre-existing gap where `bucketPerformance` silently ignored the caller's `today` entirely).
- **`AnalyticsPage`**: fetches `priceHistory` per ticker traded in the portfolio (`PriceRepository.getPriceHistory`) and passes it through; "Monthly Return" gains a third stacked "Unrealized %" bar.
- **`DashboardPage`**: fetches `priceHistory` across every ticker in every portfolio once; `mergeMonthlyPerformance` now averages realized + dividend + unrealized % (previously realized + dividend only).
- 12 new/changed tests: the continuous-month generation itself, the delta-vs-snapshot math (a two-month price swing with zero other activity), the no-double-count shift into realized on a sale, and 0%-not-fabricated when no price history exists for a ticker.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: seeded a portfolio with one buy in January and *nothing else* (no sells, no dividends, no further deposits) plus six months of historical COMI closes — confirmed Monthly Return now shows a bar for every month from January through July with real, varying (positive and negative) Unrealized % values tracking the historical price, and the Dashboard's Monthly Performance panel reflects the same via `mergeMonthlyPerformance`.

### Post-sprint-8 — remove Deposit/Withdrawal and Starting Balance entirely; returns now measured against cost basis invested

Direct, explicit user decision after an extended discussion: the user doesn't measure "where did my money end up" (a capital-account question) — they evaluate buy price vs. current value (realized, unrealized, and dividends) per position, and want portfolio-level performance evaluated the same way, with no Deposit/Withdrawal/Starting Balance concept anywhere. Confirmed directly, with a concrete worked example, that this means a sell-then-rebuy-with-the-same-money scenario will inflate the denominator (since the same capital counts again on the next buy) — the user confirmed that shape doesn't apply to how they use the app, and accepted it.

- **`performanceCurve.ts`**: `datedDeltas` no longer reads Deposit/Withdrawal events at all — the % denominator ("invested") now comes from each Trade's own cost basis (`shares × entryPrice + fees + taxes`), added the instant it's bought. A trade bought mid-period counts toward *that same period's* basis (unlike the old deposit rule, where a same-period deposit was excluded) — the money is already spent the moment it's bought. `bucketPerformance` also now generates every calendar month/year from first activity to `today` (not just periods with a realized/dividend event), so a position sitting open with nothing else happening still gets a real basis and an unrealized bar.
- **`portfolioReturn.ts`** deleted — "Portfolio Return" is now just `realizedReturnPct + dividendReturnPct` (the performance curve's last point), computed inline in `AnalyticsEngine`.
