- **`PortfolioService.ts`**: `deposit()`/`withdraw()` and the entire Starting Balance feature (`findPortfoliosMissingFundingRecord`, `backfillInitialFunding`, `getInitialFundingRecord`, the "Portfolios missing an initial funding record" banner, the "Edit starting balance" action — all shipped in the last few PRs) are removed outright. `createPortfolioAndSave` reverts to setting `Portfolio.cash` directly with no timeline event. A new **`setCash`** directly sets the cash balance to any value with zero history — the one simple, always-editable number the user asked for.
- **`PortfolioDetailPage`**: "Deposit"/"Withdraw" buttons replaced by one "Edit Cash" button (pre-filled with the current balance); "Dividend" and "Adjust Cash" (signed delta + note, unaffected) remain.
- **`PortfoliosPage`**: the Starting Balance banner and per-card "Edit starting balance" button are gone entirely.
- 33 net changed/removed tests: the cost-basis-denominator math (including the explicit sell-then-rebuy shape now measured as designed), continuous-month coverage, `setCash`'s zero-history guarantee, and every UI test touching the removed deposit/withdraw/starting-balance surfaces.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: seeded a portfolio with a buy and a full sell and **no Deposit/Withdrawal event anywhere** — confirmed Realized Return correctly showed +50% (250 profit / 1000 cost basis) with zero banners or funding prompts, the Portfolios/Portfolio-detail pages show no Deposit/Withdraw affordances anywhere, "Edit Cash" sets the balance with zero timeline events logged, and the Monthly Return chart still populates every month using the new cost-basis basis.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — one corrupted ticker's frozen Yahoo backfill was faking a huge Monthly Return dip

User-reported real bug, from a live screenshot: a buy-only ("long") portfolio's Monthly Return chart showed an implausible ~-38% dip in an early month that partially "recovered" in later months, despite every position still being open (Largest Winner/Loser correctly showing E£0.00/E£0.00 — no sells at all, so the dip had to be coming from the Unrealized bar).

- **Root cause, found by auditing this repo's own committed `public/price-history.json`** (the exact file the live site serves): ORAS's entire two-year backfill was frozen at a single value (71.05, ~10x below its real ~700+ EGP range) for every date except the most recent day, which correctly showed the live quote (718.65) fetched via the already-working daily accumulation path. This is the same "Yahoo returns 200 OK with stale/wrong data" failure mode already guarded against for the *live* quote (`isFresh`/`MAX_QUOTE_AGE_DAYS`) — but `fetchYahooHistory`'s one-time bulk backfill had no equivalent sanity check, so a bad response was persisted verbatim and never revisited (the retry condition only fired when a ticker had *zero* stored history). Any portfolio holding an affected ticker would see a fake, deeply negative unrealized swing in every historical month before today, and a fake huge gain in whichever month contains "today" — exactly the reported shape.
- **`isFrozenHistory`** (new, `scripts/fetch-prices/index.ts`): flags a history series where one price accounts for ≥90% of all points (with at least 10 points) — a threshold picked well above the flattest *genuinely* illiquid real ticker on record (~30% repeats) so real flat spells are never misflagged. `fetchYahooHistory` now rejects (throws on) a freshly-fetched backfill that comes back frozen, exactly like an outright HTTP failure.
- **`main()`**'s backfill trigger now also fires when the *already-stored* history is frozen (self-healing a ticker corrupted by a previous run), and on a failed retry, discards (rather than keeps) a stored series that was already known-frozen — no history and a 0% fallback is safer than a fake price feeding every calculator downstream.
- Manually purged ORAS's frozen entries from the committed `public/price-history.json` (kept only the one confirmed-real day) so the next scheduled price-fetch run re-backfills it cleanly under the new guard, rather than waiting for a ticker to naturally go through a zero-history state.
- 4 new tests (417 total).

### Post-sprint-8 fix — Win Rate/Profit Factor/etc. read as 0 on a buy-only ("long") portfolio, with no indication why

User-reported real screenshot: a portfolio with 29 open trades and zero sells showed Win Rate +0.0%, Profit Factor 0.00, Avg Winner/Loser E£0.00, Avg Holding Time 0.0d, and Largest Winner/Loser E£0.00 — all indistinguishable from "you're breaking even," when the actual cause is that every one of those calculators (`winRate`, `profitFactor`, `avgWinner`, `avgLoser`, `holdingTime`, and `portfolioHealth`'s `largestWinner`/`largestLoser`) derives exclusively from `TradeAllocation`s (recorded sells) and returns `0` by construction when none exist yet — nothing had been sold, so there was nothing to be a bug.

- **`AnalyticsResult.closedTradeCount`** (new, `AnalyticsEngine.ts`): `allocations.length`, exposed alongside the existing metrics so the UI can tell "genuinely zero" apart from "no closed trades yet" without re-deriving it.
- **`AnalyticsPage`**: Win Rate, Profit Factor, Avg Winner, Avg Loser, Avg Holding Time, and the Portfolio Health "Largest Winner / Loser" tile now render `—` with a "No closed trades yet" sublabel when `closedTradeCount` is 0, instead of a misleading `0.0%`/`E£0.00`. The Strategy Attribution table's per-row Win Rate/Profit Factor cells do the same using the row's own `closedAllocationCount` (already computed by `strategyAttribution.ts`, just not read by the page before now).
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: a fresh portfolio with one open buy (no sell) shows `—`/"No closed trades yet" on every affected tile while Exposure, Cash Ratio, Realized Return (correctly 0.00%), and Unrealized Return still render normally; adding a sell on a second portfolio immediately replaced the placeholders with real figures (Win Rate 100%, Profit Factor Infinity, Largest Winner E£500.00).
- 2 existing `computeAnalytics` tests extended to assert `closedTradeCount` (417 total, unchanged — no new test cases).

### Post-sprint-8 fix — replaced the "No closed trades yet" placeholder with a real mark-to-market fallback

Direct user follow-up, immediately after the fix above shipped: rejected the blank `—` placeholder outright — wanted Win Rate/Profit Factor/Avg Winner/Avg Loser/Avg Holding Time/Largest Winner/Loser computed against **today's market price** on a buy-only portfolio, explicitly labeled as unrealized so it's never mistaken for a closed-trade result.

- **`openPositionStats.ts`** (new calculator, one file/one registry entry per the usual extension pattern): mark-to-market win/loss breakdown of every still-open Trade lot against `priceMap` — same win/loss/profit-factor/avg-winner/avg-loser/largest-winner/largest-loser shape as the realized calculators, plus `avgHoldingDays` (days held so far, not days-to-close since nothing's closed). A ticker missing from `priceMap` is skipped entirely rather than priced at zero, matching `summarizeOpenPositions`' documented behavior; cost basis uses the same prorated-by-remaining-shares `Money` math as `summarizeOpenPositions`.
- **`AnalyticsPage`**: the six affected tiles now show, in priority order, (1) the real realized figure once `closedTradeCount > 0`, (2) the `openPositionStats` mark-to-market figure when there's at least one open position, labeled "Unrealized — positions not closed", or (3) "No trades yet" only when the portfolio truly has nothing recorded at all.
- 5 new tests for `openPositionStats` (mixed win/loss profit factor, missing-price skip, fully-closed-trade exclusion) plus one `computeAnalytics` test asserting the fallback kicks in when `closedTradeCount` is 0; realized-path behavior is unchanged and re-verified (423 total).
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: a fresh buy-only portfolio now shows a real Win Rate/Profit Factor/Avg Winner/Largest Winner computed from today's price with the "Unrealized — positions not closed" sublabel on every affected tile; a portfolio with an actual closed sell still shows the plain realized figures with no such label (no regression); a portfolio with zero trades at all still correctly shows "No trades yet".

### Post-sprint-8 — batch of direct user UX requests: %-only Analytics, portfolio name on every tab, nav reorder, cash-free Total Portfolio Value

Six items requested together; four were unambiguous and shipped now, two (full Arabic i18n, and a cash/"allocated capital" tracking redesign) are large/ambiguous enough that they're intentionally deferred — see "Next recommended sprint".

- **Every money figure in Analytics is now a %**: `avgWinner`/`avgLoser` (both the realized calculators and `openPositionStats`' unrealized fallback) and `portfolioHealth`/`openPositionStats`' `largestWinner`/`largestLoser` now report each lot's own return **as % of that lot's cost basis** (user's explicit choice over % of total portfolio value), not a money amount — new `realizedReturnPctForAllocations` helper in `shared.ts` mirrors the existing money-based one. `strategyAttribution` gained a `totalRealizedReturnPct` field (total realized P/L over total cost basis for that tag) so the Strategy Attribution table's last column is a % too; `profitFactor` deliberately stays money-weighted (gross profit/gross loss in currency) since it's a dimensionless ratio, not a currency figure, and the user didn't ask to change its weighting.
- **Portfolio name on every portfolio-scoped tab**: `TradesPage`/`TimelinePage`/`JournalPage`/`AnalyticsPage` headers are now `"{Portfolio Name} — {Tab}"` instead of just the tab name (Holdings/`PortfolioDetailPage` already did this). `TimelinePage`/`JournalPage` didn't fetch the portfolio at all before this — added a `repos.portfolios.getById` `useLiveQuery` to each.
- **Sidebar top-nav reordered** to Import, Dashboard, Portfolios, Data (was Dashboard, Portfolios, Import, Data), per explicit numbered request.
- **Dashboard's "Total Portfolio Value"** now shows `totalMarketValue` only (sublabel: cost basis), not `totalMarketValue + totalCash` — user didn't want cash blended into the headline "how much is my stock worth" number. `totals.totalAssets` (cash+market value) is unchanged internally and still backs Cash Ratio/return-weighting, which weren't part of the complaint.
- 423 tests updated/passing (percent-basis math re-derived by hand for every changed assertion, not just re-run); typecheck clean.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: sidebar order, portfolio name in all four tab headers, Analytics tiles showing e.g. "+1197.1%" instead of an E£ amount, and Dashboard's Total Portfolio Value showing only market value with a cost-basis sublabel.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — Edit Cash reverted to the old balance the instant the field was cleared, before Confirm

User-reported real bug, from live screenshots: every attempt to edit a portfolio's cash balance seemed to "revert on its own" before pressing Confirm. Root cause in `PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`'s `CashModal`: the input's `value` was `kind === "editCash" && amount === "" ? String(currentCash) : amount` — meant to pre-fill the field when the modal first opens, but it re-fired on *every* render where the local `amount` state happened to be empty, including the moment a user backspaces the field down to nothing to type a fresh number. The field would snap back to the old balance mid-edit, making it look uneditable.

- Pre-fill now happens once, via a `useEffect` keyed on `kind`/`currentCash` (mirroring the existing `RenamePortfolioModal` pattern) that sets `amount` to `String(currentCash)` only when the modal opens for `editCash`. The input's `value` is simply `amount` from then on — clearing it behaves like any normal controlled input.
- `handleSubmit`'s parsing simplified to a plain `Number.parseFloat(amount)` (the old `amount === "" ? currentCash : ...` special case is no longer needed, and correctly surfaces the "enter the correct cash balance" validation error if the field is left empty on submit).
- 2 new tests reproducing the exact bug shape (clear-then-type doesn't revert; the newly typed value, not the pre-fill, is what actually gets saved) — 425 total.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build with Playwright, replicating the user's actual gesture (click into the field, clear it character-by-character via repeated Backspace, then type a new number): the field stays empty while clearing and accepts/saves the new value correctly.
- **Separately raised, not changed**: the user also described an expectation that recording a Buy should *increase* Cash Balance (their proposed definition: cost of shares bought + realized dividends + closed-trade P&L). Verified live that a Buy currently *decreases* cash by its cost (E£100,000 → E£99,000 on a E£1,000 buy) — standard spendable-cash bookkeeping, and the same model this app's cash handling was deliberately redesigned around in the "remove Deposit/Withdrawal and Starting Balance" sprint above, per that sprint's own explicit user confirmation. Flagging as open rather than changing it, since reversing that would contradict a previous direct decision — needs explicit re-confirmation from the user before any change.
- **Follow-up from the user, next message**: re-walked through the exact same cash math with concrete numbers (5,000 allocated → buy 3,000 → 2,000 left) and confirmed this already matches; also confirmed that cash doesn't feed into Win Rate/Profit Factor/Avg Winner-Loser/Realized-Unrealized-Dividend Return (verified live: allocating 5,000 and buying exactly 3,000 of stock left Cash Balance at exactly 2,000). No code change needed — this exchange was pure confirmation, not a bug.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — Dashboard's Best/Worst Portfolio and Total Return silently ignored unrealized P/L

User-reported real screenshot: an all-open, nothing-sold-yet portfolio ("SMC Auto Scanner") with a substantial unrealized gain showed up as "Worst Portfolio +0.00%" on the Dashboard — because `best`/`worst`/`totalValueWeightedReturn` all ranked by `analytics.portfolioReturn`, which is deliberately realized+dividend only (see its own doc comment). A portfolio that hasn't sold anything yet always reads as a flat 0% on that basis, regardless of how its open positions are actually doing — misleading for exactly the kind of buy-and-hold portfolio this app is meant to support.

- **`AnalyticsResult.totalReturnPct`** (new, `AnalyticsEngine.ts`): `portfolioReturn + unrealizedReturnPct` — an intentionally simple combined snapshot for ranking/comparing portfolios "right now, including what's still open." Documented as mixing two different denominators (cost basis ever invested vs. cost basis of currently-open positions only), so it's explicitly a headline figure, not offered as a mathematically pure single ratio.
- **`DashboardPage`**: `totalValueWeightedReturn`, `best`, and `worst` now rank by `totalReturnPct` instead of `portfolioReturn`; "Total Return" tile's sublabel updated to say so explicitly ("Value-weighted, incl. unrealized").
- **"Portfolio Comparison" chart deliberately left unchanged** (still realized+dividend only, no unrealized): extending that *cumulative curve over time* to include unrealized isn't a simple field swap like the snapshot metrics above — bucketPerformance's period-level unrealizedReturnPct is a delta against a growing, period-specific denominator, so naively summing those deltas across periods to build a comparable curve would silently understate/overstate the real number (the exact kind of percentage-across-different-bases bug this app's cash/return model was previously redesigned specifically to avoid — see the "remove Deposit/Withdrawal" sprint above). Its caption now explicitly says so and points to Total Return/Best/Worst Portfolio and the Monthly Performance chart (which already correctly includes unrealized) as the figures that do include it, rather than leaving the gap implicit.
- AnalyticsPage's own "Portfolio Return" tile is unchanged on purpose — it already sits directly next to a separate, clearly-labeled "Unrealized Return" tile on that page, so there's no ambiguity there the way there was on the Dashboard's single ranking number.
- 2 new/updated `computeAnalytics` test assertions for `totalReturnPct` (425 total, no new test files).
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: an all-open portfolio with a real unrealized gain and a separate portfolio with a modest realized gain — the all-open one now correctly wins "Best Portfolio" at its true unrealized %, and "Total Return" reflects the blended figure, instead of the all-open portfolio reading as a flat, misleading 0%.

### Post-sprint-8 fix — the per-portfolio "Total Assets" tile still blended cash into the headline stock value

User-reported follow-up, from a live screenshot: `PortfolioDetailPage`'s "Total Assets" tile (`marketValue + portfolio.cash`) was the one per-portfolio holdout from the earlier "Dashboard's Total Portfolio Value should be stock value only, not cash" fix — same complaint, different page. On the reported portfolio: Total Assets read E£80,565.63 (E£42,565.63 invested + E£38,000 cash), when only the E£42,565.63 stock value was wanted.

- **Removed the "Total Assets" tile entirely** from `PortfolioDetailPage` rather than changing it to market-value-only — that would have made it a byte-for-byte duplicate of the "Invested (Market Value)" tile sitting right next to it. Cash Balance and Invested (Market Value) are both still shown individually, just never pre-summed.
- No calculator/test changes needed (this was presentation-only); 425 tests still pass.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build: the portfolio detail page now shows exactly 3 stat tiles (Cash Balance, Invested (Market Value), Unrealized P/L) with no combined figure.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — the Import page's "ignore before 2026-01-01" filter is now a user-selectable start-year picker

Direct user request: the OCR import cutoff was a fixed `TRACKING_START_DATE = "2026-01-01"` constant, silently dropping any real transaction from before it — a real problem for anyone with older broker history. Asked whether this should be an Import-page-only filter or a genuine app-wide change; user chose the latter (recommended, since the old constant also gated manual entry — a value the OCR filter alone couldn't have honored without failing at commit time).

- **`trackingWindow.ts`** (domain): `TRACKING_START_DATE` constant replaced by a mutable module-level value with `getTrackingStartDate()`/`setTrackingStartDate()`, defaulting to the old `"2026-01-01"` so existing behavior is unchanged until a user actually picks a different year. `isBeforeTrackingStart()` now reads the live value.
- **`trackingStartDateStore.ts`** (new, presentation): reactive `localStorage`-backed wrapper (`useTrackingStartDate()`, mirrors `language.ts`'s pattern) that calls the domain setter directly, so `TradeService`/`PortfolioService`'s validation (no React dependency) sees the change immediately too, not just the UI.
- **`ImportPage`**: new "Import transactions starting from" year dropdown (2020 → current year) in the Step 1 box, defaulting to 2026; changing it re-filters the pending pool immediately (existing stale-candidate purge effect now also depends on the tracking start date) and takes effect on the next file parsed.
- **`ThndrParser`/`CsvStatementParser`**: `trackedSince` constructor param is now an optional override (tests still pin exact dates); with no override, the cutoff resolves live via `defaultTrackedSince()` on every parse instead of being frozen at construction time — necessary because `ImportOrchestrator`'s parser instances are memoized as a singleton.
- **`TradesPage`/`PortfolioDetailPage`/`SellAllocationForm`**: every manual-entry date input's `min` attribute now reads the live `useTrackingStartDate()` value instead of the old fixed constant.
- 445 tests passing (no test changes needed — all existing parser tests already pinned explicit override dates); typecheck and `arch:check` clean.
- Verified end-to-end against a real running build (English and Arabic): the dropdown lists 2026→2020, defaults to 2026, and picking 2021 updates the hint text ("Transactions before 2021-01-01 are ignored…") live with no console errors.

### Standard Trading Exchange Schema (STES v1.0) — design

Direct user request: design the official standard exchange format between external AI systems and Trade Manager — the single Excel format any AI (ChatGPT/Claude/Gemini/future) converts broker statements, PDFs, invoices, notifications, screenshots, and emails into, and the only external format Trade Manager accepts. Design-only sprint; the spec is the deliverable, the importer/exporter is deliberately a separate implementation sprint.

- **`docs/STANDARD_TRADING_EXCHANGE_SCHEMA.md`** (new): the complete v1.0 spec — three-sheet workbook (`Metadata` / `Transactions` / `Sell_Allocations`), full column definitions (name, type, required/optional, validation rules, description), field-ownership matrix, row→ledger transformation, tiered duplicate detection, and edited-row recognition on re-import.
- Designed to map **one-to-one onto the existing raw-transaction architecture** rather than inventing a parallel model: a BUY row becomes one `BuyExecution` fact → one immutable Trade (never aggregated); a SELL row becomes a `SellExecution` fact with allocations carried separately (`Sell_Allocations` sheet → `SellAllocationDecision`), so an unallocated sell is a legitimate imported state awaiting the in-app lot picker — FIFO/LIFO/average-cost never assumed; DIVIDEND rows become `DividendPayment` facts dated to the real payout. Edits are proposed `Correction` facts requiring user approval; file-row absence is never a deletion (`Retraction` stays in-app only).
- Duplicate matching codifies the ledger's existing rules as spec tiers: Ledger Transaction ID (round-trip identity, minted once by Trade Manager, echoed in exports) → broker `Transaction Reference` (`transactionNumber`/`sameExecution` semantics, including "mismatched reference excludes attribute-match candidacy") → count-aware ticker+date+quantity fingerprint with the `timesConflict` rule — which is also why the spec bans fabricated `00:00` times outright.
- Deliberate exclusions, each stated in the spec: portfolio assignment is not a column (organization, not a source-document fact — stays in the Distribute step as a `PortfolioAssignment` fact); deposits/withdrawals/transfers/funds are rejected, never coerced; `Gross Amount`/`Net Amount` are optional redundant cross-checks that flag rows rather than "fix" numbers.

### STES v1.1 — schema frozen, importer implemented end-to-end

The v1.0 design above was revised after a direct architectural challenge from the user ("the project is an Evidence Investigation Engine, not an Excel importer") and refrozen as **v1.1**: workbook rows are **observations** (one row per document × execution mention — the same execution seen by three documents is three rows, never merged by the generating AI), a `Documents` sheet gives every source document its own identity, and three v1.0 concepts were deliberately deleted from the raw-extraction contract because they were downstream logic smuggled into the exchange file: `Ledger Transaction ID` (doesn't exist at extraction time), the `Sell_Allocations` sheet (no broker document states lot allocation), and v1.0's §11 rule 8 ("emit once from the most authoritative source" — extraction-time evidence destruction that would have starved the Verification Engine of the very duplicate that upgrades an execution to verified). `docs/STANDARD_TRADING_EXCHANGE_SCHEMA.md` fully rewritten for v1.1; the official fillable template ships at `docs/templates/STES-v1.1-raw-extraction-template.xlsx`.

Implementation, converged into the one existing pipeline (user requirement: "another input source equivalent to PDF/OCR, not a parallel system"):

- **`src/infrastructure/stes/StesWorkbookParser.ts`** (new): reads/validates the workbook (`xlsx` dependency, dynamically imported so it stays its own lazy chunk — main bundle unchanged) and returns the exact `ParsedTradeCandidate`/`ParsedDividendCandidate` shapes the OCR parsers return. File-level failures (missing sheet/column, wrong schema name/major version, duplicate Document ID) reject the file with a specific message; every row-level problem rejects only that observation, warning by Observation ID with the exact reason. Blank = unknown (never 0); Excel date/serial cells coerced so real AI-generated workbooks need zero hand-editing; tracked-date-range filtering reuses `trackedDateRange.ts`; Gross-vs-Quantity×Price contradictions flag the row for review but never silently "fix" numbers. Zero matching/dedup/verification/ledger logic in the parser — two observations of one execution import as two raw facts, exactly like two separately-uploaded documents.
- **`ImportOrchestrator`**: routes `.xlsx` before any text extraction (new docType `"stes-workbook"`); the workbook's bytes are archived via `Upload.fileBlob` like any image/PDF evidence document. Existing image/PDF/CSV routing untouched.
- **Domain (additive)**: `RawTransactionSource` gained `"notification" | "email" | "screenshot" | "other-document"` (Documents-sheet types with no existing equivalent — STATEMENT/INVOICE/ORDERS_SCREEN/CSV_EXPORT map onto the existing sources so corroboration/authority treat an STES-carried statement identically to a self-parsed one; PDF deliberately maps to `other-document`, never fabricated statement authority). `ExtractionMethod` gained `"stes-workbook"`. `ParsedDividendCandidate.source` added so an STES dividend records its real document type (pre-STES default `"position-verification"` preserved). `evidenceAuthority.ts` ranks the four new sources at the generic tier.
- **Everything downstream reused unchanged**: `importRecording` appends the same immutable facts; duplicate detection, cross-source verification ("two documents agree"), the Completeness Engine, Constraint Check, and Evidence Graph all run on STES observations with zero new business logic; nothing writes to the ledger without explicit per-ticker portfolio assignment + user confirmation.
- 25 new tests (873 total): 22 parser tests (validation matrix, coercion, honest source mapping, zero-dedup) + 3 orchestrator routing tests (STES routed, non-STES xlsx fails with a named reason, CSV path regression-pinned).
- **Verified end-to-end in a real production build** (Playwright + Chromium against `dist/`): uploading a 4-observation workbook (COMI buy seen by statement AND invoice, EAST sell, EAST dividend) produced exactly the investigation the architecture promises — COMI "Verified — two documents agree" with the second observation flagged as the corroborating suspected-duplicate, EAST sell triggering the completeness recovery plan ("80 short… a My Position screenshot closes this gap"), constraint checks green, ledger untouched.

## Next recommended sprint

0. ~~**Implement the STES v1.1 importer**~~ — done (see "STES v1.1 — schema frozen, importer implemented end-to-end" above). Still open, deliberately deferred: an **exporter** (emitting the ledger back out as an STES-shaped workbook with ledger identity) is a different, round-trip contract — design it as its own explicitly-versioned template if/when the user wants AI-assisted ledger editing, not as a silent extension of the frozen raw-extraction template.
1. **Split/Rights Issue automatic rebasing**: still deliberately out of scope (see `PortfolioService.recordSplit`/`recordRightsIssue`); revisit if a real user hits this.
2. ~~**Sector Allocation**~~ — done (see above): `Trade.sector` added, auto-assigned from a known-ticker map, feeding a real Dashboard pie chart.
3. ~~**OCR confidence-aware UX**~~ — done, then superseded twice (see above): the original confirmation-checkbox gate was replaced by auto-commit with a visible low-confidence flag + delete action; auto-commit was then itself replaced by the broker-screenshot verification gate, per direct, explicit user feedback each time. The low-confidence flag + delete action on an already-committed row is still in place today, now reached via the Confirm button instead of either of the previous two mechanisms.
4. **A real second broker's screenshot format**: `CsvStatementParser` validated the interface with a non-OCR input; the OCR-specific parts of the interface (`parseOrdersScreenText`, `parseOrderRowsText`, `resolveHeaderTicker`) still only have one real implementation (Thndr) — worth validating against an actual second brokerage app's screenshots if/when real sample data is available.
5. ~~**Innovative ticker/company-name extraction accuracy improvements**~~ — partially done (see above): the two concrete duplicate-group bugs reported live (missing EGX tickers, inconsistent bracket-glyph OCR) are fixed; using the Invoice format's labeled "Symbol Code" (ISIN-like) field as a second corroborating signal is still open if another real misresolution surfaces.
6. ~~**Full Arabic translation with an EN/AR toggle**~~ — done (see Sprint 9 above): i18n infrastructure, sidebar toggle, and every page/component translated. Not yet covered: the `docs/` files themselves stay English-only (out of scope — user-facing app only), and no automated test asserts translation-key completeness (`en`/`ar` parity is currently only enforced by convention/code review, not a lint rule) — worth adding if the dictionaries keep growing.
7. **Cash/"allocated capital" tracking redesign** (user follow-up, still not fully resolved): user's complaint is that `Portfolio.cash` blends the original amount set aside for a portfolio with realized sell proceeds/dividends, making "how much of what I allocated is left" hard to read at a glance — despite `setCash`/"Edit Cash" already allowing a direct edit at any time. Likely needs a genuinely new concept (e.g. a separate "allocated capital" figure tracked independently of `cash`) rather than a tweak to the existing edit flow; get a concrete confirmation of the desired shape before implementing, since a wrong guess here means new domain state that's hard to unwind.
8. ~~**Reconciliation false-positive/negative fixes**~~ — done (see above): time-of-day added to the duplicate signature, a specific diagnostic for total header-resolution failure, and an advisory hint for a single-digit date misread. The proposed full `CanonicalTrade`/`TradeEvidence` rewrite remains declined — revisit only if a new, concrete failure surfaces that these narrow fixes don't cover.
9. ~~**Statement Aggregate Reconciliation**~~ — done (see "Statement Aggregate Reconciliation" near the end of the sprint log): a Statement row summarizing several same-day executions now reconciles against the group instead of surfacing as an extra candidate. Open follow-up: no real aggregated-row sample was available to validate against — worth re-checking `findAggregateStatementMatches`'s price tolerance if a user hits a mismatch on a genuine aggregated Statement row.
10. ~~**Constraint Validation Layer (Facts/Contradiction/Diagnosis separation)**~~ — done (see "Architectural audit — Constraint Validation Layer request" at the end of the sprint log): audited first, found the substance already shipped across several prior sprints, and added `constraintValidation.ts` plus a small additive "Constraint check" panel formalizing the separation as its own typed, tested API rather than implicit banner wording. Open follow-up, unchanged from item 1: corporate-action share adjustments (Split/RightsIssue) are still record-only, so the inventory formula has no "+ corporate actions" term yet — revisit together if a real user hits both at once.

11. ~~**Ledger Rebuild Engine, with Dry Run**~~ — done (see "Ledger Rebuild Engine, with Dry Run" at the end of the sprint log): deterministic reconstruction from source documents only, diffed against (never built from) the current ledger, dry-run-first UI on `DataPage`. Open follow-up: `ParsedOrderEvidence`/`ParsedDividendCandidate` aren't durably archived anywhere (only `Upload.candidates` and `PositionVerification` are) — a rebuild can't use Orders-history corroboration or dividend facts once the Import session that read them is gone. Worth a persistent document archive if a real rebuild run needs that evidence.
12. ~~**Architecture Foundation (raw-transaction log + Verification/Ledger/Allocation/Holdings/Commit Engines, phases 1–9)**~~ — done (see "Architecture Foundation" and its post-review fix entry at the end of the sprint log): additive-only, dual-written alongside the existing Trade/TradeAllocation architecture, continuously validated against it (`systemValidation.ts`), backfilled for pre-existing portfolios. ~~**The closed-position blind-trust bug (JUFO/SKPC)**~~ — done (see "Evidence-First Architecture Review + real bug fix" at the end of the sprint log): `checkTickerMatch` no longer auto-matches a net-zero position with zero corroboration; `completenessEngine`'s recovery-plan is now surfaced live in `ImportPage`; `Upload.fileBlob` persists original documents permanently. ~~**Phase 10 — Holdings/Dashboard/PortfolioDetail read cutover**~~ — done (see "Production read cutover" at the end of the sprint log): `computeCanonicalPositions` serves the canonical (`ledgerCache`/`computeHoldings`-derived) number when it agrees with legacy, self-validating and falling back to legacy per-ticker (with a disclosed reason) otherwise — the always-on runtime version of `systemValidation.validatePortfolio`'s one-time manual gate, so the cutover didn't need to wait on a manual trial period that this sandboxed session has no way to run. **Still open**: `moveTrade`/`correctTradeExecutionDate`/`consolidateTicker` still don't write their own facts (Phase 9.8's known limitation, unchanged); cash is dual-written (`CashReset`/`DividendPayment`/`CashAdjustment` facts) and a pure `computeCashProjection` exists and is tested, but the cash READ itself is still `portfolio.cash`, not the projection — blocked on running `backfillRawTransactions`'s new cash-event coverage against the real production database once (a one-time operational step, not more code; see "Production read cutover"'s own remaining-blocker note). **Phase 11: legacy removal** — only once cash is also cut over and both cutovers have run in production for a real trial period with zero validation blockers; remove `Trade`/`TradeAllocation`/`PositionVerification` tables and every function that reads/writes them, and make `Portfolio.cash` a derived projection instead of an imperatively-mutated field, per this migration's own "never remove the old path until the new one is proven" discipline.

13. ~~**Lot Manager (replaces the Sell Allocation popup) + the identity-collision cross-sell corruption bug**~~ — done (see "Lot Manager + the identity-collision root-cause fix" at the end of the sprint log): fixed the reported production bug (allocating one Sell could silently mutate an unrelated Sell/Buy lot), then built the full ticker-scoped Lot Manager (Portfolio → Ticker Details → Lot Manager) on top of the fix. **Open follow-ups, not done in this sprint**: (a) `TickerDetailPage.tsx`/the Lot Manager's `RecordSellModal`/`ManageAllocationModal` are English-only — every other page has full EN/AR translation (Sprint 9), this one doesn't yet; (b) the Lot Manager reads/writes RawTransactions directly and does NOT gate on import-verification (`verifyAll`) — correct for its own purpose (see that entry's architecture note) but means a ticker touched only via the Lot Manager may show `source: "legacy-fallback"` on `canonicalHoldings.ts`'s reconciliation until its facts happen to also satisfy `verifyAll`'s terminal-verdict rule for the OLD `commitTicker`-gated cache — worth revisiting once real usage shows whether that fallback banner is confusing; (c) `ensureLegacyFactsExist`'s id-linkage self-healing is additive-only for NEW gaps (N colliding trades now correctly get N facts) but does not retroactively re-link an OLD backfilled fact whose id predates this fix to its Trade's own id — harmless (decisions still resolve via the value-hash fallback as long as that old data isn't ALSO colliding), but a real edge case if a user's very old pre-Phase-9.8 history happens to contain two coincidentally-identical trades already merged by the pre-fix bug — that data is already lost and this fix can't recover it, only prevent new occurrences.

Each of these should get its own gap-check at sprint start — this list is a starting point, not a commitment, and should be re-prioritized against whatever the repo audit finds at that time.

### Sprint 9 — Full Arabic translation with an EN/AR toggle

Executed item 6 from the list above: zero i18n infrastructure existed before this sprint — every string was a hardcoded English literal in JSX.

- **`src/presentation/i18n/language.ts`**: a module-level language store (`"en" | "ar"`, persisted to `localStorage`, `useSyncExternalStore`-backed `useLanguage()` hook) — the same pattern `importSession.ts` already established, chosen for consistency and because plain functions like `formatMoney`/`formatDate` (called from dozens of places outside any component tree) need to read the current language synchronously, not through React context.
- **`src/presentation/i18n/translations.ts`**: `en`/`ar` dictionaries (one namespace per page/component, ~40 namespaces) behind a single `translate()`/`useT()` — dot-path key lookup with `{{var}}` interpolation; a dictionary entry can be a plain string or a `(vars) => string` function for pluralization (`enPlural`/`arPlural` helpers — Arabic gets a dedicated zero/one/two/plural branch rather than English's simpler singular/plural, since "one portfolio" vs "two portfolios" reads naturally in Arabic where a bolted-on `{{n}}` wouldn't). English is the source of truth; every Arabic namespace mirrors it key-for-key.
- **`format.ts` made locale-aware**: `formatMoney`/`formatDate`/etc. now pick `en-EG`/`en-GB` vs `ar-EG-u-nu-latn` based on the current language — Arabic gets real month names and the currency symbol's natural position, but the `-u-nu-latn` locale extension deliberately keeps Western digits in both languages (confirmed via a quick `Intl.NumberFormat` check that plain `ar-EG` switches to Arabic-Indic numerals, which would look broken against a numbers-heavy trading table and isn't what Egyptian fintech apps typically do).
- **Sidebar** gained a language toggle button (next to the brand mark) showing the *other* language's name — flips `languageStore` on click, no page reload needed since every page reads the current language reactively.
- **RTL layout mirroring** (immediate user follow-up, superseding the original "toggle only, not RTL" scope): `document.documentElement.dir`/`lang` now follow the selected language (set in `App.tsx`'s `AppShell`, reactive to `useLanguage()`), and every physical-direction Tailwind utility across the presentation layer (`ml-`/`mr-`/`pl-`/`pr-`, `left-`/`right-`, `text-left`/`text-right`, `border-l`/`border-r`) was converted to its logical equivalent (`ms-`/`me-`/`ps-`/`pe-`, `start-`/`end-`, `text-start`/`text-end`, `border-e`) so the whole app mirrors automatically under `dir="rtl"` — flexbox rows already reverse for free per the CSS spec, logical properties handle spacing/alignment, and `rtl:`/`ltr:` variants handle the one case logical properties can't (the mobile drawer's `translateX` transform, which is physical by nature). One real bug surfaced and was fixed during this pass: the drawer's `rtl:translate-x-full` initially beat the desktop `lg:translate-x-0` reset at `lg+` breakpoints because the `[dir="rtl"]`-scoped selector has higher CSS specificity than a bare breakpoint variant regardless of viewport — fixed by scoping the closed-state transform to `max-lg:` so it structurally can't apply above `lg` at all. Verified end-to-end with Playwright at both desktop (sidebar correctly docks on the right, main content on the left) and mobile (390px) viewports (drawer correctly slides in/out from the right edge when open/closed in Arabic) — before the fix, the desktop sidebar was rendered 256px off-screen to the right; after, its bounding box sits exactly against the right edge of the viewport as expected.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — ticker/company-name spacing bug, and BuyZoneChart's un-mirrored axis

Two direct user follow-ups from actually using the Arabic UI:

1. **Ticker and company name rendered with no gap between them** (e.g. "COMICommercial International Bank" on `TradesPage`'s holdings table and `JournalPage`'s Lessons Learned cards) — root cause: `{trade.ticker}` and `<span className="ms-2">{trade.companyName}</span>` are two adjacent DOM text runs, both pure Latin script, with nothing bidi-isolating them from each other. Under `dir="rtl"`, the Unicode Bidi Algorithm doesn't treat element boundaries as run breaks on their own, so the two runs merge into one contiguous LTR run for reordering purposes — and the CSS margin meant to sit between them (`margin-inline-start`, i.e. physical `margin-right` under RTL) ends up on the wrong side of that merged run, collapsing visually to zero gap. Fixed by wrapping the ticker+company-name pair in an explicit `<span dir="ltr">` — this is inherently LTR content (EGX tickers and company names are always Latin) regardless of the app's current language, so isolating it as its own bidi/formatting context is the correct fix generally, not just a workaround for this one symptom.
2. **`BuyZoneChart`'s bars/axes stayed LTR-oriented in Arabic**, explicitly called out as a known limitation in the previous entry — revisited on direct request rather than left as a permanent gap, since it's a self-contained, boundable piece of work (one component) rather than the "materially larger effort" concern that applied to mirroring every chart in the app. `BuyZoneChart` now reads `useLanguage()` directly (SVG-rendered charts don't inherit `dir` the way DOM/flexbox layout does) and mirrors: `XAxis reversed`, `YAxis orientation="right"`, the chart `margin`, the price `LabelList` position, and the `Bar`'s rounded corner side all flip together so the zero-price origin sits on the right (matching RTL reading direction) with the price label staying at the bar's tip end instead of at its base.
- Verified end-to-end with Playwright: recorded a COMI buy with a company name in Arabic mode, confirmed a real visible gap now renders between "COMI" and "Commercial International Bank" on both `TradesPage` and `JournalPage`, and confirmed `BuyZoneChart` now shows its price axis descending left-to-right (140→0) with the bar anchored at the right (zero) edge and the price label at its left (tip) end — matching the rest of the RTL layout instead of standing out as the one LTR-oriented element on the page.
- Every page and shared component translated: `Sidebar`, `App` shell chrome, `Modal`/`PriceFreshness`, `DashboardPage`, `PortfoliosPage` (+ its split/misnamed-ticker banners and create-portfolio modal), `PortfolioDetailPage` (+ cash/corporate-action/rename modals, reconciliation banners), `TradesPage` (+ record buy/sell/move-trade modals), `SellAllocationForm`, `TimelinePage` (+ its per-event-type `describe()` sentences), `JournalPage`, `AnalyticsPage`, `DataPage`, `BuyZoneChart`, `CapitalDeploymentFlow`, and `ImportPage` in full — the heaviest single file (2,241 lines: the two-phase extract/verify workflow, every mismatch/verification banner, `MatchBadge`, `AutoCommitRow`, `CandidateRow`, and all their badges/tooltips).
- Verified end-to-end with Playwright against the real running app (not mocked): toggled to Arabic, confirmed the Dashboard/Portfolios/Portfolio Detail/Trades/Record Buy modal/Analytics/Import/Data pages all render fully translated with no leftover English chrome, correct `E£`/date formatting (Western digits, Arabic month names), the toggle persists across a reload, and toggling back to English restores the original UI — no console errors on any page.
- 426 existing tests still pass unchanged (no test coverage added specifically for i18n — the translation layer is presentation-only string substitution with no new business logic to unit-test; correctness was verified via the live-app Playwright pass above instead).

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — BuyZoneChart's date-axis labels overlapping/unreadable in Arabic

Direct user report with a screenshot: after mirroring `BuyZoneChart` under RTL, the Y-axis's date labels ("07 أبريل 2026" etc.) rendered as illegible overlapping text bleeding into the bars, instead of clean labels next to the axis.

- **Root cause, found by inspecting the rendered SVG directly**: recharts' `CartesianAxis.getTickTextAnchor()` computes `textAnchor = mirror ? 'end' : 'start'` for `orientation="right"` — the *opposite* of `orientation="left"`'s `mirror ? 'start' : 'end'`. Recharts' `right` orientation is designed for a *mirrored* left axis (a second axis on the right showing the same data), not a genuinely right-docked primary axis — so without `mirror` set, it defaults to `textAnchor: "start"`, which grows each label *rightward* from its anchor point instead of ending flush against the axis line. With the axis now sitting at the right edge of a narrow chart, that pushed the label text off the SVG's right edge entirely, overlapping the bars and getting clipped mid-word.
- **Fix**: `YAxis`'s `tick` prop now explicitly sets `textAnchor: "end"` unconditionally (recharts' `tick` object is spread onto the internal `Text` component and does override the computed default — confirmed by reading `CartesianAxis.js`'s prop-merge order). This is the same anchor `orientation="left"` already defaulted to, so it's a correctness fix for `right`, not a new behavior for `left`.
- Verified end-to-end with Playwright: reproduced the exact reported shape (4 COMI buys at different dates, narrow mobile-width chart) — confirmed the SVG tick's `text-anchor` attribute flips from `start` to `end` after the fix, and the rendered labels are now clean and legible next to the axis instead of overlapping the bars. Also confirmed English mode shows the identical 2-of-4 tick-skipping pattern (recharts' own overlap-avoidance interval logic, unrelated to this fix) — so Arabic now behaves consistently with English rather than differently.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — BuyZoneChart's date labels still cramped/wrapping mid-word in Arabic

Direct user follow-up with a second screenshot, right after the `text-anchor` fix shipped: labels no longer overlapped the bars, but still read as cramped and awkward — e.g. "فبراير" (February) wrapping onto a second line as just its last letter, with almost no breathing room before the bars.

- **Root cause**: the Y-axis's reserved `width` (72px, unchanged since the original English-only chart) was sized for English month abbreviations ("Feb", "Mar" — 3 characters). Arabic doesn't abbreviate month names the same way (`Intl.DateTimeFormat`'s `month: "short"` still returns the full word — "فبراير", "سبتمبر" — 6-9 characters), so the same column that fits "19 Feb 2026" on one line forces "19 فبراير 2026" into recharts' auto-wrap with barely enough room, producing the cramped/mid-word-split look.
- **Fix**: for Arabic specifically, `YAxis` now gets a wider reserved column (`width={92}` vs `72`) and a slightly smaller tick font (`10px` vs `11px`) — both of the two options the user explicitly suggested ("shrink the text or widen the space"), applied together rather than picking just one, since combining them gave the cleanest result in testing (shorter dates now fit on one line entirely; the one still-long "19 فبراير 2026" wraps to two lines but with real breathing room instead of touching the plot edge). English is completely unaffected (`width`/`fontSize` for that branch are the same values as before).
- Verified end-to-end with Playwright at a 390px mobile viewport (matching the reported phone screenshot) with the exact reported dates (19 Feb ×2, 25 Feb, 02 Mar, 04 Mar 2026) — measured the tick's actual rendered bounding box before/after: the gap between the label's right edge and the plot's right edge nearly doubled (28px → 52px), and the shorter "02/04 مارس 2026" labels now render on a single line instead of wrapping at all.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — every remaining time-series chart in the app stayed LTR-oriented in Arabic

Direct user follow-up with a screenshot: `BuyZoneChart` had already been mirrored under RTL, but it was the only chart component that read `useLanguage()` — the Dashboard's Portfolio Comparison (line) and Monthly Performance (bar) charts, and the Analytics page's Performance (line) and Monthly Return (bar) charts, still ran left-to-right (oldest date on the left) even in Arabic mode, so the app's own historical figures visually contradicted the RTL reading direction surrounding them.

- **Fix, applied identically to all four charts** (`DashboardPage.tsx`, `AnalyticsPage.tsx`): each now reads `useLanguage()` and sets `XAxis reversed={isRtl}` (flips the chronological order so the most recent period sits on the right, matching RTL reading order) plus `YAxis orientation={isRtl ? "right" : "left"}` with `tick={{ ..., textAnchor: "end" }}` — the same `textAnchor: "end"` override already proven correct for `BuyZoneChart`'s right-docked axis (recharts' `orientation="right"` default assumes a mirrored left axis and computes the wrong anchor otherwise). The two donut/pie charts (Portfolio Allocation, Sector Allocation) were left untouched — they have no axis or inherent left-right direction to mirror.
- Verified end-to-end with Playwright against the real running app: seeded two portfolios with trades spanning 6 months, confirmed in English the X-axis reads left-to-right (Feb → Jul) as before (no regression), then toggled to Arabic and confirmed all four charts now read right-to-left (Jul on the right descending to Feb on the left) with the percentage Y-axis correctly re-docked on the right edge — matching the same mirroring already shipped for `BuyZoneChart`.
- 426 existing tests still pass unchanged (presentation-only change, no new business logic).

### Cloudflare Workers deployment (out-of-band bot PR) — three follow-up fixes to actually make it work

The user connected this repo to Cloudflare, which opened bot PR #57 ("Add Cloudflare Workers configuration", `wrangler.jsonc` + `@cloudflare/vite-plugin`) — reviewed, fixed, and merged per explicit user direction (not a self-initiated sprint). Three real bugs surfaced in sequence, each only visible once the previous one was fixed and the actual deploy was attempted:

1. **`@cloudflare/vite-plugin` crashed Vitest's own dev server** — its `configureServer` hook assumes a real dev/build Vite instance. Fixed by guarding it out under `process.env.VITEST` (Vitest's documented signal) in `vite.config.ts`.
2. **`@cloudflare/vite-plugin` statically imports `node:module`'s `registerHooks`**, an API requiring Node ≥22.15 (matches `wrangler`/`miniflare`'s own `engines` field) — but `ci.yml` and `deploy-pages.yml` were both pinned to Node 20, so merely importing the plugin at the top of `vite.config.ts` crashed `npm test` *and* `npm run build` in CI regardless of the guard above. Reproduced the exact CI failure locally by running the same Node 20 binary CI uses; fixed by bumping both workflows to Node 22 (confirmed lint/test/build all pass under it).
3. **`wrangler deploy` failed outright** with "The `assets` property in your configuration is missing the required `directory` property" — the bot-generated `wrangler.jsonc` never set `assets.directory`, so it had no idea the built output lives in `dist/`. Reproduced via `wrangler deploy --dry-run`; fixed by adding `"directory": "dist"`.
4. **The built HTML still pointed at `/trade-manager/assets/...`** on the Cloudflare build even after fix #3 — `vite.config.ts`'s `base` was hardcoded to `/trade-manager/` unconditionally (correct for GitHub Pages, wrong for Cloudflare Workers, which serves from the domain root). Fixed by making `base` conditional: root (`/`) by default — correct for Cloudflare, local dev, and this repo's own CI smoke-test build — with `/trade-manager/` only applied when `deploy-pages.yml`'s build step explicitly sets `GH_PAGES_BUILD=1`. Verified by building both ways and inspecting `dist/index.html` directly: default build emits `/assets/index-*.js`, `GH_PAGES_BUILD=1` emits `/trade-manager/assets/index-*.js`. Also smoke-tested the default (Cloudflare-target) build end-to-end with Playwright against `vite preview` — 200 response, correct title, `#root` populated, zero console/network errors — confirming the root-base build actually runs, not just that the HTML looks right.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — mobile viewport: tables and text overflowing horizontally off-screen (Safari/Chrome, iPhone)

User-reported real screenshot from an iPhone (Safari, Arabic mode): `TradesPage`'s holdings table rendered with content cut off on both edges of the screen, unreachable by scrolling — the page itself had gone horizontally wider than the viewport instead of the table scrolling within its own card.

- **Root cause**: `TradesPage.tsx`'s main trades `<table>` and its nested per-lot allocations `<table>` (expand row) had no `overflow-x-auto` wrapper — unlike `PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`/`AnalyticsPage.tsx`, which already wrap their tables this way. A `<table className="w-full">` with more columns than fit a ~375px viewport forces its containing block (and therefore the whole page, since nothing else in the tree clips it) to grow wider than the viewport, instead of scrolling in place. `SellAllocationForm.tsx`'s table had the same gap, compounded: its wrapper used `overflow-hidden`, which clips the extra columns rather than exposing them via scroll — worse than a missing wrapper, since scrolling couldn't reveal them either.
- **Fix**: wrapped all three tables in `<div className="overflow-x-auto">` (nested inside `SellAllocationForm`'s existing `overflow-hidden` rounded-corner wrapper, so corners still clip but the inner div scrolls). Verified end-to-end with Playwright at an iPhone 13 viewport (390×844) in Arabic mode, with real long ticker/company-name data seeded through the UI: page-level `document.documentElement.scrollWidth` no longer exceeds the viewport, while the table's own scroll container measured `scrollWidth: 750` vs `clientWidth: 356` (genuinely scrollable) — and manually scrolling it (accounting for Chrome's negative-`scrollLeft` RTL convention) reveals every column (remaining shares, entry price, fees, status, delete action) that was previously stuck off-screen.
- **Secondary overflow-risk sweep** (same audit, same root class of bug — a flex/grid ancestor without `flex-wrap`/`min-w-0` letting a long string force the row wider than its container): `TradesPage.tsx`'s Buy Zone header row (title + ticker `<select>`) gained `flex-wrap`; `JournalPage.tsx`'s per-trade journal editor header (ticker/shares/price vs. Save button) and its Lessons Learned card header (ticker/company vs. date) gained `flex-wrap`/`min-w-0`/`shrink-0`/`truncate` so a long company name can no longer push the date or the button off the visible row; free-form user text with no natural word breaks (`TimelinePage.tsx`'s timeline-event notes, `JournalPage.tsx`'s Lessons Learned body) gained `break-words` so a single long unbroken string can't force its own overflow.
- 426 existing tests still pass unchanged (presentation-only change, no new business logic). Verified end-to-end against the real running app with Playwright rather than just typechecking, since this class of bug is invisible to `tsc`/unit tests and only shows up in an actual narrow viewport.

CLAUDE.md's architecture section now documents both deploy targets. GitHub Pages remains primary/documented; Cloudflare Workers is a second target the user opted into.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — the ORAS backfill self-heal from the earlier frozen-history fix never actually fired

User noticed, from three real screenshots, that the Dashboard's "Realized + Dividend Return"/"Portfolio Comparison" curves for a portfolio holding ORAS since January looked like they should be better than shown — every indicator that touches `priceHistory` seemed to jump all at once instead of building up gradually, even though the ORAS position had been winning the whole time.

- **Root cause**: the earlier frozen-history fix (`### Post-sprint-8 fix — one corrupted ticker's frozen Yahoo backfill...`) purged ORAS's bad entries down to "the one confirmed-real day" specifically so the next scheduled run would re-backfill it — but `main()`'s retry condition (`existingHistory && length > 0 && !isFrozenHistory`) treats *any* non-empty, non-frozen history as usable, no matter how few days it covers. That one real day (plus each day's live-quote append since) was permanently "usable" by that test, so the promised re-backfill never actually ran — confirmed live in `public/price-history.json`: every other known ticker has ~489 days back to 2024-07-07, ORAS has exactly 2 (2026-07-05, 2026-07-06). Any date-bucketed calculation (`bucketPerformance`'s `unrealizedReturnPct`, feeding Monthly Performance/Monthly Return) has no ORAS price before 07-05, so it correctly reports 0% for every earlier period (never fabricated) and then dumps the entire accumulated gain into the last day or two once real data exists — a real, large win misrepresented as a sudden spike instead of the gradual build it actually was.
- **Fix (`scripts/fetch-prices/index.ts`)**: new exported `needsBackfill()` replaces the inline `existingIsUsable` check, adding a `MIN_BACKFILLED_HISTORY_DAYS` (30) floor — a full 2y backfill is ~489 trading days, so anything drastically short of that is far more likely to be leftover day-by-day appends from a past failed/frozen backfill than a stock that's only been trading a few weeks, and re-running the backfill is harmless either way.
- 4 new tests (`needsBackfill`: missing, frozen-but-long, real-full-backfill, sparse-real-days like ORAS's actual state) — 430 total. Did not hand-edit the committed `price-history.json` this time (unlike the previous fix): the next scheduled `fetch-prices` run now backfills ORAS on its own under the corrected guard, so the fix is verified by the guard condition itself rather than a one-off manual purge.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — Yahoo's ORAS backfill is persistently frozen, not transiently; added a real second data source

Direct follow-up: manually ran `update-prices.yml` (`workflow_dispatch`) against the just-merged `needsBackfill` fix to confirm ORAS would self-heal. It didn't — the job's own log showed the retry *did* fire this time (proving the previous fix's logic is correct), but Yahoo rejected the same way as before: `Could not backfill history for ORAS: Yahoo returned a frozen (single-value) history for ORAS — discarding`. So Yahoo's bad EGX chart-history coverage for this ticker is a standing upstream gap, not a one-off blip — retrying the same provider indefinitely was never going to recover it. User, when told, explicitly authorized adding another free provider rather than depending on Yahoo alone.

- **`estimateHistoryFromPerformance`** (new, `scripts/fetch-prices/index.ts`): a second, genuinely different real-data path using TradingView's scanner — already the trusted live-quote provider ("actively covers the EGX", see `fetchFromTradingView`) — requesting its performance-percentage columns (`Perf.W/1M/3M/6M/Y/YTD`) alongside `close` and back-calculating each anchor's real historical price as `close / (1 + perf / 100)`. Sparser than a true daily backfill (a handful of week/month/year-ago points instead of ~490 daily closes) but still real market data derived from a real provider, not fabricated — used only when Yahoo's bulk history is unavailable/frozen for a ticker.
- **`main()`**'s backfill branch now falls back to this estimate on a Yahoo failure, before finally falling back to keeping whatever non-corrupt history already existed (unchanged last resort).
- 4 new tests (`estimateHistoryFromPerformance`: single-anchor back-calculation, all-anchors-plus-YTD, a missing individual `Perf.*` column skips only that anchor, missing `close` returns nothing) — 434 total.
- Manually re-triggered `update-prices.yml` again after this fix to confirm ORAS actually gets real anchor points this time (not just a passing test) before considering this closed.

### Post-Sprint-9 — second account-wide history shape: the "Transactions" screen, matched without a "My Position" screenshot

User-reported real gap, from three screenshots of the same Thndr account: the app's account-wide **"Transactions"** screen (tabs Completed/Pending/Cancelled; every row a real ticker code + Buy/Sell + an actual execution date/time + a signed net total, e.g. "Sell JUFO 17 Jan 23 – 3:20pm 737.96") is a different screen from the already-supported **"Orders" timeline** (Format 2c — "Buy/Sell Limit/Market @price", undated) and the already-supported per-stock **"Orders" screen** (Format 2 — already correctly parses the two JUFO screenshots, English and Arabic, into trade candidates with real shares/price). The Transactions screen went entirely unparsed before this fix — its rows match none of the four existing formats (no qty@price bracket for a statement row, no "Limit/Market" keyword for the timeline, no per-row "N shares" for the per-stock Orders screen). The user asked specifically that this screen's rows, matched on ticker/date/quantity/avg price against a pending row, import without needing a "My Position" broker screenshot — exactly the role `checkTickerMatch`'s existing `allPendingOrderConfirmed` gate already plays for Format 2c evidence, just via a second, dated evidence shape.

- **`ParsedOrderEvidence`** (`domain/entities/Upload.ts`) now covers two shapes sharing one interface: the existing undated one (`orderType`/`shares`/`price` set, no `date`) and a new dated one (`date`/`time` set, `orderType`/`shares`/`price` all undefined — this screen never prints a share count or per-share price, only a signed total). `date`'s presence is the discriminant the matcher branches on.
- **`ThndrParser`** gained Format 2d: detects the Transactions screen (`looksLikeTransactionsScreenImpl` — actually parses candidate rows rather than just testing for an anchor substring, so it can't misfire on an unrelated document; the statement/invoice/per-stock-Orders-screen formats never pair a `Buy/Sell <4 letters>` shape with a day-month-year + AM/PM timestamp immediately after it) and parses each row (`parseTransactionsScreenImpl`) into the new dated `ParsedOrderEvidence` shape. Wired into the existing `looksLikeOrdersTimeline`/`parseOrdersTimeline` interface methods (no `BrokerParser` interface change) rather than a fifth method, since it plays the identical corroboration role.
- **`orderEvidence.ts`** (`findOrderConfirmedKeys`/`findWrongTickerHintsFromOrders`): matching now branches on `evidence.date` — present, it requires ticker/side/date equality plus the row's total value ≈ candidate's `shares × price` (within the existing 5% tolerance); absent, the original ticker/side/shares/price check is unchanged. `orderEvidenceContentKey` (cross-file scroll-overlap dedup) folds in `date`/`time` so a different day's row for the same ticker/side/total is never treated as an overlapping duplicate.
- `ImportPage`'s order-evidence row rendering (and its tooltip copy, EN+AR) branches on the same `evidence.date` presence to show "Transactions history: Buy/Sell on {{date}} — total {{total}}" instead of the shares/price/order-type phrasing, since this shape has neither.
- 6 new tests (`orderEvidence.test.ts` ×3, `ThndrParser.test.ts` ×3) — 451 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean. Verified against the user's own screenshots' real text shapes (the JUFO Transactions rows, and confirmed the per-stock Orders screenshots — English and Arabic — still parse as trade candidates unaffected by the new format).

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — "no-verification" banner now surfaces the current net share total

Live debugging session with the user over a real, fully-closed position (JUFO — sold out entirely, so no broker "My Position" screenshot exists or ever will for it): after ruling out actual bugs (duplicate-clearing was confirmed working; the account-wide Transactions/Orders-history evidence from the previous fix was confirmed rendering and matching correctly), the real blocker turned out to be `checkTickerMatch`'s other escape hatch for exactly this case — "closed-position" (net shares across every pending Buy/Sell reconciling to exactly 0 needs no screenshot at all) — with no way for the user to see how close the batch's rows actually were to netting to zero. With ~30+ rows spanning Dec 2022–Aug 2024, manually tallying Buy shares minus Sell shares from the screen wasn't practical.

- `TickerGroupCard`'s "no-verification" banner (`ImportPage.tsx`) now interpolates `matchStatus.netShares` (already computed by `checkTickerMatch` on every branch, just never surfaced in this one) directly into the existing amber banner text, EN+AR: "Current net from the rows below: {{netShares}} shares — if this position is fully closed, that needs to reach exactly 0 to verify automatically, with no screenshot at all."
- 1 new component test (`TickerGroupCard` renders the exact net for a `no-verification` status) — 452 total.
- Verified end-to-end with a Playwright script against the real running dev server (seeded `localStorage`'s `portfolio-os:import-session` directly with a JUFO batch shaped like the user's real data — two pending Buys, one pending Sell, one matching Transactions-history evidence row — bypassing OCR): confirmed the banner renders "Current net from the rows below: 31 shares" (36 + 15 − 20, arithmetically correct) alongside the existing Orders-history suffix and the Sell row's "Matches Orders history" badge, screenshotted for visual confirmation.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — no-verification tickers now badge exactly which row is the likely culprit

Direct immediate follow-up in the same JUFO debugging session: showing the net share total (previous fix) answers "how far off am I" but not "which specific transaction is wrong" — the user asked for that explicitly ("I can't calculate this myself, you should tell me which transaction is the mistake and fix it"). A true combinatorial solver (`suggestRemovalsToReconcile`, already built for the "mismatch" case) was considered and rejected for this case: it's capped at 16 rows for tractability, JUFO's real batch has 30+, and for a batch this size and this ambiguous, picking one "the" answer out of many equally-valid subsets would be false confidence dressed up as math — not the answer the user actually needs.

The real fix was smaller and already 90% built: `highlightUnmatchedByOrders` (the amber "No matching order" per-row badge, driven by `orderConfirmedKeys`) already existed for the "mismatch" reason — a ticker's account-wide Orders/Transactions-history evidence corroborating some rows and not others, with the uncorroborated ones badged as the likely place a missing/misread/duplicate transaction is hiding. It just wasn't wired up for "no-verification" (no broker screenshot at all — JUFO's actual case, since a fully-sold-out position has no "My Position" screen to ever upload).

- `TickerGroupCard`'s `highlightUnmatchedByOrders` (`ImportPage.tsx`) now fires for `reason === "mismatch"` OR `reason === "no-verification"`, whenever the ticker's uploaded order history has at least one fulfilled row — scales to any number of pending rows (O(n) per-row evidence lookup, not a combinatorial search), and reuses the exact same badge/tooltip/discard-evidence UI already shipped for the mismatch case, no new component.
- `needsScreenshotSuffixHasOrders` (EN+AR) now explicitly points at the badge: "...rows below flagged 'No matching order' are the likely place a missing/misread/duplicate transaction is hiding; a position screenshot also settles it."
- 1 new component test (a no-verification ticker with one confirmed and one unconfirmed row shows both "Matches Orders history" and "No matching order") — 453 total.
- Verified end-to-end with Playwright against the real dev server: seeded a JUFO-shaped batch (2 Buys + 2 Sells netting to 6, one Sell confirmed by a Transactions-history evidence row) and confirmed all three uncorroborated rows badge "No matching order" in amber while the confirmed Sell badges "Matches Orders history" in cyan — screenshotted for visual confirmation.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — no-verification banner names the exact date the gap starts

Direct immediate follow-up in the same session, working from a second real ticker (ISPH, 16 pending Buys + 4 pending Sells, net 247 shares, no order-history evidence uploaded at all so the per-row badge from the previous fix couldn't narrow anything down). The user manually asked "which transaction, and when" — walking their own pasted row list by hand (in this chat, not in the app) showed something structural: a 5-Buy/2-Sell batch from Jan 2023 summed to exactly 5,700 both ways (perfectly clean), and the entire 247-share gap was isolated to the Buys/Sells dated 2024 — the imbalance had a specific start date, it wasn't smeared across the whole history.

That's a generalizable, deterministic computation, not a one-off: `findLastBalancedDate` (new, `application/services/netShareTimeline.ts`) walks a ticker's still-pending rows in chronological order, tracking the running net share count from whatever's already on the ledger, and finds the LAST date the running total returns to exactly 0. Everything up to and including that date reconciles a fully closed position; whatever's wrong only ever lives after it. Deliberately not the combinatorial `suggestRemovalsToReconcile` approach (capped at 16 rows, and would have to guess one subset out of many equally-valid ones for a batch this size) — this is exact arithmetic with no guessing, and scales to any row count.

- `TickerGroupCard`'s "no-verification" banner (`ImportPage.tsx`) now shows a second line when a balanced point is found: "Suggestion: every row through {{date}} already nets to exactly 0 — the gap starts in whatever's dated after that, so start your search there." (EN+AR).
- 6 new unit tests (`netShareTimeline.test.ts`, including the exact ISPH row list reproduced from the user's own pasted data) + 1 new component test — 460 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.
- Verified end-to-end with Playwright against the real dev server, seeding the ISPH batch exactly as the user reported it (20 rows, real dates/shares/prices): confirmed the banner renders "Current net from the rows below: 247 shares" plus "Suggestion: every row through 09 Jan 2023 already nets to exactly 0..." — matching the manual analysis exactly, screenshotted for visual confirmation.

### Post-Sprint-9 fix — Step 2 no longer buries still-pending tickers under already-finished ones

User-reported real workflow gap: once a ticker's buys were committed and its sells (if any) allocated, its card just stayed in Step 2's list forever, identical in weight to a ticker still genuinely blocked on a broker screenshot or an unallocated sell — with enough real tickers imported (verified/waiting/duplicate/etc. all mixed together) there was no way to tell at a glance which ones still needed a decision.

- **`isTickerFullyResolved`** (new, `application/services/importVerification.ts`): a pure function — matched, plus every buy/sell key in `addedKeys`/`skippedKeys`/`dismissedKeys`, every dividend key in `addedKeys`, every verification key in `acceptedKeys`, and no key stuck in `rowErrors` — same pattern as `checkTickerMatch`, unit-tested directly rather than only through a rendered page. A ticker with zero buy/sell rows (dividend/verification-only) never resolves this way, since there's no "sell = buy" question to answer for it.
- **`ImportPage`** now splits `tickerGroups` into `activeTickerGroups` (rendered as before) and `completedTickerGroups`, which collapse into a single "Fully matched (N)" banner directly under the Step 2 header — expanding it lists each ticker with its company name and transaction count ("COMI (Commercial International Bank) fully matched — 1 transaction", EN+AR with correct Arabic pluralization). The Step 2 status line, the matched/unmatched counts, and the Confirm buttons now all read off `activeTickerGroups` instead of the full pool, and a new `allDoneStatus` message replaces the confusing "0 of 0" text once every extracted ticker has resolved.
- 7 new unit tests (`isTickerFullyResolved`) — 512 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.
- Verified end-to-end with Playwright against the real dev server (seeded a matched COMI buy + verification and a still-blocked EAST buy with no screenshot via `localStorage`, then clicked COMI's own Confirm button): confirmed COMI's card disappears from the active list the moment it's committed, collapses into "Fully matched (1)" with the exact expected line, EAST stays visible as the only active card, and the same flow renders correctly in Arabic (RTL layout, "تم مطابقة سهم COMI (Commercial International Bank) بالكامل — معاملة واحدة", "كل الأسهم اتطابقت وتوزّعت بالكامل..." once nothing active remains) — screenshotted for visual confirmation in both languages.

### Import accuracy audit — broker Transaction Number as the preferred duplicate/match key

A full audit of the existing OCR import pipeline (document detection, `ThndrParser`/`CsvStatementParser`, `ImportOrchestrator`, `duplicateDetection`, `orderEvidence`, `netShareTimeline`, `mismatchResolver`, and the recording services), explicitly scoped to accuracy improvements within the current architecture — no new document types, no parser rewrite, no UI redesign. Confirmed several things were already correct and needed no change: Current Position screenshots are already validation-only and never spawn historical trades; the sibling/cross-document matching already avoids relying on exact price; statement rows deliberately fold commission into an effective price rather than leaving `fees` unset (not a bug — cost basis is already correct, and cross-document completion already backfills real `fees`/`taxes` from an invoice sibling when both are uploaded). The invoice's "Symbol Code" (ISIN-like) field was considered as a second corroborating signal but deliberately not touched — verifying it would require a hand-built ISIN↔ticker reference table with no verified source data, which is a real risk to get wrong for financial data.

**The one concrete gap found**: Thndr's Invoice document (a per-trade PDF receipt) prints a real, broker-assigned unique execution ID — "Transaction No." (e.g. `N000248458443`) — that was parsed out of the surrounding text and then silently discarded; nothing extracted it, stored it, or used it. Every duplicate/match decision in the app relied entirely on ticker+date+shares+price heuristics, which can both false-negative (a genuine re-read with a misread date/price looks like a new trade) and false-positive (two real, separate same-day trades of the same stock/share-count at a similar price look like duplicates of each other).

- **`ParsedTradeCandidate.transactionNumber`** (new, `domain/entities/Upload.ts`), extracted by `ThndrParser.parseInvoiceTextImpl` from the "Transaction No." row (matched as the first letter-prefixed alphanumeric token after the label, robust to how many header words OCR collapses/spaces between the label and the row).
- **Threaded onto the real ledger**: `Trade.transactionNumber` / `TradeAllocation.transactionNumber` (new, optional), set via `RecordBuyInput`/`RecordSellInput` — every allocation from one sell order gets the same value, same as `sellGroupId`. `ImportPage`/`SellAllocationForm` pass it through from the parsed candidate with no other UI change.
- **`duplicateDetection.ts`'s `sameExecution(a?, b?)`** (new): decisive when both sides carry a transaction number (`true`/`false`), `undefined` (inconclusive, fall back to the existing heuristic) when either lacks one. Wired into `findDuplicateBuyMatch`/`findDuplicateSellMatch` (an ID match short-circuits to "exact" regardless of date/price; an ID mismatch removes that row from consideration even when date/shares/price would otherwise look like a match) and into the sibling/cross-document checks (`suggestDuplicatePendingCandidateKeysToDelete`, `completeCandidateFieldsFromSiblings`, `findCrossSourceVerifiedKeys`) via a new `sameCandidateExecution` helper.
- **Cross-document backfill extended**: `completeCandidateFieldsFromSiblings` now also copies a donor's `transactionNumber` onto a same-execution sibling that lacks one (e.g. a statement row, which never prints an ID) — so once an invoice and its matching statement row are both in one import batch, the eventual committed Trade keeps the ID even on a future re-import where only the statement is re-uploaded.
- 21 new tests (2 `ThndrParser` extraction, 6 `duplicateDetection` buy/sell exact-ID-match and ID-mismatch-blocks-false-positive, 2 `completeCandidateFieldsFromSiblings` backfill, 2 sibling-duplicate false-positive-prevention, 4 `TradeService` persistence — plus supporting cases) — 547 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.
- **Remaining limitations**: only the Invoice document shape prints a transaction number today — the statement, Orders screens, and CSV export carry no per-row identifier at all, so this improvement's reach depends on how often a user has (or later uploads) the matching invoice. `CsvStatementParser` could recognize a "Transaction ID"/"Order ID" CSV column the same way if a real broker export with one is ever provided — not done here since no such sample text exists to verify a header-alias regex against.

### Post-audit fix — real per-stock Orders screenshots (RMDA) dropping every Buy row and one whole file

Direct user follow-up, working from real screenshots of the per-stock Orders screen for a ticker (RMDA — Rameda Pharmaceutical Company) the user had actually bought and partially sold: after uploading two screenshots (a scroll-overlap pair covering the same "All orders" list), Import showed only the 4 Sell rows and a "Missing buy history" banner claiming 4,585 shares short with zero buys anywhere — even though both screenshots visibly listed real Buy rows. Reproduced exactly against the user's own two PNGs (not synthetic text) by driving the real running app through Playwright and dumping the actual OCR'd `rawText` per upload, which pinpointed two independent, compounding bugs:

1. **A digit-shaped OCR bullet silently dropped every Buy row.** `orderActionPattern`/`rowActionPattern`'s bullet-gap (`[^\s\d]{0,2}`, between "Buy/Sell" and the share count) deliberately excludes digits — a documented, deliberate choice so a real digit could never be swallowed into the gap. But on this screenshot, Tesseract rendered every Sell row's bullet as "»" (matched fine) while rendering every Buy row's bullet as the digit **"0"** ("Buy 0 990 shares") — a real digit the gap correctly refused to consume, but with no alternative path, the whole match failed and the row vanished with no warning pointing at it specifically (only the generic "N Fulfilled but M extracted" count mismatch). Fixed by adding a second, narrow gap alternative: a single stray digit immediately followed by whitespace (`\d\s`) is now also accepted as a misread bullet — a real share count is never written as two space-separated digit groups in this document format, so an isolated single digit ahead of another number is unambiguously the bullet, not part of the quantity.
