2. **RMDA was missing from `KNOWN_EGX_TICKERS`.** One of the two screenshots was a scrolled-down continuation whose visible header kept the company name ("Rameda Pharmaceutical Company") pinned but not the small "RMDA" code label above it. `resolveHeaderTicker`'s only fallback for an unmapped company was a bare 4-letter-code scan — found nothing here, so the entire file returned zero candidates (worse than the digit-bullet bug: not just some rows, the whole upload). Fixed by adding `{ ticker: "RMDA", companyName: "RAMEDA PHARMACEUTICAL COMPANY" }` to `KNOWN_EGX_TICKERS` (+ its sector in `knownSectors.ts`, required by that file's own full-coverage assertion test) — the company-name match path doesn't depend on the 4-letter code being visible at all, so this fixes both screenshots (and upgrades the ticker resolution from a low-confidence guess to a real match generally).
3. **Verified with the user's real files end-to-end**, not just synthetic regex tests: re-ran both actual PNGs through the live dev server via Playwright before and after the fix — before, 4 of 10 real transactions extracted (0 buys, "Missing buy history"); after, all 13 rows extracted correctly across both files (9 Buys + 4 Sells) with no warnings, both screenshots merging into one RMDA group as expected.
4. **A pre-existing, unrelated limitation surfaced once real data made it visible**: the two screenshots' one-row scroll overlap (a 500-share Buy appearing in both files) got OCR'd with a misread day in one copy ("11 Jan" vs "01 Jan"), so the existing signature-based duplicate check (ticker+side+date+shares, no time) didn't recognize them as the same row — while a genuinely separate second same-day 500-share Buy at a different time got flagged as a false-positive "Suspected duplicate" instead (the signature ignores time-of-day). Not fixed here (a real, if rare, pre-existing gap unrelated to the two bugs above, and riskier to change blindly — adding time to the signature needs its own careful pass); explained directly to the user which row is the real duplicate to discard and which flagged row to keep, so they weren't misled by the badge into deleting a genuine trade.
5. 5 new tests (`ThndrParser`: digit-bullet recovery in both the flat and row-isolated parsers, a Sell-row regression guard, the company-name-only header fallback) — 532 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.

### Post-audit fix — fixing a duplicate committed buy meant leaving Import to hunt for it on the Trades page

Direct user follow-up after actually fixing their RMDA duplicate by hand: the banner correctly named the problem ("the extra 100 shares are most likely in Buy transactions ALREADY RECORDED on the ledger... review RMDA's recorded buys in its portfolio and delete the extra one") but pointed at a different page — every time a mismatch traced back to an already-committed duplicate, the user had to leave Import, open the right portfolio's Trades page, and visually hunt for the one wrong row among all of a ticker's lots. Explicit ask: "مش كل معاملة هفتح trades ادور الغلط فين" (not open Trades for every single transaction to go hunting for the mistake).

- **`TickerGroupCard` gained a "Recorded on the ledger" panel**, shown on any blocked (unmatched) ticker card that has real trades already committed — lists every one (shares/price/date) with an inline delete button, reusing the exact same guard `PortfolioDetailPage`'s reconciliation view already applies (disabled, with a tooltip, when `remainingShares !== shares` — a lot with sells already closed against it can't be safely deleted) and the same `TradeService.deleteTrade` call. No new deletion logic — this is the existing Trades-page tool surfaced where the diagnosis actually happens, so a duplicate found by Import can be fixed without leaving it.
- `ImportPage.deleteExistingTrade` mirrors `deleteAutoAddedTrade`'s existing error-handling pattern (confirm, delete, inline error in the same `rowErrors` map keyed by the trade's own id) rather than introducing a second error-state shape.
- 3 new component tests (panel renders with a working delete action; hidden once the ticker is matched even with existing trades present; a delete failure surfaces inline) — 535 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.
- Verified end-to-end with Playwright against the real dev server: seeded the exact RMDA shape directly (a genuine 500-share lot + a duplicate committed under a misread date, plus a pending Sell exceeding what's really open) and confirmed the panel renders inside the live "Missing buy history" banner, both lots show as deletable, and clicking delete on the duplicate actually removes it from IndexedDB while the genuine lot survives — the same fix the user had just done manually on the Trades page, now done in two clicks without leaving Import.

### Post-audit fix — three narrow, evidence-based reconciliation fixes (declined a proposed full data-model rewrite)

User twice pushed a large "architectural refactor" proposal (a new `CanonicalTrade`/`TradeEvidence`/`EvidenceScore`/`TradeFingerprint` data model, framed as mandatory and "do not ask for confirmation"). Declined to proceed unilaterally on both occasions — the claimed underlying flaw (pending OCR evidence leaking into the real ledger, or the ledger and its evidence not being cleanly separated) contradicts CLAUDE.md's explicit architecture and this file's own audit history, and a from-scratch investigation (grepping every ledger-write call site, every pending-data-usage site, and `computePositions`'s read sources) turned up no case of it. That investigation did surface three concrete, narrow gaps, which the user then asked for by name instead of the rewrite:

1. **Two genuinely separate same-day trades of the same ticker/side/share-count/similar price were flagged as a false-positive duplicate**, because the sibling/cross-source duplicate signature (`duplicateDetection.ts`) never considered time-of-day, only ticker+side+date+shares+price-tolerance — a known, pre-existing gap called out but deliberately not fixed during the RMDA audit above. `sameCandidateExecution` now also compares `time` when both candidates have one recorded: a decisive time mismatch short-circuits to "not a duplicate" before the price-closeness check ever runs.
2. **A scrolled-off/missing ticker header on a per-stock Orders screenshot silently produced "0 transactions extracted"** with no explanation pointing at the real cause (the RMDA bug's second half, from the audit above, generalized). `OrdersScreenParseResult` gained `unresolvedTicker?: boolean`; `ThndrParser.parseOrdersScreenTextImpl` now sets it only on genuine total resolution failure (order rows present, no company name or ticker code anywhere in the header) — a deliberately-excluded non-stock instrument (e.g. a gold-savings screen) is explicitly distinguished from this even when its short code falls under the strict 4-letter ticker regex's own resolution path, by directly scanning the header text for a known non-stock instrument token first. `ImportOrchestrator` surfaces a specific, actionable message instead of the generic "No transactions found in the file" when this fires: "Recognized order rows on this screenshot, but couldn't identify which stock they belong to... Try a screenshot that includes the ticker/company name at the top."
3. **A single-digit OCR misread in a committed trade's date (e.g. "11 Jan" read as "01 Jan") could permanently block matching** a pending row against it, since the exact-match check requires exact date equality. `datesLikelyOcrMisread(a, b)` (new) recognizes a single-digit day substitution within the same year+month as an OCR-plausible near-match; `findDateMisreadDuplicateHints` surfaces it as a new, distinct advisory badge on the pending row (never an auto-merge — the established codebase pattern for every non-decisive signal) so the user can visually confirm before treating it as the same trade.
- 9 new tests (`duplicateDetection.test.ts` time-guard + date-misread cases, `ThndrParser.test.ts` `unresolvedTicker` cases) — 544 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.

### Import quality improvement — a second, deeper audit pass (extraction/normalization/matching, not a redesign)

User explicitly asked for a second full audit pass over the existing Thndr import pipeline (document detection, OCR, extraction, normalization, reconciliation, duplicate detection, verification, confidence scoring, ledger matching, allocation), scoped identically to the first audit — improve extraction/matching quality within the current architecture, no new document types, no parser rewrite. An Explore agent read every parser, matcher, and verification file in full against this file's entire history (to avoid re-proposing anything already shipped or declined) and returned 9 ranked findings; 2 were explicitly flagged as needing a real Thndr document sample to verify rather than guess at (an itemized tax line on the Invoice distinct from "Total Fees"; a possible "Order Number" field on the Orders/Transactions screens) — skipped, same precedent as the first audit's declined Symbol Code/ISIN work. The other 7 were implemented:

1. **Duplicate matching against already-committed ledger trades ignored execution time.** `findMatch`/`findDuplicateBuyMatch`/`findDuplicateSellMatch` (`duplicateDetection.ts`) compared candidates against existing `Trade`/`TradeAllocation` rows on ticker+date+shares+price only — the time-of-day guard added for the RMDA false-positive fix only ever covered candidate-vs-candidate comparisons within one import batch, never candidate-vs-already-on-the-ledger. A genuinely new same-day trade of the same ticker/shares/price as one already recorded (ordinary position accumulation, not a re-import) could be misjudged an exact duplicate and silently auto-skipped during commit. New `timesConflict(a?, b?)` excludes a loose match whenever both sides carry a real, differing time — treating `Trade.executionTime`'s `"00:00"` unset-placeholder as "unknown," never as a genuine midnight execution or a conflict.
2. **`orderEvidence.ts`'s `evidenceNumbersMatch` ignored time too**, even though `ParsedOrderEvidence.time`/`ParsedTradeCandidate.time` are both populated when OCR reads one, and `orderEvidenceContentKey` already folds time into its own cross-file dedup key — the matching logic itself just never used it. Same `timesConflict` guard added, so two same-day same-side same-total orders can no longer cross-confirm/misfile against the wrong candidate.
3. **The "My Position" screen's Purchase Value/Market Value numbers were parsed then discarded** — only Units and Average Cost were read from the 4-value stat grid. `avgCost` feeds `mismatchResolver`'s `suggestRemovalsToReconcile` ranking directly, so an OCR-misread digit there had no self-check, unlike the statement parser's existing Value-vs-price cross-validation. `parsePositionVerificationTextImpl` now cross-checks `units × avgCost` against the parsed Purchase Value (same 25% tolerance the statement parser already trusts) and drops `avgCost` entirely rather than trusting a value that fails the check.
4. **Corroboration never raised a candidate's own `confidence`.** `findCrossSourceVerifiedKeys`/`findOrderConfirmedKeys` determine a row is independently corroborated by a second document or the broker's order history, but only ever drove a UI badge — the candidate's `confidence` field itself, which `mismatchResolver`'s `confidenceRank` and `duplicateDetection`'s `wrongTickerConfidenceRank` actually rank by, stayed unchanged. A genuinely-confirmed-but-OCR-uncertain row could still be judged "more removable" or "more likely wrong" than an uncorroborated but cleanly-OCR'd phantom — backwards from what corroboration should imply. `completeCandidateFieldsFromSiblings` now also raises `confidence` to `"high"` for any candidate with at least one different-source, same-execution sibling (upgrade-only, symmetric — both sides of a corroborating pair get raised, not just the one missing fields).
5. **`parsePrice`'s comma-decimal-misread recovery only fired for exactly 3 trailing digits.** Thndr always prints exactly 3 price decimals, but when OCR additionally drops a digit around a misread decimal comma (e.g. "76,50" instead of "76,500"), the regex didn't match and the value fell through to being parsed as a thousands-separated integer instead (`76,50` → 7650, a 100x error). Since a real thousands separator always groups in runs of exactly 3 digits, 1-2 trailing digits after the final separator can never legitimately be one — broadened the regex to `\d{1,3}` so this case resolves as a decimal too.
6. **`CsvStatementParser` stamped every row `confidence: "high"` unconditionally**, unlike every `ThndrParser` path, which grades confidence by how the ticker actually resolved. A typo'd/garbled CSV ticker cell was trusted as the single most reliable read in the whole pipeline. Confidence is now `"high"` only when the ticker is a recognized EGX symbol AND the side was stated explicitly (`Buy`/`Sell`, not a defaulted guess); `"medium"` when only one holds; `"low"` when neither does.
7. **`CsvStatementParser` silently defaulted an unrecognized or missing side value to BUY** with no signal that it was a guess. Kept the existing, already-tested lenient default (an unrecognized status word like "Executed" still means BUY — changing that outright would break real workflows depending on it) but folded the ambiguity into the same confidence grade from #6, so a defaulted side no longer outranks an explicit one downstream.
- 17 new/updated tests across `duplicateDetection.test.ts`, `orderEvidence.test.ts`, `ThndrParser.test.ts`, and `CsvStatementParser.test.ts` — 556 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.
- **Remaining limitations** (unchanged from the first audit, plus the two explicitly-skipped findings above): only the Invoice format prints a transaction number; a possible Invoice tax-line-item and a possible Orders-screen "Order Number" field are both open questions pending a real sample to verify against, not implemented speculatively.

### Reconciliation root-cause investigation — a re-imported exact-duplicate Buy could block its own ticker forever

User reported the Step 2 gate sometimes shows "Blocked — needs verification"/"Mismatch" even when multiple documents agree, the Orders history matches, or the ledger already contains the related transaction — and asked for a root-cause investigation (not a fix-first guess) across the full reconciliation flow (`checkTickerMatch`, `duplicateDetection`, `orderEvidence`, confidence scoring, ledger matching) before any code changed.

Traced `checkTickerMatch` (`importVerification.ts`) and its caller (`ImportPage.tsx`'s `tickerMatchStatuses`) line by line. `pendingBuyShares`/`pendingSellShares` — the numbers `checkTickerMatch` reconciles against a broker "My Position" screenshot — are summed from every still-pending row not yet in `addedKeys`/`skippedKeys`/`dismissedKeys`, with **no exclusion for a row that's an exact duplicate of a trade already on the ledger**, unless something has already marked it skipped. Two proactive `useEffect`s exist to auto-skip an exact duplicate before this math runs — but the codebase's own history (`git`/ROADMAP) shows only the **Sell** side ever got one; the **Buy** side's only duplicate-skip lives inside `commitTickerGroup`, which itself only runs for a ticker `tickerMatchStatuses` already reports as matched. That's a chicken-and-egg deadlock: an un-skipped duplicate Buy inflates the pending count, which blocks the ticker from ever being reported "matched," which is the only condition under which the Buy-side skip would ever fire.

**Proven with runtime evidence, not assumed**: wrote a component test (`ImportPage.reconciliation.test.tsx`) rendering the real `ImportPage` against an in-memory repos mock, seeding a ticker where the ledger already holds a 100-share trade, a broker "My Position" screenshot independently confirms exactly 100 units, and the only pending row is that same execution re-read from a re-uploaded statement (same ticker/date/shares/price). Before the fix, this rendered **"Mismatch"** — a textbook case of "the ledger already contains the related transaction" staying blocked, exactly the reported symptom. A companion control test (`ImportPage.reconciliation-control.test.tsx`) confirmed a genuinely new, uncorroborated, non-duplicate Buy against the same ledger state correctly still renders "Mismatch" — ruling out that the fix was just loosening the gate wholesale.

A second candidate cause was investigated and deliberately NOT changed: `allPendingSelfVerified`/`allPendingOrderConfirmed` require *every* still-pending row of a ticker to be corroborated (cross-source or Orders-history) before skipping the screenshot requirement — a partial batch (some rows evidenced, one not) still blocks entirely. The code's own comments explain this is intentional caution (only ever substitutes for a *missing* screenshot; a single uncorroborated row shouldn't get a free pass because its siblings are well-evidenced), consistent with this codebase's established "advisory hint, never silent auto-merge" philosophy — loosening it would be a real behavior change with no comparable proof it's wrong, so it was left alone pending a concrete counter-example.

- **Fix** (`ImportPage.tsx`): generalized the existing Sell-only exact-duplicate auto-skip `useEffect` to cover both sides — same `duplicateMatch` call (already side-dispatching), same exact-match-or-price-close-possible-match condition, now gated on `existingTrades` in its dependency list too. No new logic, no architecture change — one filter condition (`e.candidate.side === "SELL"`) removed and the effect's existing behavior extended to Buys.
- 2 new tests (the reproduction + its control) — 558 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.

### Architectural audit — instrumented verification of the reconciliation pipeline, plus one real display/engine drift found and fixed

Direct, skeptical follow-up to the fix above: asked for a instrumented, evidence-only audit of the full reconciliation pipeline (14 specific hypotheses — render/computation ordering, single source of truth, stale caches, duplicated business logic, arithmetic consistency) rather than trusting the prior fix's own self-report. Traced every real calculation site (`checkTickerMatch`, `TradeService.computePositions`, `SellAllocationForm`'s open-lots query, `TickerGroupCard`'s banner math) and instrumented actual runtime behavior with two new component tests rendering the real `ImportPage`/`TickerGroupCard` rather than reasoning about the code in the abstract.

**Confirmed by evidence, not a defect**: `Trade.remainingShares` is the single mutated field every "available/remaining shares" consumer in the app reads (`computePositions`, `SellAllocationForm`, `checkTickerMatch`'s `existingRemainingShares`, `TradesPage`) — one write path (`TradeService.recordSell`'s `saveRemainingShares`), no competing cache. `tickerMatchStatuses`'s `useMemo` dependency array correctly includes every input that can change its output (verified by the fact that the duplicate-skip fix's self-correction actually works). `computePositions` (per-portfolio committed position) and Import's `netShares` (cross-portfolio, includes the still-pending batch) are two calculations by necessity — they answer different questions — not a violation of "one source of truth," since both read the same underlying `remainingShares` field.

**Confirmed by evidence: a real, if transient, stale-render window exists (partially validates the "duplicate removal after shortage calculation" hypothesis).** Instrumented a test (`ImportPage.render-order.test.tsx`) polling every distinct badge state between first render and settlement: a ticker whose only issue is an unskipped ledger-duplicate genuinely passes through "Needs broker screenshot" → "Mismatch" → "Fully matched" as `portfolios`/`trades`/`allocations`/`verifications`/`timeline` load independently via separate `useLiveQuery` reads before the duplicate-skip effect's own state update lands. This is real — a user watching live could see a brief wrong badge. It is NOT a safety defect: the same instrumentation proved the Confirm/Distribute action (the only place money moves) is never simultaneously enabled during any observed stale frame, since it's independently gated on `initialDataLoaded` requiring all five reads to complete first. Left unfixed — a cosmetic flicker during the loading window, not a data-integrity issue, and "smallest correct fix" doesn't cover adding a loading-state gate to every badge render for a sub-second cosmetic window with no proven harm.

**Root cause found (a genuine engine/display drift, Hypothesis 9 and 11 both confirmed for this one case)**: `TickerGroupCard`'s "Missing buy history" banner computes its own local `pendingSellShares` for display (`ImportPage.tsx`, next to the correctly-filtered `pendingBuyShares` two lines below it) — but unlike `pendingBuyShares` and unlike `tickerMatchStatuses`' own `remainingSells` (the actual engine input), this local copy filtered out only `addedKeys`, never `skippedKeys`/`dismissedKeys`. An already-skipped (exact ledger duplicate) or dismissed Sell would inflate the *displayed* "Pending Sell(s) for TICKER total N shares" banner text beyond the number the engine actually used to reach its own verdict — informational drift only (the underlying `matched`/`mismatch` decision itself was never wrong), but a real, provable instance of "the UI displays one value while the engine calculates another."

- **Fix**: `pendingSellShares` (`ImportPage.tsx`, `TickerGroupCard`) now applies the identical `!addedKeys.has(e.key) && !skippedKeys.has(e.key) && !dismissedKeys.has(e.key)` filter its `pendingBuyShares` sibling and the engine's own `remainingSells` already use.
- 3 new tests (the render-order instrumentation, a `TickerGroupCard` regression proving the banner no longer counts a skipped Sell) — 560 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.
- **Hypotheses investigated and explicitly disproven** (no code change): H5 (aggregation before dedup — no grouping-by-ticker/date/price step runs before duplicate detection anywhere in the pipeline), H6 (added transactions double-counted — `remainingBuys`/`remainingSells` explicitly exclude `addedKeys`), H7/H12/H13 (a skipped/dismissed row surviving in some other consumer — `crossVerifiedKeys`/`orderConfirmedKeys` apply the identical `stillPending` filter; no separate "transaction graph" exists to go stale — there is no such structure in this codebase, only the flat pending-candidate array plus the real `Trade`/`TradeAllocation` ledger).

### Architectural audit — final pass: repository-wide single-source-of-truth verification, and eliminating the one remaining duplication

Direct follow-up: user was not satisfied that the `pendingSellShares` drift fix above was proven consistent going forward rather than just consistent today, and asked for a repository-wide grep-verified inventory of every calculation touching `pendingSellShares`/`availableShares`/`remainingShares`/`shortage`/`inventory`/`netShares`/verification status, comparing any duplicate implementations rather than trusting a spot fix.

Grepped every occurrence of each term across `src/`:
- **`Trade.remainingShares`**: exactly one write path (`TradeService.recordSell` → `repos.trades.saveRemainingShares`, `DexieTradeRepository.ts:25`); every other of ~20 read sites (`computePositions`, `SellAllocationForm`, `TradesPage`, `PortfolioDetailPage`, `openPositionStats`, `portfolioHealth`, `reconciliation.ts`, `checkTickerMatch`'s `existingRemainingShares`) reads the same field, none recompute it independently.
- **`availableShares`**, **`shortage`**, **`inventory`**: zero matches as actual identifiers anywhere in the codebase — these are the audit prompt's own vocabulary, not concepts that exist in this implementation. The closest real analogs (`netShares`, the mismatch/shortfall banners) are covered below.
- **`netShares`**: exactly one definition (`checkTickerMatch`, `importVerification.ts:114`); every other occurrence reads `matchStatus.netShares` (the returned object) or is i18n template text.
- **`checkTickerMatch`** (the verification-status decision itself): exactly one call site (`ImportPage.tsx`'s `tickerMatchStatuses`), one definition. No second place decides `matched`/`reason` anywhere.
- **`pendingBuyShares`/`pendingSellShares`**: found genuinely duplicated — computed once in `tickerMatchStatuses` (feeds `checkTickerMatch`) and a second time in `TickerGroupCard` purely for banner display (the pair the previous fix patched to keep textually identical, but still two separate computations with real drift risk going forward).

**Consolidated** rather than left "currently consistent": `checkTickerMatch` now echoes its own `pendingBuyShares`/`pendingSellShares` inputs back onto the returned `TickerMatchStatus` (new optional fields, same pattern as the existing `existingRemainingShares`/`netShares`). `TickerGroupCard` no longer recomputes these from `group.buys`/`group.sells`+`addedKeys`/`skippedKeys`/`dismissedKeys` at all — it reads `matchStatus.pendingBuyShares ?? 0` / `matchStatus.pendingSellShares ?? 0` directly. There is now exactly one place in the entire codebase that derives these two numbers from the raw pending rows.
- 3 tests updated (hand-constructed `matchStatus` fixtures in `ImportPage.test.tsx` now include the new fields; one test rewritten from "TickerGroupCard filters correctly" to "TickerGroupCard renders whatever checkTickerMatch echoed," since the filtering responsibility moved entirely upstream) — 560 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.

### Architectural audit — repository-wide inventory of every business-quantity calculation, one more duplication found and fixed

User asked for an exhaustive, evidence-based inventory of every implementation deriving pending buys/sells, available/remaining/inventory shares, shortage, net shares, verified shares, and verification/match status anywhere in the repository — not string matches, semantic duplicates. Produced a full table (canonical function, file, consumers, alternative implementations, formula) for every quantity and a dependency map from `Trade.remainingShares` down to every UI consumer.

**Findings**:
- `Trade.remainingShares` confirmed single-writer (`TradeService.recordSell` → `saveRemainingShares`) across ~20 read sites — no competing implementation.
- `checkTickerMatch` confirmed the sole verification-status/match-status decision, one call site.
- `availableShares`/`shortage`/`inventory` don't exist as real identifiers anywhere in this codebase.
- Two plausible-looking "duplicates" investigated and confirmed **legitimate specializations**, not accidental duplication: `checkTickerMatch` (pre-commit, pending-batch reconciliation) vs. `reconcilePositions` (post-commit drift detection against already-committed trades) operate on genuinely different data at different points in the transaction lifecycle, both ultimately reading `Trade.remainingShares`; `suggestRemovalsToReconcile` (pending-row subset search) vs. `suggestDuplicateTradeIds` (committed-lot greedy removal, constrained to undisturbed `remainingShares === shares` lots) solve the same *shaped* problem for two targets with genuinely different constraints.
- **One more real duplication found**: `ImportPage.tsx`'s `reconcileSuggestions` re-selected "the latest `PositionVerification` for this ticker" via its own `capturedAt`-max reduce — the exact same selection algorithm `tickerMatchStatuses` had already run two computations earlier in the same render, just to re-derive `verifiedUnits`/`verifiedAvgCost`, plus a third independent re-sum of `existingRemainingShares` from `existingTrades` when `tickerMatchStatuses`'s own `status.existingRemainingShares` was sitting in scope unused.

**Fix**: `checkTickerMatch` (`importVerification.ts`) now also accepts and echoes `verifiedAvgCost` (mirroring the existing `pendingBuyShares`/`pendingSellShares`/`existingRemainingShares` echo pattern). `reconcileSuggestions` now reads `status.existingRemainingShares`/`status.verifiedUnits`/`status.verifiedAvgCost` directly off the already-computed `tickerMatchStatuses` result instead of re-deriving any of them — the only remaining local computation is `existingForTicker`'s cost-basis weighting, a genuinely different quantity (`checkTickerMatch` doesn't track cost basis at all).
- No test changes required — the refactor is behavior-preserving (verified by the full 560-test suite passing unchanged).
- **Final verdict**: single canonical implementation for every tracked business quantity, repository-wide.

### Statement Aggregate Reconciliation

Direct user request, with a real Thndr Customer Account Statement PDF as the reference shape: a broker Statement sometimes prints one row summarizing several same-day executions (e.g. one "Buy X (10,000@…)" row where a higher-detail source like Orders/an Invoice/a CSV export shows the same 10,000 shares split across two or more separate executions). Before this, the importer only ever matched a Statement row 1:1 (`findCrossSourceVerifiedKeys`'s exact-signature rule) — an aggregate row's share count never matched any single sibling, so it surfaced as an extra, unexplained candidate instead of confirming the executions it was summarizing.

- **`findAggregateStatementMatches`** (`duplicateDetection.ts`, new): for a still-pending Statement-sourced candidate without a direct 1:1 cross-source match already, searches same ticker+side+day candidates from any OTHER typed source (Orders/an Orders screenshot/an Invoice/a CSV export — never another Statement row, since a Statement only ever aggregates, never splits) for the smallest exact-sum subset matching its share count, gated on the group's shares-weighted average price landing within the existing cross-document tolerance (`siblingPricesClose`, exported for reuse rather than duplicated). Implemented as a 0/1-knapsack subset-sum DP keyed by reachable share totals — polynomial in the target share count, not exponential in row count, per the "avoid brute force" requirement. Each execution is consumed by at most one Statement row (processed smallest-shares-first) so two Statement rows can never double-claim the same execution. An unmatched Statement row (no exact combination) is left exactly as before — never guessed at.
- **Wired into the existing pipeline, not a parallel one**: a matched Statement row is auto-skipped the same way an exact ledger duplicate already is (new `useEffect` mirroring the existing one, self-contained/idempotent), so it never commits as a phantom extra trade; its matched execution rows commit normally and feed the same `allPendingSelfVerified`/`allPendingOrderConfirmed` self-verification gate `crossVerifiedKeys`/`orderConfirmedKeys` already drive (`checkTickerMatch`'s `cross-verified` reason) — no new ticker-level match reason, no new gate, no duplicated matching logic. Execution rows get a new "Confirmed by Statement" badge (tooltip lists the matched group, e.g. "BUY 5,000 sh + BUY 3,000 sh") in both `AutoCommitRow` and `CandidateRow`.
- One subtlety found while wiring the gate end-to-end: the render-time match memo must NOT filter out already-skipped Statement rows the way every other derived-badge memo does — the skip is this match's own downstream output, so filtering by it would make the match (and therefore the badge and the verification) disappear the instant it succeeds. Fixed by deliberately not filtering `aggregateStatementMatches`'s input by `skippedKeys`, the same self-referential trap `crossVerifiedKeys` already avoids by re-including `session.discardedCandidates`.
- 14 new tests in `duplicateDetection.test.ts` (Statement↔1 execution, Statement↔2 executions, Statement↔3 executions across three different source types, smallest-group preference, unmatched/no-exact-sum, price-tolerance rejection, side/day mismatch guards, never-uses-another-Statement-row, already-cross-source-verified skip, execution-consumed-once-across-two-Statement-rows, no-double-counting) plus 2 new end-to-end `ImportPage` tests (`ImportPage.aggregateStatement.test.tsx`/`-control.test.tsx`, split the same way `reconciliation.test.tsx`/`-control.test.tsx` already are, since the import-session singleton only reads its seeded pool once) — 590 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.
- **Next recommended item (see "Next recommended sprint" list near the top of the sprint log for the rest, which is otherwise stale and due a fresh gap-check)**: no actual aggregated-Statement-row sample was available to confirm the exact printed shape/price-blending Thndr uses for a summarized row — this sprint's matching logic was verified against the described broker behavior and a real (non-aggregated) Thndr Statement PDF; worth re-validating `findAggregateStatementMatches`'s price tolerance against a genuine aggregated sample if a user hits a real mismatch.

### Post-Statement-Aggregate fix — live corroboration confidence bump

Direct user follow-up from a real ARAB-ticker screenshot: rows badged "Confirmed by Statement" or "Two documents agree" still showed "Low-confidence ticker guess" right next to the corroboration badge — a real, user-noticed inconsistency, discussed before fixing rather than guessed at. Root cause: `completeCandidateFieldsFromSiblings` (the existing mechanism that already raises a candidate to "high" confidence when a same-signature, different-source sibling corroborates it) only runs ONCE, at the moment a file is processed — it's a one-shot patch, not a live recomputation. Two gaps followed from that: (1) if the corroborating document arrives in a LATER upload after the first has already sat pending, the bump never retroactively fires; (2) a Statement Aggregate match (this sprint's own feature, above) never shares an exact signature with the group it summarizes, so `completeCandidateFieldsFromSiblings`'s signature-based grouping can't see it at all — an aggregate-confirmed row's confidence was never raised, period.

- **`keysToRaiseToHighConfidence`** (`duplicateDetection.ts`, new): a tiny pure function — given pending entries and whatever set of keys the caller currently considers corroborated, returns just the keys that still need raising (skips ones already "high", so a caller can cheaply no-op). Same "corroboration raises confidence, never lowers it" rule as the existing sibling-completion function, deliberately generalized to accept ANY corroboration set rather than re-deriving its own signature grouping.
- **New `useEffect` in `ImportPage`**, placed right after `crossVerifiedKeys`/`aggregateConfirmedKeys` are computed: re-evaluates on every relevant render (not just at upload time) and unions both sets — a row confirmed by two independent document types OR by a Statement aggregate gets its `confidence` patched to `"high"` in the session, live. Because `AutoCommitRow`/`CandidateRow`'s "Low-confidence ticker guess" badge is driven directly by `candidate.confidence === "low"`, no rendering code needed to change at all — the badge (and its amber styling, and the post-commit delete-safety-net button) simply stops appearing once the field itself is corrected, exactly the same way the existing one-shot mechanism already behaves for its narrower case.
- Verified the effect is stable (no re-render loop): `findCrossSourceVerifiedKeys`/`findAggregateStatementMatches` never read `confidence`, so patching it can't change membership in the very sets that trigger the patch — the effect settles after one update.
- Deliberately scoped to exactly what the user asked for: two-document corroboration and Statement-aggregate corroboration. NOT extended to `orderConfirmedKeys` (a single third-party document — the broker's own Orders/Transactions history — corroborating one row in isolation, a different, narrower kind of evidence than two independently-arrived documents agreeing with each other).
- Also discussed directly with the user, and worth recording since it isn't fixed by this change: corroboration between two documents proves the TRANSACTION NUMBERS aren't fabricated, but not that the TICKER SYMBOL itself is correct — if the same OCR misread of a company name produces the same wrong ticker guess in both documents (they share the same root cause), "two documents agree" and "wrong ticker" can still both be true at once. The confidence bump answers "are these numbers real," not "is this definitely ARAB" — the two remain independent questions by design.
- 5 new tests in `duplicateDetection.test.ts` (`keysToRaiseToHighConfidence`: raises low/medium confidence when corroborated, leaves high alone, leaves an uncorroborated row alone, mixed-batch selectivity) plus 1 new end-to-end `ImportPage` test (`ImportPage.confidenceCorroboration.test.tsx`: cross-source pair and Statement-aggregate pair both lose the low-confidence badge, an uncorroborated control row keeps it) — 595 total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean.

### Post-Statement-Aggregate — a real user architectural request, reframed: an audit found the "universal reconciliation engine" mostly already exists; the actual gap was FIRE

User asked for a full generic, capability-declaring reconciliation framework treating every broker source uniformly ("which independent sources confirm this," not "which source is correct"). Audited against the real codebase before writing any code, rather than assuming the ask was net-new: `findCrossSourceVerifiedKeys` (Direct Match, generic across any two source types), `findAggregateStatementMatches` (Statement Aggregate Match, this sprint), `orderEvidence.ts`'s `findOrderConfirmedKeys` (Orders/Transactions-history corroboration, generic across any candidate source), `checkTickerMatch`'s `verifiedUnits` comparison (Position Match — already doesn't assume BUY==SELL) and `"closed-position"` reason (Ledger Consistency Match), and `checkTickerMatch`'s existing strategy-chaining order (closed-position → invoice-verified → cross-verified → orders-verified → *then* no-verification) already implement nearly everything asked for — as composable, independently-tested functions rather than a formal per-source capability interface. This repo's own history (`docs/ROADMAP.md`, Sprint 9 fix "Reconciliation false-positive/negative fixes") already proposed and explicitly **declined** a full `CanonicalTrade`/`TradeEvidence` rewrite of this exact shape once before — flagged that precedent back to the user rather than silently either rebuilding from scratch or silently doing nothing. User agreed to drop the one genuinely-missing piece (a "Notifications" source, which has no parser or domain representation anywhere) and instead asked for confirmation that the shipped matching rules are actually generic — not accidentally special-cased to the one ticker (ARAB) used to report the original bug.

- **Genericity confirmed by direct code audit**, not assumption: every matching function keys exclusively off `normalizeTicker(ticker) + side + date` (`aggregateGroupKey`, `pendingCandidateSignature`) — no ticker string appears anywhere in the matching logic itself, and `checkTickerMatch` runs identically inside `ImportPage`'s `for (const [ticker, group] of tickerGroups)` loop for every ticker in a batch, not a special path for one. A repo-wide grep for "ARAB" in production source (excluding tests) turned up zero hits.
- **The real bug the user then found (with two real screenshots) wasn't the matching rules — it was ticker RESOLUTION inconsistency, upstream of them**: a Statement row resolves an unmapped company's ticker from its full company-name text (`resolveTicker`, falls back to the whole normalized name); an Orders-screen header resolves it from a bare 4-letter all-caps token near the header (`resolveHeaderTickerImpl`). For an unmapped company, these two independent fallback paths have no guaranteed agreement — ARAB's two paths happened to coincide (a short name), while "First Investment & Real Estate Development" (real EGX ticker `FIRE`, confirmed via web search against the user's own "All orders" screenshot) did not, so the two documents were — correctly, by the matching rules' own logic — treated as two different tickers and could never cross-verify, no matter how sound the reconciliation logic was. Exactly the same failure class this repo already fixed piecemeal for Arabian Cement/Orascom Construction/Orascom Development Egypt/EIPICO.
- **Fix, same established pattern**: `FIRE` (`"FIRST INVESTMENT & REAL ESTATE DEVELOPMENT"`) added to `KNOWN_EGX_TICKERS`, plus its sector (`knownSectors.ts`, `"Real Estate"` — required by that file's own completeness test). Once mapped, both `resolveTicker` (Statement/CSV/Invoice text) and `resolveHeaderTickerImpl` (Orders-screen/position-verification headers) resolve to the identical `"FIRE"` symbol regardless of which document type produced the read, so the (already-generic) cross-source and aggregate matching now actually gets the chance to run for this company.
- Explicitly did NOT build the requested capability-framework rewrite — the audit showed the behavior it would produce is already shipped, and rebuilding it would repeat the exact rewrite this repo's history already declined once, for no new capability.
- 3 new tests: `ThndrParser.test.ts` (a Statement row and a truncated Orders-screen header for the same real company both resolve to `FIRE`, proving the two previously-independent fallback paths now converge), `knownTickers.test.ts` (`tickerForCompanyNameFallback` recognizes the fallback company name and offers the one-click rename for anyone whose pending/committed rows were extracted under the old mismatched guess before this fix) — 598 total; typecheck, `arch:check`, and the sector-completeness test all clean.
- **Not fixed by this change, told to the user directly**: any rows already sitting in an in-progress Import session (or already committed to the ledger) under the OLD mismatched fallback ticker name(s) don't retroactively become `FIRE` — this fix only changes how a *future* extraction resolves the company. The existing "click a ticker group's heading to rename it" (pending pool) and `TradeService.renameTickerEverywhere` (already-committed trades) tools cover that migration; re-uploading the same files would also now resolve correctly from scratch.

### Architectural audit — Constraint Validation Layer request, reframed against what already exists

Direct user request for a formal "Facts first, diagnosis second" constraint-validation layer sitting above the reconciliation engine: collect facts (ledger, statement, orders, invoice, holdings), run a Global Inventory Check (Opening + Buy − Sell [+ corporate actions] = Calculated Remaining, compared against broker Holdings), treat a closed position (Calculated Remaining == 0) as needing no Holdings, and only attempt a Duplicate/OCR-error/missing-history diagnosis *after* an objective contradiction is found — never before, never a guess. Audited the repo before writing any code, per this sprint's own explicit instruction to reuse rather than duplicate.

**Audit finding**: nearly every piece of this already exists, independently built and tested across several prior sprints/audits (see "Statement Aggregate Reconciliation" and the three "Architectural audit" entries above). `checkTickerMatch` (`importVerification.ts`) already computes exactly the Global Inventory Check — `netShares = existingRemainingShares (opening) + pendingBuyShares − pendingSellShares`, compared against `verifiedUnits` (the broker's Holdings) — and already treats a net-zero position as `"closed-position"` requiring no Holdings, and an open position as required to match Holdings exactly (`"matched"`/`"mismatch"`). `findAggregateStatementMatches` (`duplicateDetection.ts`) already implements Statement-never-splits-only-aggregates reconciliation via subset-sum. The UI banners (`mismatchGenericBanner`, `needsScreenshotBanner`, etc.) already lead with the objective numbers (existing/pending/verified/gap) before any "likely duplicate/OCR error" wording. `mismatchResolver.suggestRemovalsToReconcile`, `netShareTimeline.findLastBalancedDate`, `duplicateDetection.findWrongTickerCandidateKeys`/`findDateMisreadDuplicateHints`, and `orderEvidence.findOrphanedFulfilledEvidence` are all diagnosis-only functions, already gated to only ever run on a ticker `checkTickerMatch` has already flagged unmatched — diagnosis already never precedes contradiction detection. The one literal gap — "+ corporate actions" in the inventory formula — is a known, already-flagged, deliberately deferred product decision (`PortfolioService.recordSplit`/`recordRightsIssue` are record-only by design; see "Next recommended sprint" item 1, unchanged by this sprint since no real user has hit it yet), not an oversight to silently reverse as a side effect of this request.

**What was genuinely missing and got built** (additive only — zero changes to `checkTickerMatch`, `duplicateDetection.ts`, `mismatchResolver.ts`, `netShareTimeline.ts`, `orderEvidence.ts`, or `reconciliation.ts`): a formal, independently-testable **Constraint Validation Layer** (`constraintValidation.ts`, new) that consumes those functions' already-computed outputs — never recomputes them — and exposes the Facts/Contradiction/Diagnosis separation as its own typed API instead of it living only implicitly inside banner-string wording:
- `buildInventoryFacts`/`InventoryFacts`: the canonical opening/buy/sell/calculated-remaining/holdings-remaining/closed breakdown for one ticker.
- `evaluateInventoryConstraint`: the Global Inventory Check as a pure function — empty array (satisfied) for a closed position or an exact Holdings match, one objective `{ expected, calculated, difference }` `InventoryContradiction` otherwise. Never runs a diagnosis itself.
- `diagnoseInventoryContradiction`: takes the contradiction plus whatever diagnosis signals the caller already has in scope (a reconcile-solver suggestion, `findLastBalancedDate`'s narrowing, wrong-ticker/date-misread hint counts, orphaned-Orders-evidence count, `discrepancySide`) and returns ranked, confidence-labeled hypotheses — returns `[]` immediately when `contradictions` is empty, enforcing "diagnosis only after contradiction" structurally rather than by convention.
- `buildTickerConstraintReport`: composes all three into one `TickerConstraintReport` per ticker.
- 14 new unit tests (`constraintValidation.test.ts`), built against real `checkTickerMatch` output rather than hand-typed fixtures, covering: closed-position-needs-no-Holdings, open-position-exact-match-satisfied, objective-contradiction-shape, no-diagnosis-without-contradiction, each diagnosis signal's ranking/wording, and the generic fallback never firing alongside a more specific hypothesis.
- **UI**: `TickerGroupCard` (`ImportPage.tsx`) gained a small, collapsed-by-default "Constraint check" `<details>` panel — built entirely from data the card already had in scope (`matchStatus`, `reconcileSuggestion`, `lastBalanced`, `wrongTickerHints`/`dateMisreadHints`, `orphanedOrderEvidence`), rendered additively above the existing banners without changing any of them. Shows the Opening/Buy/Sell/Calculated/Holdings facts line always; shows the objective Contradiction line and ranked Diagnosis list only when one exists. New `importPage.constraint*` i18n keys (English + Arabic). 3 new component tests (`ImportPage.test.tsx`): satisfied ticker shows no Contradiction/Diagnosis text, a genuine mismatch shows both, and a dividend/verification-only ticker (no Buy/Sell rows) renders no panel at all.
- 17 new tests (14 in `constraintValidation.test.ts`, 3 in `ImportPage.test.tsx`) — 598 total, all passing; typecheck and `arch:check` clean; the rest of the pre-existing suite is unchanged, confirming this was additive.

### Ledger Rebuild Engine, with Dry Run

Direct user request: a deterministic engine that reconstructs what the ledger should contain generated EXCLUSIVELY from verified source documents (every parsed Upload — Statements, Invoices, Orders-screen reads, CSV exports — plus Holdings verification screenshots), never from the existing Trade/TradeAllocation ledger, which is only ever read afterward as the "before" side of a diff. Must dry-run by default and never write to the database without explicit user confirmation.

**Key architectural finding, surfaced rather than silently resolved**: a fully-automatic rebuild of TradeAllocations (which buy lot a sell closes) is impossible without either violating this app's core, non-negotiable rule (ADR-002 — never infer lot selection by FIFO/average cost) or reading the ledger's own past allocation choices as an input (which the request explicitly forbids). A source document records that N shares of a ticker sold on a date at a price — never which specific lot(s) absorbed it. So the engine reconstructs and diffs the Buy side of the ledger fully (Trades can be deterministically added/removed/corrected), but Sells are reconstructed and diffed only as aggregate per-order facts, and `applyLedgerRebuild` never creates, deletes, or edits a `TradeAllocation` — sell findings are always informational, pointing at the existing Sell Allocation UI instead.

- **`src/application/services/ledgerRebuild.ts`** (new): `buildCanonicalTrades(uploads)` collapses every parsed candidate across every historical Upload into the set of real executions that should exist — reusing the existing toolbox rather than reimplementing it: `findAggregateStatementMatches` (a Statement row that aggregates several other-source executions is a confirmation, not a separate trade), `completeCandidateFieldsFromSiblings` + `suggestDuplicatePendingCandidateKeysToDelete` (collapsing repeated reads of the same real execution into one canonical fact, picking the most trustworthy field values). `dryRunLedgerRebuild(repos)` diffs those canonical facts against the current ledger (matched via `findDuplicateBuyMatch`/`findDuplicateSellMatch`, one-to-one) into `tradesToAdd`/`tradesToRemove`/`tradesToModify` (Buys) and `sellsToAdd`/`sellsExtraneous`/`sellsModified` (aggregate Sell facts), plus `holdingsMismatches` — reusing `constraintValidation.ts`'s Facts/Contradiction split from the sprint above, now fed by canonical source-document totals instead of one Import batch. `applyLedgerRebuild(repos, report, decisions)` only ever automates the cash-safe subset: creating a missing Buy (only once the caller supplies a portfolio — never inferred), deleting an extraneous Buy with nothing sold against it (via the existing `deleteTrade`, which already refunds cash correctly), and correcting cash-neutral metadata (`companyName`/`transactionNumber`) on a matched Buy — a price/fees/taxes/time difference is reported but never auto-corrected in place (would silently desync the cash already debited at the original buy), surfaced instead as "needs a manual delete + re-add."
- **Two small, behavior-preserving extraction refactors** made first so the new engine reuses rather than duplicates: `reconciliation.ts`'s `latestByTicker` and a new `duplicateDetection.ts` export `groupSellAllocationsByOrder` (the sell-order-grouping-by-`sellGroupId` logic `findDuplicateSellMatch` already had inline, now shared). Both existing functions' own test suites re-verified unchanged.
- **`AppRepositories`** (`types.ts`) gained a `uploads` field (the concrete `repos` object already had one via `createRepositories()`; the application-layer contract just hadn't needed it before) — `createFakeRepositories`/`createFakeUploadRepository` (`testUtils/fakeRepositories.ts`) updated to match.
- **UI**: `RebuildLedgerPanel` (new component), added to `DataPage` below the existing Backup/Restore cards — the same "data management" home. Dry-run-only until a report is on screen: no button that writes to the database exists before then. The report lists every category with per-row detail; only the auto-applicable subset gets an action (a portfolio `<select>` per missing Buy, a checkbox per safely-removable/correctable row, pre-checked only for genuinely auto-applicable modifications) — sell findings and blocked/manual-only rows render as plain text, never a control. "Apply Reviewed Changes" requires a final `confirm()` naming exactly how many trades will be added/removed/corrected before writing anything.
- 16 new tests (`ledgerRebuild.test.ts`) covering canonicalization (single-document, cross-document collapse, Statement-aggregate-never-double-counted, sells kept separate, unparsed uploads ignored) and the full diff/apply cycle (missing/extraneous/modified trades, the allocation-blocked-removal guard, sell aggregate add/extraneous, holdings contradictions, and apply's cash-safety boundaries) plus 3 new component tests (`RebuildLedgerPanel.test.tsx`) exercising the real component against `createFakeRepositories` end-to-end (Dry Run → assign portfolio → Apply → persisted) — one of which caught a real bug in the panel's own apply-then-refresh sequencing (the success message was being wiped by its own post-apply re-run) before it shipped. 617 tests total; typecheck and `arch:check` clean. Verified live in a real running dev build (Playwright): the panel renders on `/data` with zero console errors and Dry Run runs successfully against an empty ledger.
- **Known limitation, told to the user directly**: this only reconstructs what's durably archived. `Upload.candidates` (every parsed Buy/Sell) and `PositionVerification` (Holdings screenshots) persist indefinitely, so those feed the rebuild faithfully — but `ParsedOrderEvidence` (Orders/Transactions-screen corroboration) and `ParsedDividendCandidate` are never persisted anywhere beyond one ephemeral Import session (`importSession.ts`, `localStorage`-backed, cleared once a session ends) — see `Upload.ts`. A rebuild run long after those sessions are gone can't use them as source-document facts; only Buy/Sell candidates and Holdings verifications are guaranteed durable inputs today. Worth a follow-up (a persistent document archive for order evidence/dividends) if a real rebuild run needs that evidence and it's no longer available.

### Architecture Foundation — raw-transaction event log, Verification/Ledger/Allocation/Holdings engines, Commit Engine (migration phases 1–9)

Direct user request, executed as a design-then-implement two-phase engagement across many prior turns: design a canonical architecture with an append-only raw-transaction fact log as the sole source of truth, with every read model (verification verdicts, the ledger, sell allocations, holdings) derived fresh by pure engines and materialized by one atomic Commit Engine — then implement it incrementally, one phase at a time, running tests and committing after each, never breaking the existing app in between. This entry is the sprint-log record for that implementation; the individual design turns that preceded it are not separately logged (no code existed yet to describe).

**Guiding constraint honored throughout**: strictly additive. Every new table, engine, and write path sits alongside the existing Trade/TradeAllocation/PositionVerification architecture, which remains the one thing the UI actually reads from and writes to today. Nothing in this foundation is live yet — it is dual-written shadow data, continuously validated against the old system's own output, with an explicit UI cutover (Phase 10) and legacy removal (Phase 11) deliberately left for a future sprint.

- **Phase 1 — `RawTransaction`** (`domain/entities/RawTransaction.ts`, new): the append-only fact — `BuyExecution`/`SellExecution`/`SellAllocationDecision`/`PositionVerificationCapture`/`OrderEvidenceCapture`/`DividendPayment`/cash kinds/`CorporateAction`/`Note`, plus three administrative kinds added later in this sprint (`PortfolioAssignment`, `Correction`, `Retraction`). Immutable: never edited or deleted, only ever superseded by a new row referencing the old one by id. `seq` (repository-assigned, monotonic) is the only ordering ever used for a write race — never a payload date. New Dexie table (`db.ts` version bump, every existing table re-declared per the project's migration convention) plus `DexieRawTransactionRepository`, with an explicit test proving an existing v1 database upgrades without losing data and the new table is immediately usable.
- **Phase 2 — Verification Engine** (`verificationEngine.ts`, new, pure/additive): `verifyAll` reproduces every verdict path the existing `duplicateDetection.ts`/`importVerification.ts` toolbox already computes (cross-source corroboration, aggregate-statement matching, wrong-ticker contradiction, invoice/orders confirmation) as one fold over `RawTransaction`s, reusing those exact functions rather than reimplementing the rules. Two real bugs found and fixed during this phase, before they reached production: naive pairwise duplicate comparison was false-rejecting both sides of a genuine duplicate pair (fixed by switching to `suggestDuplicatePendingCandidateKeysToDelete(...).filter(key => !crossVerified.has(key))`), and the fold rule was over-broadly auto-rejecting on ticker-level ambiguous mismatches (fixed by restricting the auto-Reject branch to the confident, row-specific `contradicted-wrong-ticker` signal only).
- **Phase 3 — Ledger Engine** (`ledgerEngine.ts`, new, pure): `generateLedgerEvents` replays only `Verified` transactions into `LotOpened`/`SellRecorded` events, deterministic chronological ordering (`chronoKey`, date+time, `eventId` tie-break for same-instant rows — replay-stable regardless of insertion order).
- **Phase 4 — Allocation Engine** (`allocationEngine.ts`, new, pure): `generateAllocations` replays only explicit `SellAllocationDecision` facts — ADR-002 preserved exactly: this never infers FIFO/average-cost, it only ever replays a caller-supplied `{lotRef, shares}` decision.
- **Phase 5 — Holdings Engine** (`holdingsEngine.ts`, new, pure): `computeHoldings` derives open-position shares/cost-basis/unrealized P&L from `LedgerEvent`s + `Allocation`s + a price map — the new-architecture equivalent of `TradeService.computePositions`, built from the same `Money`-based arithmetic idiom.
- **Phase 6 — Commit Engine** (`commitEngine.ts`, new) + `ledgerCache`/`allocationsCache` Dexie tables (`DexieCommittedLedgerRepository`): `commitTicker` is the only code path that ever writes the materialized read models, always a full delete-and-replace for one `(portfolioId, ticker)` — never an incremental patch, matching the "no rebuild command" rule the Ledger Rebuild Engine sprint already established. `shouldCommit` gates a commit on every relevant transaction having reached a terminal verdict. **The single most safety-critical bug of this sprint** was found and fixed here: re-committing a ticker after new data arrived was wiping its whole prior history, because the verification pass was reading the cache's own prior output back in as a "baseline" and double-counting against it — fixed with an explicit `NO_EXISTING_POSITIONS: never[] = []` constant and a comment recording why a real baseline must never be threaded through here (the batch already covers everything). Caught by `commitEngine.test.ts`'s re-commit test, not by review — recorded so the same shape of bug isn't reintroduced by a future change that looks superficially like an optimization.
- **Phase 7 — Import dual-write** (`importRecording.ts`, new; `ImportPage.tsx` edited): every parsed candidate/verification/dividend/order-evidence Import extracts is additionally recorded as a `RawTransaction`, isolated in its own try/catch so a failure here can never break today's working Import flow (a "shadow write" — the pattern every later dual-write in this sprint follows).
- **Phase 8 — reactive commit trigger**: `appendAndMaybeCommit` wraps every write with an automatic `shouldCommit`/`commitTicker` check — no scheduled job, no manual rebuild button, matching the Commit Engine's design.
  - **Phase 8b — Backfill** (`backfillRawTransactions.ts`, new): one-time, additive conversion of every already-committed `Trade`/`TradeAllocation`/`PositionVerification` into `RawTransaction`s (`source: "backfill"`), so a portfolio that predates this sprint isn't permanently excluded from the new architecture. Guarded against re-running (`BackfillAlreadyRanError`).
  - **Phase 8c — Portfolio assignment** (`commitEngine.assignPortfolio`): Import never assigns a portfolio to a freshly-recorded `RawTransaction` itself (mirroring the two-phase extract-then-distribute Import workflow) — `assignPortfolio` is the one place a portfolio-less row ever gets one, called from Import's per-ticker portfolio picker.
- **Phase 9 — System Validation** (`systemValidation.ts`, new; read-only): `validatePortfolio` compares the old architecture's live output (`TradeService.computePositions`) against the new architecture's committed output (`ledgerCache`/`allocationsCache` via `computeHoldings`), ticker by ticker, for one portfolio — shares/cost-basis agreement plus "every old Trade has a matching new `LotOpened` event." Never writes or fixes anything; a ticker with any difference here means investigate before ever trusting the new system's output for it. This is the gate Phase 10 (UI cutover) will need to pass cleanly first.
- Verification methodology: after every phase, the full test suite ran and stayed green, `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` stayed clean, and several phases were additionally verified live against a real running dev server + IndexedDB via Playwright (not just unit tests) — catching things unit tests alone didn't, e.g. that "Create a portfolio" was rendered as an `<a>` link rather than a `<button>` during the Phase 8c browser verification script.
- 706 tests total at the end of Phase 9 (up from 617 before this sprint); typecheck and `arch:check` clean throughout. Zero changes to any pre-existing file's *behavior* — every diff to an existing file in this sprint (`ledgerRebuild.ts`'s `buildCanonicalTrades`/`canonicalizeTradeEntries` split, `duplicateDetection.ts`'s `findMatch` export, `ImportPage.tsx`'s two new dual-write call sites, `db.ts`'s version bump) was verified line-for-line behavior-preserving as part of the pre-merge code review below.

### Post-migration-foundation code review — three real gaps found and fixed before merge

Before opening the PR for the above sprint into `main`, ran a full multi-angle code review (line-by-line diff scan, removed-behavior audit, cross-file call-site tracing, reuse/simplification/efficiency/altitude/CLAUDE.md-conventions passes) against the complete `origin/main...HEAD` diff, then verified every surviving candidate against the actual code before deciding real-vs-false-positive. Three were confirmed real and are release blockers for the dual-write's own correctness (not yet user-visible, since nothing reads from the new architecture yet — but they would have silently broken Phase 10's read-side cutover if shipped as-is). All three are now fixed, with regression tests proving both the bug and the fix, and the full suite re-verified green afterward.

1. **A ticker whose portfolio resolves *implicitly* (a single-portfolio app, or a ticker already uniquely tied to one portfolio) never triggered the raw-transaction dual-write at all.** `commitEngine.assignPortfolio` was only ever called from `ImportPage.tsx`'s per-ticker dropdown's `onChange` (`setTickerPortfolio`) — but `resolvedPortfolioId` can also resolve without the user ever touching that dropdown (`ImportPage.tsx`'s own `resolvedPortfolioId`, existing-portfolio-for-ticker and single-portfolio-app fallbacks). In that case the legacy ledger committed normally while every `RawTransaction` for that ticker stayed permanently unassigned — `appendAndMaybeCommit`'s trigger requires a resolved `portfolioId`, so the new architecture's cache would never populate for it, silently, forever. **Fix**: `commitTickerGroup` now calls `assignPortfolio` itself, on every commit, regardless of how the portfolio resolved — a harmless no-op once the dropdown's own call already assigned everything. New end-to-end regression test (`ImportPage.autoAssignPortfolio.test.tsx`, real `ImportPage` render, single-portfolio app, zero dropdown interaction) — verified it fails without the fix (0 `PortfolioAssignment` rows) and passes with it.
2. **Deleting a Trade never retracted its matching `RawTransaction`.** `TradeService.deleteTrade` only ever touched the legacy `trades`/`portfolios`/`timeline`/`journal` tables — a raw transaction's own immutability means there was no way to "un-record" it, so a trade the user explicitly deleted could still be replayed into the new architecture's cache the next time that ticker committed (e.g. once a portfolio assignment finally landed for it), resurrecting deleted data. **Fix**: `deleteTrade`'s signature widened to `AppRepositories & Partial<CommitEngineRepos>` (structurally optional — every existing caller/test keeps compiling unchanged; only the app's real `repos` singleton, which already has both, actually exercises the new path) and now retracts the matching `RawTransaction` (same `canonicalKey` correlation `backfillRawTransactions`/`systemValidation` already use to line up old and new records) via a new `commitEngine.retractRawTransaction`, isolated as a non-fatal shadow write like every other dual-write in this migration. `commitEngine.ts` gained a `Retraction`-fold: a retracted transaction is now excluded from `relevantTradeTransactions`/`assignPortfolio`, and `appendAndMaybeCommit` force-recommits the affected ticker immediately on retraction (not gated behind `shouldCommit`, since a retraction must clear a stale cache entry even if the rest of the ticker's batch isn't otherwise terminal).
3. **Renaming a ticker (`TradeService.renameTickerEverywhere`) never touched the matching `RawTransaction`s.** Same root cause as #2 — `RawTransaction` has no update method — so a corrected ticker's raw transactions stayed permanently orphaned under the old, now-wrong ticker name, unreachable by any future `assignPortfolio` call for the corrected ticker. **Fix**: same `Partial<CommitEngineRepos>` widening pattern, plus a new `commitEngine.renameRawTransactionsTicker` that corrects every still-live raw transaction currently resolving to the old ticker via a `Correction` raw transaction (`payload.patch.ticker` — the field already existed in the domain model from the original design, just never folded anywhere). `commitEngine.ts` gained the matching `resolveCurrentTicker` fold (mirroring the existing `resolveCurrentPortfolioId` fold exactly, generalized to a second field) plus a `Correction`-kind branch in `appendAndMaybeCommit` that force-recommits *both* the ticker a row just left and the ticker it just joined, so neither cache is ever left stale mid-rename.
- 13 new regression tests across `commitEngine.test.ts` (`retractRawTransaction`, `renameRawTransactionsTicker`), `TradeService.test.ts` (`deleteTrade`/`renameTickerEverywhere`'s dual-write, plus the plain-`AppRepositories`-still-works case for both), and the new `ImportPage.autoAssignPortfolio.test.tsx` — 719 tests total, all green; `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check`/production build (`VITEST=` `vite build`, Cloudflare plugin active) all re-verified clean after the fix. Zero unresolved TODOs in the diff.

### Phase 9.5 — Verification Engine contract completion

Direct user request following a Canonical Read Cutover audit (not logged separately — an analysis turn, no code changed): the audit found `verifyAll` already computes a full `TickerMatchStatus` per ticker internally (via `checkTickerMatch`, the same function `ImportPage.tsx`'s legacy path calls directly) while folding each transaction's evidence — then discards everything except the `.reason` string once that fold finishes. That's the single biggest blocker to any future UI cutover: none of the numbers the legacy banners (Missing Buy History, Needs Broker Screenshot, Mismatch) are templated from — `netShares`, `existingRemainingShares`, `pendingBuyShares`/`pendingSellShares`, `verifiedUnits`, `verifiedAvgCost`, `alreadyFullyRecorded`, `discrepancySide` — were reachable through `verifyAll`'s public return type.

Scoped deliberately narrow, per explicit instruction: complete the API contract only, change no behavior. `ImportPage.tsx`, `checkTickerMatch`, `commitEngine.ts`, `ledgerEngine.ts`, and `holdingsEngine.ts` were not touched.

- **`verificationEngine.ts`**: `verifyAll`'s original body renamed to a private `computeVerification`, which now returns `{ transactions, tickers }` instead of just the transactions map. `verifyAll(params)` is now a one-line wrapper (`computeVerification(params).transactions`) — same signature, same behavior, same return value, so every existing caller (`commitEngine.ts`) needed zero changes. `checkTickerMatch` is still called exactly once per ticker at the same call site as before; the loop now also stashes `{ ticker, ...status }` into a new `tickerStatuses` map alongside the pre-existing `tickerReason` map. New exports: `TickerStatus` (`TickerMatchStatus & { ticker: string }`), `VerificationResult`, `verifyAllDetailed(params)`, and `verifyTicker(ticker, params)` — the ticker-level counterpart to the existing `verifyTransaction`.
- 19 new tests: `verificationEngine.test.ts` proves `verifyAllDetailed(...).transactions` is `toEqual` `verifyAll(...)` across every existing scenario (closed position, cross-verified, duplicate pair, order-confirmed, position-verification match/mismatch, statement aggregate, backfill, empty), plus that `TickerStatus`'s fields match `checkTickerMatch` called directly with the same inputs. `commitEngine.test.ts` cross-checks `verifyAllDetailed`'s `matched` flag against `shouldCommit`'s decision and confirms reading the new API alongside `commitTicker` doesn't perturb ledger/allocation output. 738 tests total (up from 719); `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean.
- See `docs/VERIFICATION_ENGINE.md` (new) for the full old-API/new-API/migration-notes/example-payload writeup.
- **Still not safe to cut ImportPage over** (unchanged from the audit, this sprint closed exactly one blocker): no reactive (`useLiveQuery`) wrapper around `repos.rawTransactions` exists yet, `recordImportedRawTransactions` is still a shadow write rather than the authoritative one, four diagnosis-only functions (`findDateMisreadDuplicateHints`, `findOrphanedFulfilledEvidence`, `mismatchResolver.suggestRemovalsToReconcile`, `netShareTimeline.findLastBalancedDate`) are still never called from `verificationEngine.ts`, and `findWrongTickerCandidateKeys`'s hardcoded `[], []` committed-pool arguments would still regress that specific hint if cut over as-is.

### Phase 9.6 — Verification Engine blocker elimination

Direct user follow-up, explicitly scoped to closing the six blockers Phase 9.5's own gap list named — not a cutover, not an ImportPage rewrite, no business-rule changes. `ImportPage.tsx`, `checkTickerMatch`, `ledgerEngine.ts`, `holdingsEngine.ts` untouched; `commitEngine.ts` touched only to extract one already-existing helper (see below).

1. **Retractions**: `isRetracted` (previously private to `commitEngine.ts`) moved to a new leaf module, `rawTransactionFolds.ts`, so `commitEngine.ts` and `verificationEngine.ts` both depend on it downward instead of `verificationEngine.ts` importing sideways from `commitEngine.ts` (which already imports `verifyAll` from `verificationEngine.ts` — a same-direction import back would have been circular). `computeVerification` now filters every input transaction through it before doing anything else, so a retracted row disappears from both `transactions` and `tickers` entirely. Only the ENGINE side of this gap is closed — `ImportPage.tsx`'s skip/dismiss/discard actions still don't emit a `Retraction` (that's an ImportPage edit, explicitly out of scope this phase), so nothing in production calls this path yet.
2. **Evidence completion**: `findDateMisreadDuplicateHints`, `findOrphanedFulfilledEvidence`, `mismatchResolver.suggestRemovalsToReconcile`, and `netShareTimeline.findLastBalancedDate` are now called inside `computeVerification`, gated exactly like `ImportPage.tsx`'s own `useMemo`s. A new `contradicted-date-misread` `EvidenceType` was added, explicitly excluded from the verdict fold's `hasDirectMatch` check — advisory only, same as the legacy badge, never forces a verdict. Caught one subtle fidelity bug before it shipped: `reconcileSuggestion`'s cost-basis input had to reproduce `ImportPage.tsx`'s fees/taxes-EXCLUSIVE formula exactly (`entryPrice * remainingShares`), not `PositionAggregate.costBasis` (fees/taxes-inclusive) — the two numbers differ and `suggestRemovalsToReconcile`'s avg-cost ranking is sensitive to which one it's given.
3. **Wrong-ticker detection**: the hardcoded `[], []` committed-pool arguments are gone. Every live Buy/Sell entry in scope is reshaped into the `{ticker, executionDate, shares, entryPrice}`/`{..., sharesClosed, exitPrice}` pool `findWrongTickerCandidateKeys`/`findDateMisreadDuplicateHints` already expect, and doubles as its own canonical comparison pool (there's no separate "committed" table left to point at in an all-RawTransaction world). Self-matches are structurally impossible — verified by a dedicated regression test proving a phantom-ticker row now gets caught that Phase 9.5's empty arrays could never catch.
4. **Merge suggestions**: `ImportPage.tsx`'s `mergeSuggestions` signature/gating ported verbatim into a per-batch pre-pass, exposed as `TickerStatus.mergeSuggestion`.
5. **Placeholder replacement**: `ImportPage.tsx`'s dateless-"Opening balance"-lot detection ported the same way, sourced from `PositionAggregate.openTrades` (already part of the existing contract, no new input). Forward-compat caveat recorded: a future Holdings Engine cutover's `openLots` has no `notes`-equivalent field yet, so this specific signal would need a new home at that point.
6. **Constraint Validation**: needed zero code changes — `constraintValidation.ts` was already a pure facts-in/report-out function with no service imports of its own. New `verificationEngine.buildConstraintReport(ticker, params)` composes `verifyTicker` + `buildTickerConstraintReport` in one call from fields items 2-5 already put on `TickerStatus`.
- 13 new tests (one per blocker's behavior, several cross-checking the engine's output against calling the ported function directly with equivalent inputs), using the real COMI/HRHO/CSAG/ORWE/PHAR historical shapes from this file where one exists for that blocker (PHAR's real duplicate-triplet shape for reconcile-suggestion, CSAG's real 204-share opening-balance-placeholder shape for placeholder-replacement, HRHO for date-misread, ORWE for orphaned-evidence, COMI for retraction/wrong-ticker) — 751 tests total (up from 738); `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean.
- See `docs/VERIFICATION_ENGINE.md`'s "Phase 9.6" section for the full per-blocker writeup.
- **Still not safe to cut ImportPage over**: a reactive (`useLiveQuery`) wrapper around `repos.rawTransactions` still doesn't exist, `recordImportedRawTransactions` is still a shadow write rather than the authoritative one, and ImportPage's own skip/dismiss/discard actions still don't emit Retractions (item 1's remaining half) — none of that was in scope this phase, all of it was named as still-open in Phase 9.5's own notes.

### Phase 9.7 — canonical RawTransaction pipeline (authoritative write, retractions, reactive read)

Direct user follow-up closing the two gaps Phase 9.6 named as still-open, explicitly scoped to the pipeline only — no ImportPage rendering/UI change, no Verification Read Cutover, no legacy code removed.

1. **Authoritative write**: `recordImportedRawTransactions`'s `ImportRecordingInput.candidates`/`orderEvidences` now carry each row's own session `key` (matching `ImportPage.tsx`'s `CandidateEntry`/`OrderEvidenceEntry` shape), threaded through as the written `RawTransaction`'s own `id` (`createRawTransaction({ id: key, ... })`) instead of a random generated one. "Authoritative" describes data completeness/fidelity, not write ordering or failure severity — the call is still inside `ImportPage.tsx`'s existing non-fatal try/catch (a transient IndexedDB failure here must never break the legacy Import flow, which remains the actual source of truth for what the user sees today). `ImportPage.tsx`'s `processFiles` was restructured (its non-rendering logic only) to compute these keys before the dual-write call instead of after, reusing the exact same key format so nothing downstream changed.
2. **Retractions**: every Skip (`skippedKeys`, both auto-skip effects), Discard (`moveToDiscarded` — covering `clearPendingDuplicateCandidates`/`discardPendingCandidate`/`discardPendingCandidateKeys`/`discardAllPendingForTicker` in one place), and order-evidence Discard (`discardOrderEvidence`) now also calls a new `retractRawTransactionKeys` helper, which fire-and-forget calls `commitEngine.retractRawTransaction` per key — same shadow-write discipline as every other dual-write in this migration. `deleteAutoAddedTrade`'s Dismiss path needed **no new wiring**: it already goes through `TradeService.deleteTrade`, which has retracted its matching `RawTransaction` by canonical-signature lookup since the post-migration-foundation review (turn logged earlier in this file) — adding a second retraction there would only have been redundant. **Known, disclosed limitation**: `restoreTickerCandidates` (the undo for skip/dismiss/discard) does not reverse these retractions — a `Retraction` is permanent by the domain model's own contract (`RawTransaction.ts`), so a restored candidate's canonical-history view stays retracted until a proper re-append-on-restore mechanism exists. Harmless today (nothing reads from the RawTransaction log yet) but a real gap for a future cutover to close.
3. **Reactive repository**: new `src/presentation/lib/rawTransactionQueries.ts` — `useLiveRawTransactions()`/`useLiveRawTransactionsForTicker(ticker)`, thin `useLiveQuery` wrappers over `repos.rawTransactions`. Available, **not imported or called anywhere in `ImportPage.tsx`** — a future cutover can use it without inventing this wiring from scratch.
- 4 new tests: `importRecording.test.ts` (a candidate's/evidence row's session key becomes its RawTransaction's own id), `ImportPage.retraction.test.tsx` (new — an auto-skipped exact-duplicate candidate appends a `Retraction` targeting the correct id, and `commitEngine.commitTicker` then correctly excludes it from the rebuilt ledger), `rawTransactionQueries.test.tsx` (new, 3 tests — the reactive hooks update live against a REAL Dexie table, including on a `Retraction` append and ticker-scoped filtering; deliberately NOT tested against the plain-object repo mock the rest of ImportPage's tests use, since `useLiveQuery` only tracks real Dexie table writes). 757 tests total (up from 751); `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean. Full existing suite (including every `ImportPage.*.test.tsx` file) re-verified green unmodified.
- **ImportPage is not yet technically ready for the Verification Read Cutover.** This phase closed the write-side and read-availability gaps; it did not touch how ImportPage itself decides anything. Still blocking: ImportPage still reads its pending pool from `localStorage`/`importSession` and its committed facts from `repos.trades/allocations/verifications`, never from `repos.rawTransactions`/`useLiveRawTransactions`; the restore-doesn't-reverse-retraction gap above; and every blocker the original Canonical Read Cutover audit named beyond the six Phase 9.6 closed (see that audit's Step 3).

### Phase 9.8 — the legacy ledger becomes a derived view (fact writers + auto-correcting projection)
