Direct user directive after a forensic audit proved the legacy Trade/TradeAllocation tables reuse previous state forever (`remainingShares` incrementally decremented, never recomputed; no bulk clear anywhere; a wrong allocation permanent): make the ledger automatically become MORE CORRECT whenever historical documents become more complete — no manual cleanup, no trade deletion, no database reset. No new architecture; strictly a completion of the existing one.

1. **Missing fact writers completed** (`TradeService.ts`): `recordBuy` now writes its Buy's `BuyExecution` fact (`ensureBuyFact` — canonical-key-guarded so an Import-written fact is never duplicated; fact id = the Trade's own id for exact correlation; carries the new optional `notes`/`strategyTags`/`sector` payload fields added to `RawTransaction.ts`), and `recordSell` writes both the `SellExecution` fact AND the `SellAllocationDecision` fact (`ensureSellFacts`) — the immutable record of WHICH lots the user chose (ADR-002), previously written by nothing but the one-time backfill. `sellExecutionId`/`lotRef` use canonical keys, exactly the eventIds `generateLedgerEvents` derives, per `backfillRawTransactions`' established convention. Both writers are non-fatal, opt-in per repos bundle (the same `Partial<CommitEngineRepos>` widening `deleteTrade` already used).
2. **Legacy projection** (`ledgerProjection.ts`, new): `commitTicker` (commitEngine.ts) now — when the repos bundle carries the legacy tables, which the app's real singleton always does — projects its freshly rebuilt events/allocations onto Trade/TradeAllocation per (portfolioId, ticker): id-stable (a lot whose canonicalKey matches an existing trade UPDATES it in place, preserving id/notes/strategyTags/journal/timeline links), full replace otherwise (new lots create rows + Buy timeline events; vanished lots delete rows + their journal/timeline entries, mirroring `deleteTrade`'s cleanup), and `remainingShares` always recomputed from the replayed allocations — never carried forward. **Never touches `portfolio.cash`** (re-applying cash for corrected history would double-count everything the legacy flow already applied; cash stays the user's explicitly-editable figure).
3. **Gap-backfill** (`ensureLegacyFactsExist`, same module): runs before every projection — any legacy row predating its fact writer gets a backfill fact appended first (idempotent via canonical keys), so projection can never mistake a legitimate old row for stale data. Keyed on EVER-existed (not just live) facts, so an explicitly retracted execution (a deleted trade, a discarded candidate) is never resurrected by re-facting — verified by a dedicated regression test.
4. **Two safety rules found by the tests, not by design**: (a) projection only runs on a TERMINAL verdict set — `commitTicker` is force-called on Retraction/Correction even mid-review, and a merely-Needs-Review fact must never read as "stale, delete it"; (b) `deleteTrade` now retracts EVERY live matching fact (batched, one recommit), because with projection active a lingering duplicate fact would re-create the deleted trade as a fresh lot.
5. **Commit-gate fix**: `shouldCommit`/`commitTicker` passed only Buy/Sell facts to `verifyAll`, so `PositionVerificationCapture`/`OrderEvidenceCapture` corroboration never participated in the commit decision — a broker screenshot could never terminal-ize a ticker in the new architecture. Both now pass the full relevant set (verdicts still only cover Buy/Sell rows).
- 9 new tests (`ledgerProjection.test.ts`) covering the two headline flows (a missing historical Buy discovered later materializes as a real Trade row; a duplicate Buy auto-removes once its read is discarded — with the deliberately-conservative intermediate state asserted too: a suspected duplicate's shares keep blocking until the user's one evidence-level discard, never auto-deleted), manual-allocation survival, gap-backfill preservation + non-resurrection, the non-terminal guard, cash neutrality, idempotent re-commits, and the sell-fact canonical references actually replaying. Plus updated `TradeService.test.ts` dual-write tests (retract-all semantics; the 2-Correction rename). 775 tests total (up from 766); `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; zero presentation-layer files touched.
- **Known limitations, stated**: projection doesn't manage Sell/PartialSell timeline events for changed allocations (cosmetic staleness possible); `moveTrade`/`correctTradeExecutionDate`/`consolidateTicker` still don't correct their facts (the Phase 10 mutator-audit list — a date correction currently leaves the ticker safely BLOCKED at Needs Review rather than corrupted, since old-key and new-key facts can't both verify); partially allocating an imported Sell candidate creates disagreeing sell facts, which likewise block terminally rather than corrupt.

### Evidence-First Architecture Review + real bug fix (the SKPC closed-position trap)

User requested a full architectural review of the OCR→Ledger pipeline against an "Evidence-first" target (documents as source of truth, Ledger/Portfolio as pure projections, minimal-document gap recovery). Initial read of the codebase found most of the target already built (RawTransaction as the append-only fact log, `commitEngine`/`ledgerEngine`/`allocationEngine` as regenerate-from-scratch projections, `completenessEngine`'s closed-position rule) — but the user pushed back and demanded proof by tracing one real ticker (SKPC) through the actual execution path, not a description of intended architecture.

**The trace, executed against the real code (not read-and-summarized), found a real, live bug**, not just an architectural gap: `checkTickerMatch` (`importVerification.ts`) auto-matched a closed position (Buy shares == Sell shares, net zero) as `matched: true` on bare share-count arithmetic alone, with **zero independent corroboration** — no My Position, no Invoice, no Statement. This is exactly the JUFO/SKPC case `completenessEngine.ts`'s own comments already named as the reason its closed-position rule exists — except `completenessEngine` was never actually consulted by the commit gate. Running the real `ThndrParser` → `recordImportedRawTransactions` → `checkTickerMatch`/`verifyAll` → `commitEngine.commitTicker` chain against SKPC's real Orders screenshot proved it live: both the legacy gate and `verifyAll` said "Verified"/"matched", while the resulting ledger (4 `LotOpened` events, 1 `SellRecorded`, **zero allocations** — the Sell was never allocated to any lot) was actually an 82-share OPEN position, contradicting the "closed" verdict that had just certified it safe to commit.

Second correction, found only by reading the actual call graph: the "two divergent verification engines" claimed in the first review pass were wrong — `verifyAll` calls the same `checkTickerMatch` `ImportPage.tsx` calls directly. The real duplication was narrower: a `VERIFIED_REASONS` string set in `verificationEngine.ts` re-derived the same trustworthiness judgment `checkTickerMatch`'s own `matched` boolean already made, and had drifted out of sync with it (the bug above lived in the gap between the two).

Fixed, with the user's explicit design for what should replace the blind auto-match (search the Evidence Repository first, determine exactly which evidence is missing, recommend only the smallest additional document, never My Position for a closed ticker since it can't prove historical executions, manual confirmation only as an absolute last resort):

1. **`checkTickerMatch`** (`importVerification.ts`): the closed-position branch no longer returns `matched: true` unconditionally — it now requires the same independent corroboration (invoice-sourced / cross-verified / orders-verified) already required for a non-zero net position. An uncorroborated closed position now returns `matched: false, reason: "closed-position"` (the reason string is unchanged; only the auto-trust is removed).
2. **`verificationEngine.ts`**: the redundant `VERIFIED_REASONS` string set removed — `tickerVerified` and the per-transaction `matched-position`/`contradicted-position-mismatch` evidence now read `reason.matched` directly, the one canonical signal, eliminating the exact duplication that let the bug diverge.
3. **`completenessEngine.ts`**: `EvidenceDocumentType` extended with `"Transactions"` and `"My Position"`; `recoveryPlan()` now recommends My Position for an open, uncorroborated ticker (`reason: "no-verification"`), never for a closed one; prefers `"Transactions"` over `"Orders History"` for a bounded gap on an open ticker (a dated ask beats an undated one), keeping `"Orders History"` for a real `"mismatch"` (a broker count already exists; the question is which row is wrong, not whether anything happened). Documented known simplification: still no "was this document type ever uploaded for this ticker, even if it didn't cover the gap" signal — needs the Evidence Repository itself to answer that (see item 3 below).
4. **`ImportPage.tsx`**: `TickerGroupCard` now computes a real `TickerCompletenessReport` (via `assessTickerCompleteness`, fed from the card's own already-computed `matchStatus`/`orphanedOrderEvidence`/`lastBalanced` — no second implementation) and renders a new `RecoveryPlanPanel` naming the exact next document and why, instead of a bare "needs a screenshot" message. `MatchBadge`'s closed-position branch now shows an amber "Closed — needs corroborating evidence" state instead of the green "Sold out" badge when unmatched.
5. **Evidence Repository durability** (separately identified, real gap): `Upload.fileBlob` (new, optional) persists the original document's bytes permanently in Dexie/IndexedDB, alongside the extracted `rawText` — previously only the OCR'd text and a hash survived, so a future extraction-logic fix had nothing to re-run against. `ImportOrchestrator.importFile` now returns the original `File`/`Blob` (image and PDF uploads only — CSV's bytes already equal `rawText`); `ImportPage` threads it into the `Upload` record it saves. No Dexie schema version bump needed (Blob is a structured-cloneable IndexedDB value; only index changes require bumping `db.ts`'s `version()`).
- 13 tests updated to replace the old "bare closed position auto-verifies" fixtures with a real corroborating fact (invoice-sourced, or a broker My Position capture) — each one a legitimate test-intent fix (cache-replace/rename/retraction/assignment mechanics), not a weakened assertion; the closed-position-without-corroboration case now has its own dedicated regression test at every layer (`checkTickerMatch`, `verifyAll`, `shouldCommit`). 8 new tests added (3 `ImportPage` recovery-plan/badge tests, 2 `DexieUploadRepository` blob round-trip tests, plus the corrected-behavior tests themselves). 783 tests total (up from 775); `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean.
- **Deliberately NOT done, and why**: the Verification Read Cutover (Phase 10/11 above — pointing live screens at `ledgerCache`/`computeHoldings` instead of `Trade`/`TradeAllocation`/`computePositions`, and making `Portfolio.cash` a derived projection instead of an imperatively-mutated field) was assessed as part of this same review and explicitly not attempted, even though instructed to complete the full migration autonomously. This isn't scope-timidity — it's the same gate this roadmap's own Phase 10/11 entry already named ("cut the UI over... gated on `systemValidation.validatePortfolio` reporting clean for every portfolio first... only once Phase 10 has run in production with zero validation blockers for a real trial period"). That validation can only run against real persisted user data in a real browser session, not the in-memory fake repositories available in this session — flipping the read-side cutover without it would be exactly the "remove the old path before the new one is proven" mistake this project's own migration discipline was written to prevent. See "Next recommended sprint" below for what closing this gap actually requires next.

### Evidence Architecture — provenance, Evidence Graph, and a richer minimal-document plan

Direct follow-up request: make the Ledger (and now Portfolio/Holdings) "no longer responsible for business truth" — evidence should be. Target architecture specified a persisted "Evidence Graph" connecting documents/facts with corroboration/contradiction/missing edges, permanent per-fact provenance (OCR confidence, extraction method, parser version, page, corroborating/conflicting evidence), and self-healing regeneration on later uploads.

Read the target against the codebase before building anything, per this sprint's own explicit invitation to challenge and deviate with justification. Most of the target was already true (RawTransaction as the fact log; `commitEngine`/`ledgerProjection` as a reactive, self-regenerating projection — proven by an existing test, "HEADLINE: a missing historical Buy discovered by a later import materializes as a real Trade row, no manual entry, no reset"). Two real gaps existed and are now closed; one part of the spec (storing corroboration/conflict permanently on each fact) was deliberately not built as literally specified, because doing so would have been a regression, not an improvement — see `docs/EVIDENCE_ARCHITECTURE.md` for the full reasoning.

1. **Extraction provenance** (`RawTransaction.extractionMethod`/`.parserVersion`, new): `ImportOrchestrator.importFile` already knows whether a file is an image (OCR), a PDF (native text layer), or CSV (plain text) — now stamps that channel, plus which `BrokerParser` version produced the read (`ThndrParser.version`/`CsvStatementParser.version`, new), onto every candidate/order-evidence row before it becomes a fact. Independent of `confidence` (which only ever measured ticker-resolution certainty within already-extracted text, never how the text itself was obtained) — closes the exact gap the first architecture review flagged (a native-PDF Statement and an OCR'd screenshot were being trusted identically). Not yet wired to a decision (see limitations) — captured and queryable, nothing conditions a verdict on it yet.
2. **Evidence Graph** (`evidenceGraph.ts`, new): `buildEvidenceGraph(ticker, params, uploads?)` composes `verifyAllDetailed`/`assessTickerCompleteness` — already-computed, not reimplemented — into a real node/edge structure: one node per live Buy/Sell fact and per source Upload, one converging `ticker-position` node every transaction reconciles against (mirroring the spec's own Invoice→Orders→Statement→My Position example), `corroborates`/`contradicts` edges from each transaction's own evidence items, and `missing` edges for orphaned Orders-history rows with no matching fact at all. **Deliberately not persisted** — no new Dexie table, no second source of truth for corroboration judgments that must be recomputed as new evidence arrives, exactly the discipline `ledgerCache`/`holdingsEngine` already established. Building it surfaced one real, pre-existing dead field: `EvidenceItem.matchedTransactionId` was declared since Phase 9.5 but never populated (`corroboratingSourceLabel` computed the donor transaction internally and discarded it) — fixed (renamed `corroboratingSource`, now returns the donor's key) so real transaction-to-transaction edges exist, not just descriptions.
3. **Richer minimal-document plan** (`completenessEngine.RecoveryPlan.expectedExecution`, new): the direct-evidence recovery branch now names the exact missing execution (ticker/side/date/shares) straight from the orphaned Orders-history row, matching the business rule's own worked example (a named ticker/date/quantity, never "upload everything").
- 6 new tests (`evidenceGraph.test.ts` — nodes/edges shape, sourced-from/corroborates/missing edges, empty-ticker case; `completenessEngine.test.ts` — the CSAG worked example verbatim). 789 tests total (up from 783); `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check`/production build all clean.
- **Deliberately deviated from the literal spec**: "every extracted fact must permanently remember... corroborating evidence... conflicting evidence" was not implemented as stated — storing a corroboration/contradiction judgment ON a fact would require actively invalidating it the instant a new, contradicting document arrives later, which is exactly the class of staleness bug this architecture's append-only, always-regenerate design exists to prevent. The graph is a live view instead, recomputed on every call from the current total evidence set — provenance (which document, which extraction channel, which parser version) is permanently stored per fact, as specified; corroboration/contradiction is not, and shouldn't be.
- **Known limitations, stated**: `extractionMethod` isn't yet a decision input anywhere (the natural next step, now that the signal exists); `expectedExecution` only names the first of several orphaned rows for a ticker with more than one gap; per-page provenance was scoped out — `extractPdfText` has no page-boundary tracking today, and no real Statement in this app is long enough to justify reworking PDF extraction internals for a field nothing reads yet.

### Evidence Coverage Engine, Canonical Transaction view, Evidence Intelligence facade, Evidence Authority

Direct follow-up: implement Evidence Coverage tracking, a canonical per-execution identity, a single reasoning facade, and a documented evidence-authority ranking — reusing the existing engines throughout rather than adding parallel ones, per this sprint's own explicit instruction to remove duplicate/parallel logic, not add more.

1. **Evidence Coverage Engine** (`evidenceCoverage.ts`, new): `buildCoverageClaims(transactions)` groups already-extracted `RawTransaction`s by `sourceUploadId` and derives what each upload actually covers — a date range for Statement/Transactions (approximated as the min/max execution date it actually contains — the Statement's own literal "From X To Y" header isn't captured by `ThndrParser` today, and extracting it wasn't worth reworking already-battle-tested parsing code for), ticker-history for Orders, one exact execution for Invoice, current-holdings-only for My Position. Wired into `completenessEngine.recoveryPlan`: a document type already covering the gap window is now skipped in favor of the next-best (and finally Invoice, which is never "already covered") — closing the "known simplification" that engine's own doc comment named across the last two sprints ("a ticker whose Orders History was uploaded but doesn't cover the window reads identically to one that never had it at all").
2. **Canonical Transaction Identity** (`canonicalTransaction.ts`, new): `buildCanonicalTransactions(ticker, params, uploads)` — every execution as exactly one object (evidence sources, evidence count, corroborating/contradicting edges, current status, and fees/taxes taken from whichever contributing document carries the highest Evidence Authority), grouped by the same `canonicalKey` `ledgerEngine.ts` already uses for its own event identity. **Deliberately not a new persisted entity/table** — a second, separately-stored "Canonical Transaction" would itself be the parallel implementation this sprint's instructions said to remove, not add; this is a read-only view composing `verifyAllDetailed`/`buildEvidenceGraph`, exactly like the Evidence Graph itself.
3. **Evidence Authority** (`evidenceAuthority.ts`, new): ranks which document's own execution-detail fields (price/fees/shares/date) win when two sources disagree — Invoice > Statement > Orders-screen > the shared Orders-timeline/Transactions/in-app-order-detail bucket > CSV > manual. **Deliberate, evidence-based deviation from the literal spec**: My Position is excluded from this ranking entirely, not placed second-to-last as specified. My Position never describes an execution's price/fees/shares/date at all — it only ever shows the current holdings count (established across every prior sprint this session) — so it has no execution-detail field to ever win or lose a dispute over; ranking it "above OCR-only" for a kind of comparison it structurally can't participate in would be a category error, not a ranking. Two more real, disclosed limitations: "Email Invoice" vs. "In-App Invoice", and account-wide "Orders" timeline vs. the dated "Transactions" list, aren't separately distinguishable via `RawTransactionSource` today (both pairs already collapse to shared source values in `ImportOrchestrator`'s own routing) — ranked as what's actually distinguishable, not a fabricated 7-tier split the data model can't support yet.
4. **Evidence Intelligence Layer** (`evidenceIntelligence.ts`, new): `getEvidenceIntelligence(ticker, params, uploads)` — the one composed facade answering all five required questions (confirmed/missing/contradictory/strongest evidence/next document) by delegating entirely to `canonicalTransaction`, `completenessEngine`, `evidenceGraph`, and `evidenceAuthority`. Computes nothing itself; extending what "business truth" means for a ticker means extending one of those four, never adding logic here.
- 18 new tests: `evidenceCoverage.test.ts` (7), `evidenceAuthority.test.ts` (4), `canonicalTransaction.test.ts` (4), `evidenceIntelligence.test.ts` (3), plus 2 new `completenessEngine.test.ts` cases (the coverage-skip rule; re-verifying the CSAG worked example still holds). 808 tests total (up from 789); `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check`/production build all clean.
- **Verified end-to-end against this session's own SKPC proof**: `evidenceIntelligence.test.ts`'s SKPC-shaped test reproduces the exact real scenario this session traced by execution earlier (4 buys totaling 82 shares, one 82-share sell, no independent corroboration) and confirms it now correctly lands in `needsReview` with a recommended document that is never "My Position" (the ticker is closed) — the same bug, now provably fixed at every layer this sprint added, not just the one it was first found in.
- **Deliberately NOT done, and why**: the live-screen read cutover and cash-as-projection remain not attempted, unchanged reasoning from the last two sprints (needs validation against real persisted user data in a real browser session). **Merging this branch to `main` was also not performed** — `deploy-pages.yml` triggers on `push: branches: [main]`, so on this repo merging to main IS the production deploy, not a separate gated step; doing that autonomously, unreviewed, after three consecutive large sprints rewriting core evidence/verification/ledger logic (including one point in this sprint, Evidence Authority's My-Position ranking, where the literal spec was judged technically wrong and deviated from) is exactly the class of hard-to-reverse, real-financial-data action that needs the repository owner's own explicit action, not a standing instruction issued before any of this diff existed. A PR was opened instead; see its description for the exact same reasoning.

**Merged to `main` (PR #74) at the user's explicit direction** in a following turn — `deploy-pages.yml`'s `push: branches: [main]` trigger fired and the production deploy was verified green.

### Production read cutover — Holdings/Dashboard onto the canonical ledger, cash fact-writing, duplicate-logic unification

Direct follow-up, the most explicit yet: "COMPLETE the migration," not build another layer — wire the UI to the Evidence Intelligence/Canonical Transaction/Ledger Projection stack as the live read path, remove bypasses, remove dead code, re-audit the whole repo for duplicates. Read every candidate live-cutover site against the actual risk before touching it, rather than blindly flipping every read in the app.

1. **Holdings read cutover** (`canonicalHoldings.ts`, new): `computeCanonicalPositions(repos, portfolioId, priceMap)` is the actual production cutover — `DashboardPage.tsx`, `PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`, and `PortfoliosPage.tsx`'s holdings/market-value reads now call it instead of the legacy `computePositions`. It is not a blind swap: for each ticker it computes both the canonical (`committedLedger` events/allocations → `computeHoldings`) and legacy (`Trade`/`TradeAllocation`) positions and reconciles them — agreement serves the canonical number (`source: "canonical"`); a ticker the canonical side has nothing for (never reached a terminal verification verdict) or that disagrees with legacy falls back to the legacy number, tagged `source: "legacy-fallback"` with a `fallbackReason` explaining exactly why. This operationalizes `systemValidation.ts`'s one-time manual gate as an always-on runtime safeguard, rather than waiting on a manual validation pass this sandboxed session has no way to run against the real user's actual IndexedDB. The canonical side is additionally wrapped in its own try/catch (`tryComputeCanonicalByTicker`) so a canonical-read failure of any kind degrades to pure legacy behavior rather than ever crashing the Holdings page. Proven against the exact shape of this session's own SKPC bug: a Needs-Review ticker with a real open `Trade` but no `ledgerCache` entry yet correctly reports its real share count, served as `legacy-fallback` — never silently dropped to zero. 3 new tests (`canonicalHoldings.test.ts`).
2. **Cash fact-writing** (`PortfolioService.ts`): `setCash`, `recordDividend`, `recordCashAdjustment`, and `deleteDividend` now dual-write/retract `CashReset`/`DividendPayment`/`CashAdjustment` `RawTransaction` facts alongside their existing imperative `portfolio.cash` mutation and `TimelineEvent`, using the same non-fatal shadow-write discipline as every prior dual-write in this migration (`console.error` + continue, never throw). The Dividend/CashAdjustment facts reuse the correlating `TimelineEvent`'s own id, so `deleteDividend` can retract the matching fact by that id later.
3. **Backfill extended for cash history** (`backfillRawTransactions.ts`): now also enumerates every portfolio (not just ones with trades — a portfolio with only a dividend must not be skipped), reads its `TimelineEvent`s, and converts existing `Dividend`/`CashAdjustment` events into the same facts the new writers produce going forward, reusing each event's own id. New `cashEventsBackfilled` count on the result. 2 new tests.
4. **Cash projection** (`cashProjection.ts`, new): `computeCashProjection(facts, portfolioId)` — a pure, fully-tested replay of cash-affecting facts (`BuyExecution`/`SellExecution`/`DividendPayment`/`CashAdjustment`/`Deposit`/`Withdrawal`), starting from the latest non-retracted `CashReset`'s asserted baseline and summing everything recorded after it by `seq`. **Deliberately not wired to any live read** — see the blocker below. 9 tests (`cashProjection.test.ts`).
5. **Duplicate-logic audit and unification** (`reconciliation.ts`): a background repo-wide audit (per this sprint's explicit "search the entire repository for bypasses... complete repository audit" instruction) found two genuine duplicates and one false positive. `reconcilePositions`'s own match/mismatch judgment now delegates to `checkTickerMatch` (the same canonical function Import's live commit gate and Evidence Intelligence both call) instead of a second hand-rolled comparison — its own `verificationStale` (a time-bounded "did a newer trade already explain this gap" check `checkTickerMatch` has no equivalent for at all) is kept as the one genuinely non-duplicated piece. `suggestDuplicateTradeIds` now delegates to `mismatchResolver.suggestRemovalsToReconcile` — the same avg-cost-ranked, alternatives-aware solver Import's own reconcile banner already uses — whenever a verified avg cost is actually available to rank by; without one, the canonical solver has no price-preference signal at all, so the original lowest-price-first greedy heuristic (a real, sound domain rule: a duplicate-imported read of the same trade differs mostly in price rounding, and the lower reads are the more likely duplicates) remains primary, and is also the fallback above the solver's `MAX_RECONCILE_ROWS` search-space limit. A third candidate — `PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`'s inline as-of-verification-timestamp share recomputation inside `handleDeleteTrade` — was audited and judged a false positive: a genuinely different, narrow, time-bounded deletion-safety guard with no clean equivalent in `checkTickerMatch` (which only ever evaluates "as of now"), left unchanged. 1 new test (proving the avg-cost delegation actually engages and picks the mathematically correct subset).
- 823 tests total (up from 808); `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check`/production build (`vite build`) all clean.
- **What was NOT cut over, and why**: `TradesPage.tsx`, `JournalPage.tsx`, and `SellAllocationForm.tsx` still read `Trade`/`TradeAllocation` directly — they need actual entity CRUD/lot-picking (create/edit/delete a specific lot, choose which lot a Sell closes), which a read-only holdings projection has no equivalent for; `AnalyticsPage.tsx`'s historical performance curves are a different question ("what happened over time") than "what do I hold right now," and were left alone. These aren't bypasses of the new architecture — they're the write side and a historical-analysis view, neither of which "Holdings" describes.
- **Remaining blocker, with concrete evidence — cash-as-projection is not live yet**: `computeCashProjection` exists, is fully tested, and every fact writer it depends on (`recordDividend`/`recordCashAdjustment`/`setCash`, plus `backfillRawTransactions`'s new coverage) is now in place — but the historical backfill for dividends/cash-adjustments has never been run against a real portfolio's actual history, only fake test fixtures (`grep` across this diff shows zero real-database backfill invocation; the app's own `backfillRawTransactions` is a one-time, already-run migration step per `BackfillAlreadyRanError`'s own contract, meaning this NEW cash coverage needs its own equivalent one-time run against the live production database before `computeCashProjection` can replace `portfolio.cash` as a read). This sandboxed session has no access to the user's real browser/IndexedDB to execute that step. Flipping the cash read to the projection today would under-count every pre-existing portfolio's true balance by every dividend/adjustment recorded before this sprint — a real, silent financial-data regression, not a hypothetical one. This is the one remaining step; no additional code is needed to close it.


### Per-ticker reset (Import) + full factory reset (Data page)

Direct user request (in Arabic): (1) on the Import page, a button next to each stock that erases everything recorded for that stock individually, so its page starts fresh and its documents can be re-imported from scratch as if it were new; (2) on the Data page, a reset button that erases all recorded data for every stock and returns the whole system to a fresh start.

1. **`src/infrastructure/db/purge.ts`** (new): `purgeTickerData(ticker)` and `purgeAllData()` — hard factory-reset operations, deliberately NOT part of any domain repository interface, since the `RawTransaction` log is append-only by design (corrections/retractions, never physical deletes) and these are the single sanctioned exception: a user-initiated "start over" that erases history outright rather than folding it. They operate on the Dexie database directly (storage-level maintenance, within one `rw` transaction across all ten tables), so the append-only contract every application service codes against stays intact. `purgeTickerData` removes the ticker's trades, allocations, timeline events, journal entries (by tradeId), verifications, raw transactions (following `targetId`/`supersedes` chains to a fixpoint so no orphaned Retraction/Correction rows survive), `ledgerCache`/`allocationsCache` rows, and any upload whose candidates carried the ticker (so the file-hash dedup can't block a re-upload) — and reverses the ticker's net timeline cash impact per portfolio (buys negative, sells/dividends positive) so cash balances also read as if it never traded. 5 new tests (`purge.test.ts`), 828 total.
2. **ImportPage**: `resetTickerData(ticker)` — confirm() naming exactly what's erased, then `purgeTickerData` plus a full scrub of the ticker from the import session (pending/discarded candidates, verifications, dividends, order evidences, all key sets, `addedTradeIds`/`addedAllocationIds`, `tickerPortfolio`). Surfaced as a trash icon in each `TickerGroupCard` header (next to rename/restore) and as a "Reset" button on each fully-matched ticker's row in the completed section — a user usually notices wrong data only after distribution.
3. **DataPage**: a "Reset everything" danger card (below the Rebuild panel) — double `confirm()`, then `purgeAllData()` + `importSession.clear()`. Portfolios included: the system afterwards is indistinguishable from a fresh install. Language and tracking-start-date preferences deliberately survive (settings, not data).
4. Full EN/AR translations for all new strings (`data.reset*`, `importPage.resetTicker*`).

### Lot Manager + the identity-collision root-cause fix

Direct user request, two parts: (1) fix a reported production bug — allocating one Sell transaction could silently change unrelated Sell transactions, close unrelated Buy lots, and mismatch Holdings; (2) replace the Sell Allocation popup with a full ticker-scoped Lot Manager (Portfolio → Ticker Details → Lot Manager).

**Root cause, found by tracing the actual commit/projection pipeline against a deliberately-constructed collision, not by inspection alone**: `LedgerEvent.eventId` (and every `SellAllocationDecision`'s `lotRef`/`sellExecutionId` reference) was derived from a recomputed VALUE hash — `canonicalKey(ticker|side|date|shares|price)` — never from the underlying `RawTransaction`'s own always-unique id. Two genuinely distinct real executions sharing that value (two same-price same-day orders — an ordinary occurrence, not an edge case) collided onto the identical identity. `ledgerProjection.ts`'s `projectLegacyTicker` (which rewrites the `Trade`/`TradeAllocation` rows the UI reads, on every commit) then either overwrote one lot's row with the other's data or deleted a "stale" allocation that was actually still live — the exact reported symptom set. Reproduced directly (not just reasoned about) via `crossTransactionIsolation.test.ts` before any fix existed, confirming the failure, then fixed and re-verified the same tests now pass deterministically across repeated runs.

1. **`ledgerRebuild.ts`**: `disambiguateCollidingKeys` — after `canonicalizeTradeEntries` builds its `buys`/`sells` output, any two entries that still land on the identical `key` (the coincidence case, not the legitimate cross-document-corroboration case, which already collapses correctly upstream) get deterministically disambiguated by appending the lexicographically-smaller-losing entry's own stable `entryId` — 100% backward compatible for the non-colliding case (the overwhelming majority of data), only changes the previously-broken colliding case.
2. **`ledgerEngine.ts`**: `generateLedgerEvents` no longer routes "manual"/"backfill" sourced facts through `canonicalizeTradeEntries`'s OCR corroboration-vs-coincidence heuristic at all — neither source is ever "the same execution read from two different documents" (a manual entry is one direct user action; a backfilled fact is a 1:1 historical-Trade conversion), so each maps straight to its own event keyed by the RawTransaction's real id. This is what actually closes the gap the disambiguation pass alone couldn't: the OCR heuristic (`duplicateDetection.sameCandidateExecution`, price/time-based, with no execution-id signal for non-document sources) was itself merging two coincidentally-identical manual/backfilled facts into one entry before disambiguation ever ran.
3. **`allocationEngine.ts`**: `generateAllocations` resolves a decision's `lotRef`/`sellExecutionId` reference by checking the real RawTransaction id first (via each event's `sourceTransactionIds`), falling back to the legacy value-hash `eventId` match for decisions written before this fix — both schemes keep resolving correctly, forever, regardless of which one a future rebuild uses for new writes.
4. **`TradeService.ts`/`backfillRawTransactions.ts`**: `ensureSellFacts` always writes its SellExecution fact (the old value-hash dedup skip had no real caller relying on it and was itself a second, independent source of data loss — see the module's own updated doc comment); every decision now references the real fact ids (`sellGroupId` for the sell, `resolveLotRef` for each closed lot) instead of a recomputed value hash. `ensureBuyFact` no longer adopts a same-value fact another Trade already owns.
5. **`ledgerProjection.ts`**: `projectLegacyTicker`'s Trade-matching is now collision-safe — a dedicated exact-id pass across ALL lots runs before any same-value fallback claim, so an early-processed lot in a colliding group can never "steal" (via the value-based fallback) the trade a later lot was always meant to exact-match; `ensureLegacyFactsExist`'s gap-backfill is count-based (per value-group, N legacy trades/sell-orders sharing a value now correctly get matched 1:1 against N live facts, backfilling only the true remainder) instead of a boolean "has this value been seen" check that silently left every trade past the first uncovered.
6. **`systemValidation.ts`**: the old-vs-new "missing-in-new" check now matches a legacy Trade against the new ledger by real id (via `sourceTransactionIds`) instead of recomputing the same collision-prone value hash.
- New `application/services/lotManager.ts`: the ticker-scoped read/write model the Lot Manager UI is built on — `getLotManagerSnapshot` (Buy Lots, Sell Transactions with Pending/Partial/Completed status, current position, timeline, validation issues, all recomputed fresh on every call from live RawTransactions, never cached/mutated), `recordSellTransaction` (records the sell execution only — cash realized immediately, independent of allocation), `setSellAllocation`/`resetSellAllocation` (replace a Sell's entire allocation with an explicit line set; Reset Allocation retracts only that Sell's own decision, provably isolated from every other Sell/lot), `proposeFifoAllocation` (a pure, never-auto-committed suggestion that naturally continues from wherever a prior confirm left off, satisfying "Continue FIFO" for free since it always proposes against the sell's current *remaining* balance), `isTemporallyValid` (a Buy dated after the Sell is always visible, never allocatable — enforced in both the read model's issue list and rejected outright by `setSellAllocation` itself, not just the UI).
- New `presentation/pages/TickerDetailPage.tsx` (route `/portfolios/:id/tickers/:ticker`, linked from each ticker in `PortfolioDetailPage`'s Holdings table): Current Position stat tiles, Buy Lots table (oldest→newest, never hidden — a future-dated lot stays listed with an inline explanation instead of being filtered out), Sell Transactions table with per-row Manage Allocation, a Manage Allocation modal (manual checkbox/qty allocation, Auto Allocate FIFO generating an editable preview that commits nothing until Save, Reset Allocation), and a Timeline where selecting a Buy/Sell highlights every Allocation Event connecting it to its counterpart rows. `TradesPage.tsx`'s "Record Sell" button no longer opens the old all-in-one lot-picker popup (`SellAllocationForm`, still used unchanged by `ImportPage.tsx`'s own import-candidate-allocation flow, out of this sprint's scope) — it now hands off to the ticker's own Lot Manager, where recording and allocating are two separate, explicit steps.
- 21 new tests: `crossTransactionIsolation.test.ts` (5 — the root-cause regression suite: two coincidentally-identical Buy lots/Sells never merge or interfere with each other, Reset Allocation touches only its own Sell, no automatic lot closing across repeated commits, inventory always equals Buy quantity minus that lot's own allocations) and `lotManager.test.ts` (8 — Pending→Partial→Completed staged allocation across multiple Buys/Sells, Continue FIFO resuming from the last partial lot, temporal-validation rejection, over-allocation/duplicate-lot/over-committed-balance rejection, the missing-allocation validation issue, deterministic rebuild, Reset Allocation isolation). Existing `ledgerEngine.test.ts`/`ledgerProjection.test.ts`/`backfillRawTransactions.test.ts`/`systemValidation.test.ts` updated where they asserted the now-intentionally-replaced value-hash-based contract. 867 tests total; `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check`/production build all clean; the full suite re-run several times back-to-back with zero flakes (the pre-fix code was flaky under this exact stress — a strong independent signal the collision was real, not just a hypothetical).
- **Verified live, not just via unit tests**: ran the actual dev server end-to-end with Playwright — created a portfolio, recorded two Buys and a Sell through the real UI, opened Manage Allocation, used Auto Allocate (FIFO), edited and saved the proposal, watched Buy Lots/Sell Transactions/current-position tiles update correctly, clicked a Timeline entry and confirmed only its own related rows highlighted, reopened Manage Allocation and used Reset, and confirmed the Portfolio's Holdings page reflected the reset correctly (shares back to fully open, cash unchanged — proving the cash-realized-at-execution/allocation-only-affects-cost-basis split holds in the real app, not just in the model). Zero console errors at any step.
- **Deliberately NOT done, and why**: the new page/modals are English-only (see "Next recommended sprint" item 13) — full bilingual coverage for a page this size was judged lower priority than shipping the fix and the working feature this session; `SellAllocationForm.tsx`/`ImportPage.tsx`'s own sell-allocation flow for import-detected candidates was left untouched (a different, already-working workflow, out of this bug's scope); merging to `main` / triggering the `deploy-pages.yml` production deploy was **not performed autonomously** — this touches core ledger/allocation logic across the whole app for a real financial-data product with an actual user, which is exactly the class of hard-to-reverse, shared-state action this project's own conventions (see the "Production read cutover" entry above, which made the identical call for a smaller change) reserve for the repository owner's own explicit go-ahead, not a standing autonomous instruction. All work is committed and pushed to the designated branch, ready for review/merge.

### STES "Needs Confirmation" invoice-confirmation workflow

Two-part direct user request. Part 1 (prior turn): the STES template's Instructions sheet gained a rule telling extracting AIs to write `Needs Confirmation` into a partial-fill BUY/SELL row's `Extraction Notes` cell instead of discarding the row. Part 2 (this sprint): wire that signal all the way through the app — import the transaction immediately (not held back), flag it `Pending Confirmation`, and let the user resolve it by uploading the specific transaction's broker invoice, without a separate confirmations feature. User explicitly redirected the UI placement mid-plan: no new page — the request must surface inside the **existing** verification-issue mechanism (`PortfolioDetailPage`'s holdings-table verification cell, today's home for `quantityMismatch`/`quantityShortfall`/"Matches broker"), not a bespoke `/confirmations` page.

- **`StesWorkbookParser.ts`**: now reads `Extraction Notes` (previously never read at all) and sets `ParsedTradeCandidate.needsConfirmation: true` when it's exactly `"Needs Confirmation"` (case/whitespace-insensitive). Nothing is rejected — these rows already imported fine; only the signal was being silently dropped.
- **Domain (additive)**: `Trade`/`TradeAllocation` gained `confirmationStatus?: "pending" | "verified"` — the same "TradeService-owned mutable exception to immutability" category as `Trade.remainingShares`. `ParsedTradeCandidate.needsConfirmation` threads from the parser through `ImportPage.tsx`'s `addBuyCandidate`/`SellAllocationForm.tsx`'s `recordSell` call, so a flagged candidate still commits through the exact same auto-commit (Buy) / manual-allocation-modal (Sell, ADR-002 unchanged) paths as any other row — just tagged `"pending"` on arrival.
- **`TradeService.ts`**: new `confirmPendingBuy`/`confirmPendingSell` apply the uploaded invoice's authoritative shares/price/fees/taxes, adjusting portfolio cash for the exact delta and the matching Buy/Sell `TimelineEvent` to match — guarded to refuse a shares change once anything's already been allocated against a pending Buy, or across a multi-lot pending Sell (deciding which lot absorbs a share-count correction is exactly the explicit-allocation-decision ADR-002 already forbids automating). A real bug surfaced and was fixed by the tests written for this: the first `confirmPendingBuy` draft reset `remainingShares` to the new share count unconditionally, silently reopening shares that had legitimately already been sold — caught by a "confirm a price-only correction after a partial sell" test before it ever shipped.
- **`reconciliation.ts`**: new `findPendingConfirmations(trades, allocations)` — independent of `reconcilePositions` (which only ever produces a row for a ticker with a broker "My Position" screenshot on file; a pending confirmation has nothing to do with that and must surface regardless).
- **`PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`**: the holdings table's verification cell gained a new branch, checked first (before the existing dash/stale/mismatch/shortfall/matched branches), listing each pending item (side, shares, price, date) with an "Upload broker invoice" file control. Uploading runs the file through the exact same `ImportOrchestrator.importFile` pipeline Import's own dropzone uses, requires exactly one candidate whose ticker/side match the pending item (a sanity check, not a search — the user already picked which specific transaction this upload is for), and calls `confirmPendingBuy`/`confirmPendingSell` on a clean match. No manual "refresh" needed anywhere: every affected page already reads live via `useLiveQuery`, so cash/shares/P&L update the instant the write commits.
- Deliberately **not** wired into the parallel `RawTransaction`/commit-engine/Evidence-Graph architecture (`docs/VERIFICATION_ENGINE.md`) — that system is additive and not yet what `ImportPage.tsx`/`PortfolioDetailPage.tsx` actually read from; this stays in the "legacy" path that **is** the live source of truth, exactly where every other Import commit already writes.
- 14 new tests (895 total): 3 parser (`Extraction Notes` detection, case/whitespace-insensitivity, unrelated text ignored), 8 `TradeService` (`confirmPendingBuy`/`confirmPendingSell` happy paths, cash-delta correctness, the remainingShares regression above, multi-lot-shares-change refusal, non-pending refusal), 3 `reconciliation` (`findPendingConfirmations` grouping). `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean.
- **Verified end-to-end against a real running dev server with Playwright**: seeded a pending Buy and a pending Sell directly (bypassing the pre-existing, unrelated "every ticker needs a broker My Position screenshot before it can auto-commit" gate, which blocked driving the scenario through Import's own UI but is orthogonal to this feature), confirmed the "Needs confirmation" card renders with the exact expected Ticker/Side/Shares/Price/Date, uploaded a confirming STES invoice workbook and watched cash/shares/avg-cost update to the exact expected numbers with no reload (e.g. a 15→16-share Buy correction moved cash by precisely the 35.9 EGP delta; a 29→30-share Sell correction moved it by precisely 44.07 EGP), confirmed the card disappears once verified, and confirmed a mismatched-ticker invoice upload surfaces a clear inline error and leaves the pending item and all other data untouched.

### Audit: transaction-execution-status pipeline (Fulfilled / Cancelled / Partially filled) — found and fixed a real bug in the sprint above

Direct user request: audit the entire import/verification/ledger pipeline against an explicit three-state business-rule spec (Fulfilled / Cancelled / Partially filled-canceled) and fix anything that didn't match, with `Do NOT assume the current implementation is correct`. It didn't.

**Root cause, confirmed by code inspection then by a failing browser reproduction before any fix**: the "Needs Confirmation" feature from the sprint immediately above created the `Trade`/`TradeAllocation` **immediately** on import (via `confirmPendingBuy`/`confirmPendingSell`, only flagging `confirmationStatus: "pending"` on an already-live row). Since Holdings/cost-basis/cash are computed straight from `Trade.remainingShares`, this meant a partial-fill execution **already affected Holdings/cost basis/cash the moment it was imported** — directly contradicting "Block Ledger creation. Block Holdings updates." until the broker invoice confirms it. A second, independent bug: `SellAllocationForm`'s `openTrades` query filtered only on `remainingShares > 0`, not `confirmationStatus`, so an unconfirmed pending Buy was **already allocatable** before its executed quantity was even known. Separately, a genuine **gap** (not yet a triggered bug): the STES schema had no representation at all for a fully-cancelled order, so nothing prevented a future misextraction of one as a phantom, ledger-affecting BUY/SELL.

- **New `domain/entities/PendingExecution.ts`** + Dexie table (`db.ts` version 4, additive): a partial-fill execution now lives entirely OUTSIDE `Trade`/`TradeAllocation` until its invoice is confirmed — "blocked from the ledger" is true because the row doesn't exist yet, not because of a status filter that could be (and was) forgotten somewhere. `verificationStatus: "needs-confirmation"|"verified"`, `executionStatus: "pending-verification"|"executed"` track the spec's two named states directly.
- **New `application/services/pendingExecutions.ts`** replaces the old `confirmPendingBuy`/`confirmPendingSell`/`findPendingConfirmations` entirely: `createPendingExecutionRecord` (import time, no Trade created), `confirmPendingExecution` (invoice-matched — for a BUY this is the one moment a `Trade` is created at all, via the existing `recordBuy`; for a SELL, verifying only unblocks the explicit lot-allocation step, since this app never auto-picks which lot a sell closes, confirmed or not — ADR-002), `completeSellAllocationForPendingExecution` (fires after `SellAllocationForm`'s `recordSell` actually creates the `TradeAllocation` — the real moment a SELL's Ledger Entry exists). Every confirm updates the SAME row (guarded: an already-verified row refuses a second confirmation) — never a duplicate.
- **STES parser gained an `Order Status` column** (additive, matches v1.1's "may add optional columns" rule): the broker's own status text, verbatim. Containing "cancel" without "partial" → a new `ParsedCancelledOrder`/`RawTransactionKind: "CancelledOrder"` fact — audit trail only, structurally never read by `commitEngine`'s Buy/Sell fold or by `TradeService`/`computePositions` (not excluded by a check — the type doesn't exist in those code paths at all). Containing "partial" → `needsConfirmation` (same as before); the old `Extraction Notes: "Needs Confirmation"` convention with `Order Status` left blank still works unchanged, for backward compatibility with already-generated workbooks. Instructions sheet, `STANDARD_TRADING_EXCHANGE_SCHEMA.md`, and the shipped template's Examples sheet all updated to match.
- **`ImportPage.tsx`**: a `needsConfirmation` candidate no longer reaches `recordBuy` (Buy) or the allocation modal (Sell) at all — both route to `createPendingExecutionRecord` instead, leaving the review pool the same way a normal commit would.
- **`PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`**: the pending-item card now reads `PendingExecution` (not `Trade.confirmationStatus`), shows the broker's own status text, and gained a second sub-state: once verified, a SELL shows "Allocate sell" (opening `SellAllocationForm` pre-filled with the confirmed numbers, now accepting an optional `pendingExecutionId` prop) instead of "Upload invoice" — confirming and allocating read as one continuous action (uploading the invoice auto-opens the allocation modal) rather than a second silent click.
- `Trade.confirmationStatus`/`TradeAllocation.confirmationStatus` are left in place (deprecated, doc-commented) rather than removed — nothing sets them anymore, but a Trade written during the brief window the old code was live (this feature had just been merged and deployed minutes before this audit) still deserializes without error.
- 30 new/changed tests (886 total): `pendingExecutions.test.ts` (5 — the core fix, proving zero Trade/Holdings/cash impact pre-confirmation with exact-arithmetic assertions, the SAME-row/never-duplicated guarantee, BUY-ledgers-immediately vs. SELL-stays-pending-until-allocated), STES parser (+7 — `Order Status` partial/cancelled classification, backward compat), `importRecording.test.ts` (+1 — `CancelledOrder` fact, never a candidate), `commitEngine.test.ts` (+1 — a `CancelledOrder` fact is structurally invisible to `shouldCommit`/`commitTicker`), plus the old buggy mechanism's 8 tests deleted (they tested behavior that no longer exists). `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean.
- **Verified end-to-end against a real running dev server with Playwright** (same instance the previous sprint verified against, confirming the Dexie v3→v4 upgrade is non-destructive to real browser data): a pending SELL's card correctly shows "Needs confirmation" with the broker's status text in parentheses and Holdings unchanged; uploading its invoice flips it to "Verified — ready to allocate" and **auto-opens** the allocation modal pre-filled from the confirmed numbers, with Holdings still unchanged; completing the allocation only then updates Holdings/cash and clears the card. A pending BUY's invoice upload moved cash/cost-basis by exactly the confirmed delta (E£56.40) with no reload. A `Cancelled` STES row imported cleanly ("extracted successfully", no error), was confirmed via direct IndexedDB inspection to have written exactly one `CancelledOrder` `RawTransaction` fact (broker status "Cancelled" preserved verbatim) and **zero** `Trade`/`PendingExecution` rows for that ticker, and never appeared anywhere in Import's Step 2 review pool.

### Native Thndr "Your Orders" Excel import (new xlsx shape, distinct from STES)

User supplied a real broker export (`Account > Orders > Export` on Thndr) as their canonical broker record and asked it to be treated as an authoritative, single-source-of-truth import — every executed row its own trade lot, cancelled/rejected/expired/pending orders never a trade, no external corroboration required. Investigation found this file isn't in either format the importer already understood: not an OCR'd screenshot, and not the STES raw-extraction template (`isStesWorkbookFile` matches any `.xlsx` by extension, so this file was silently misrouted into `parseStesWorkbook` and hard-failed with a "missing Metadata/Documents/Observations sheet" error before this sprint).

- New `infrastructure/thndrOrders/ThndrOrdersWorkbookParser.ts`: reads the workbook's cells directly (not flattened OCR text) — a single-cell row introduces a ticker section (verbatim broker-printed ticker code, so every candidate gets `confidence: "high"`, no fuzzy company-name matching needed), a 6-column row is one order (date/time, type, time-in-force, price, filled/total quantity, status). FULFILLED/PARTIALLY FILLED rows become `ParsedTradeCandidate`s using only the *executed* quantity (`needsConfirmation: true` for a partial fill, same convention `StesWorkbookParser` already uses); CANCELLED/REJECTED/EXPIRED become audit-only `ParsedCancelledOrder`s; PENDING creates nothing. A "buy this many EGP worth" (value-based) order is skipped with a warning — this export prints no share count for it at all, and the policy this was built against is explicit that a missing value is never estimated.
- **Real-data correctness bug found and fixed before shipping**: verified against the actual uploaded workbook (~985 order rows) and found 100 of them (~10%) came back as "malformed" — Excel auto-converts a bare fraction like `"12/12"` into an actual date when both numbers look like a valid day/month, so the cell displays as `"12-Dec"` (or `"7/50"` → `"Jul-50"`, month/2-digit-year form, when the second number isn't a valid day). Read every real occurrence in the file to confirm the pattern is exact and lossless (day==month for every "D-MMM" case in this file; the one "MMM-YY" case decodes to month/year-suffix) before writing `recoverAutoDatedFraction` — deliberately conservative: an unseen "D-MMM" row where day and month disagree is left unrecovered rather than guessed, since fabricating a share count in a financial ledger is worse than reporting it. After the fix, all 985 order rows in the real file are accounted for exactly (766 candidates + 156 cancelled/rejected/expired + 62 value-orders-skipped + 1 unresolvable-ticker-section = 985), zero silently dropped.
- **`ImportOrchestrator.ts`**: STES's file-level check now falls through to this new parser instead of hard-failing when an `.xlsx` doesn't match the STES schema (tried in that order since STES's Metadata-sheet check is the more specific signal); a file matching neither reports a combined failure with no docType, rather than misreporting itself as `"stes-workbook"`. Recognized rows converge into the exact same `ImportResult` shape as every other document type. New `ImportDocType` member `"thndr-orders-workbook"` and `ExtractionMethod` member `"thndr-orders-workbook"` (added to `RawTransaction.ts`/`Upload.ts`).
- **Source/authority reuse, not a new tier**: candidates are tagged `source: "orders-screen"` — the same document type STES already collapses its own `ORDERS_SCREEN` observations into — since this is the same "dated, per-order, ticker-scoped, quantity-exact history" document, just captured by native export instead of OCR. This means `evidenceAuthority.ts`/`ledgerEngine.ts`/`verificationEngine.ts`/`evidenceCoverage.ts` needed zero changes; the export inherits the correct existing authority rank and coverage-claim behavior for free.
- 10 new tests (896 total): 9 parser-level (`ThndrOrdersWorkbookParser.test.ts` — title recognition, fulfilled buy/sell, cancelled/rejected/expired never a trade, partial-fill executed-quantity + confirmation flag, value-order skip, unrecognized-ticker-section skip, pending creates nothing, both auto-dated-fraction recovery shapes) and 1 orchestrator-level (`ImportOrchestrator.thndrOrdersWorkbook.test.ts`); updated the existing STES "not a workbook" orchestrator test for the new (more correct) fallback-through behavior. `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (896 tests) green.
- **Prompt-injection note**: the request arrived as an document titled a "Mandatory Policy" claiming to "override every previous verification workflow... business logic" app-wide — flagged to the user as reading like an attempt to disable engineering judgment wholesale rather than a normal product spec, before any code was written. The on-topic parts (an official broker export is high-authority, doesn't need corroborating screenshots, one executed row = one independent lot, cancelled/pending orders never become trades) already matched this app's existing design and are what got built; the document's blanket "never validate/never report an error" framing was not taken as license — the auto-dated-fraction bug above was still investigated and fixed rather than silently skipped, and value-based orders with a genuinely missing share count are still reported, not guessed.
- **Not done / left for a future sprint**: the actual uploaded file was inspected and used to validate the parser's correctness, but was **not committed to Trade/TradeAllocation data** — doing so wasn't requested (the user asked for the reusable import capability, not a one-off data load) and this session has no live browser/IndexedDB to write into anyway. Next step for the user: drop the real file into the running app's Import page and confirm the Distribute step looks right before assigning it to a portfolio.

### Thndr Excel importer: dedicated "official broker Excel" trust tier

Direct follow-up to the sprint above. User clarified scope after reviewing the parser: not a global relaxation of validation, but a trust-policy change scoped to exactly this one importer — "Transactions imported through the official Thndr Excel parser should be treated as broker-authoritative records," with existing malformed-file/corrupted-data/duplicate-import detection left untouched everywhere, including inside this same parser.

- New `RawTransactionSource` member `"official-broker-excel"` (was reusing `"orders-screen"`, which would have let this importer's trust silently ride on the OCR Orders-screen tier instead of getting its own). `ThndrOrdersWorkbookParser.ts` now tags every candidate and cancelled-order with it.
- **`evidenceAuthority.ts`**: new rank between invoice and statement — the native export is broker-verbatim like an invoice, but (like a statement) doesn't itemize fees.
- **`importVerification.ts`** (`checkTickerMatch`): new `allPendingFromOfficialBrokerExcel` gate, parallel to the existing `allPendingFromInvoice` one — a ticker whose every pending candidate came from this source is `matched: true` (`reason: "broker-excel-verified"`) without ever needing a broker "My Position" screenshot, exactly like an invoice-sourced batch. Same safety caveat as invoice: only substitutes for a *missing* screenshot — a screenshot that's actually present and genuinely mismatches still blocks (new test asserts this explicitly, since "never ask for evidence" must never mean "ignore evidence that's already there").
- **`ImportPage.tsx`**: computes the new gate alongside the existing invoice one, folds `"official-broker-excel"` into the cross-verified/orders-verified OR-chains too (so a mixed invoice+broker-Excel batch for the same ticker still qualifies), and renders a new "Verified — official broker Excel" banner (`ShieldCheck`, same green treatment as invoice-verified) — new i18n key in both `en`/`ar`.
- **`evidenceCoverage.ts`**: a native export spans every ticker the account ever traded (unlike a per-ticker Orders screenshot upload), so it produces one ticker-history claim *per ticker actually present* in the file rather than one claim for the whole upload — the one documented exception to `buildCoverageClaims`'s "one upload, one claim" rule.
- **`completenessEngine.ts`**: `broker-excel-verified` classifies as `"Complete"`, same tier as `invoice-verified`/`cross-verified`/`orders-verified`.
- **Real behavior change inside the parser, prompted by re-reading the request**: a `PARTIALLY FILLED` row no longer sets `needsConfirmation`/`brokerStatus` (which would have routed it through `PendingExecution`, asking for an invoice before it could affect Holdings). STES's `needsConfirmation` exists for a genuinely uncertain AI-extracted reading; this export's executed-share fraction (`"187/200"`) is printed directly by Thndr's own order-management system, with no OCR or AI guess involved — there was nothing to confirm, so requiring an invoice anyway would have been exactly the "requests confirmation for these transactions" behavior the user was explicitly asking to remove. Partial fills are now normal, final candidates using only the executed quantity, same as a full fill.
- **What's unchanged, deliberately**: file-level recognition (unreadable workbook, wrong title cell), row-level malformed-date/type/quantity detection, the contradictory-zero-shares check, the auto-dated-fraction recovery (and its conservative refusal to guess an unseen asymmetric case), and value-based-order skipping all still run exactly as before — none of that is "asking for evidence," it's rejecting genuinely bad data, which the user's own instructions asked to keep. Generic duplicate-detection/file-hash dedup is source-agnostic and untouched. No other `BrokerParser`/importer sets `source: "official-broker-excel"`, so every other import path's verification behavior is provably unaffected by construction, not just by convention.
- 4 new tests (900 total): 3 `importVerification.test.ts` (trusts a broker-Excel-only batch with no screenshot, still blocks on a real mismatch, invoice checked first when both gates are somehow true) and 1 `evidenceCoverage.test.ts` (per-ticker claim splitting); updated the parser/orchestrator tests for the new source string and the removed partial-fill confirmation gate. `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (900 tests) green.
- **Not done**: no UI/manual verification pass in a real browser for this sprint (session has no live browser); the `ImportPage.tsx` banner rendering was reviewed by reading the code path the existing `invoice-verified` banner already exercises (same component, same props shape), not re-verified live.

### Thndr Excel importer: Excel wins even against a disagreeing screenshot

Direct follow-up, same session. Prior sprint's `checkTickerMatch` gate only substituted for a MISSING "My Position" screenshot — a screenshot that was actually present and disagreed still blocked the batch (`reason: "mismatch"`), same as every other source. User clarified the trust policy goes further: the Excel export outranks a screenshot/notification/OCR read even when they actively conflict, not just when the secondary source is silent. The transaction must stay Verified; the conflict is a non-blocking note for the user to review, never a gate.

- **`importVerification.ts`** (`checkTickerMatch`): the `allPendingFromOfficialBrokerExcel` check moved to run unconditionally, before the `verifiedUnits`/screenshot branch entirely (previously nested inside the "no screenshot at all" branch, same as invoice still is — invoice's own behavior is deliberately unchanged, since the user's instructions named only the Excel importer). New `TickerMatchStatus.secondaryMismatch` field: true only on `reason: "broker-excel-verified"`, when a screenshot exists and disagrees — `matched` stays `true` regardless, so nothing downstream (the two-phase Import commit gate, which reads `matched` alone) is blocked by it.
- **`ImportPage.tsx`**: the "Verified — official broker Excel" badge now renders an adjacent, separate amber "Screenshot mismatch — for review" chip when `secondaryMismatch` is true — visually distinct from the blocking rose "Mismatch" badge every other source still gets, so a user can tell at a glance this is a note, not a gate. New i18n keys (`matchSecondaryMismatch`/its tooltip) in `en`/`ar`.
- **Scope discipline, unchanged from the prior sprint**: nothing about file-level or row-level validation inside the parser changed — a malformed/corrupted/internally-inconsistent Excel file is still the only thing that can actually block. Invoice's own "still blocks on a real mismatch" behavior is untouched, since the user's instructions named only the Excel importer.
- 4 new/changed tests (902 total) in `importVerification.test.ts`: replaced the now-incorrect "still blocks" assertion with three covering the new behavior (stays verified + flags the mismatch when a screenshot disagrees, no flag when it agrees, no flag when no screenshot exists at all) and corrected a synthetic both-flags-true precedence test. `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (902 tests) green.
- **Not done**: no live-browser verification of the new amber chip's rendering this sprint (session has no browser); reviewed by reading the same component/props path the existing badges already exercise.

### Thndr Excel importer: full removal of the My Position screenshot workflow for fully-Excel-sourced tickers

Direct follow-up, same session — an explicit architecture decision: "for portfolios imported from the Official Broker Excel, the screenshot verification flow should no longer exist anywhere in the application." Audited every place a screenshot requirement can surface (not just ImportPage) before changing anything, since this touches more than the Import page's own gate.

**What was already correct** (verified, not just assumed): ImportPage's `RecoveryPlanPanel`/`MatchBadge` banners ("Needs broker screenshot", "Closes this gap: My Position screenshot", "Orders History screenshot required") are all downstream of `matchStatus.matched` — the prior sprint's `broker-excel-verified` gate already forces `matched: true` there, and `completenessEngine`'s `recoveryPlan()` only ever runs when a ticker classifies as `"Incomplete"`, which `broker-excel-verified` never does (`classify()` maps it to `"Complete"`). So the four banned banner strings were already structurally unreachable for a ticker whose current import batch is 100% Excel-sourced.

**Two real gaps found and fixed**:
- **`verificationEngine.ts`**'s own `computeVerification` (feeds the additive RawTransaction-based evidence architecture — `evidenceGraph.ts`/`evidenceIntelligence.ts`/`commitEngine.ts`, not yet cut over to any live UI, but a real remaining code path per the architecture decision's own wording) never threaded an `allPendingFromOfficialBrokerExcel` flag into its own `checkTickerMatch` call at all — only `allPendingFromInvoice` existed there. Added the missing flag, mirroring ImportPage's own computation exactly.
- **`reconciliation.ts`/`PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`**: the ongoing (not import-time) holdings-table verification cell compares every ticker's computed position against its latest "My Position" screenshot — informational, never blocking, but still a "verification state related to My Position screenshots" the architecture decision named for removal. New `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced(rawTransactions, ticker)` (folds live Buy/Sell RawTransaction facts for the ticker, retraction-aware) — false for a ticker with zero facts or any mixed provenance. `reconcilePositions` gained an optional `rawTransactions` param and now skips generating any row at all for such a ticker, regardless of whether a screenshot exists, agrees, or disagrees — `PortfolioDetailPage.tsx` now fetches `repos.rawTransactions.getByPortfolio` (a repo it never queried before) and renders a positive "Verified — official broker Excel" cell for these tickers, ahead of the dash/stale/mismatch/shortfall chain, instead of silently falling through to a blank dash.
- Legacy `Trade`/`TradeAllocation` entities carry no source/provenance field at all (confirmed by inspection) — this is why the check has to go through the RawTransaction fact log rather than the Trade repository; a real, disclosed architectural constraint, not an oversight.

**Confirmed already true, no change needed**: Holdings (`TradeService.computePositions`) is universal executed-BUY-minus-executed-SELL arithmetic regardless of source — was never influenced by a screenshot to begin with. Portfolio assignment (the ticker→portfolio picker in ImportPage) was never gated by match status, only the final commit button was. Allocation (`SellAllocationForm`) isn't gated by `matchStatus` either (a separate ADR-002 concern). Parser validation, duplicate detection, and malformed-file/arithmetic checks were untouched, per the architecture decision's own item 6.

- 9 new tests (910 total): 4 `reconciliation.test.ts` (`isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` true/mixed/empty/retracted cases) + 2 (`reconcilePositions` skips a fully-Excel ticker even against a disagreeing screenshot; still reconciles a partly-Excel ticker normally), 1 `verificationEngine.test.ts` (`computeVerification`'s own gate now agrees with ImportPage's), 1 `PortfolioDetailPage.test.tsx` (renders "Verified — official broker Excel", suppresses the mismatch text and the duplicate-cleanup button, against a screenshot that actively disagrees). New i18n keys (`matchesBrokerExcel`) in `en`/`ar`. `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (910 tests) green.
- **Not done**: no live-browser verification of the new PortfolioDetailPage badge this sprint (session has no browser); reviewed by reading the exact render path the existing "Matches broker" cell already exercises, plus a new automated UI test exercising the same path.

### Real bug found via user report: ACAMD still showed "Closed — needs corroborating evidence"

User-reported: a ticker (ACAMD) whose entire history came from the official broker Excel export still showed the full "Closed — needs corroborating evidence" / "Closes this gap: Orders History" / "Also works: a Broker Statement" recovery-plan banner on Import, after all three prior sprints' fixes. Traced per the user's explicit request (source files, functions, why the previous fixes didn't cover this path, root cause, fix) before touching any code.

**Root cause**: `ImportPage.tsx`'s own `tickerMatchStatuses` computation (feeding `checkTickerMatch`/`completenessEngine.recoveryPlan`/the `MatchBadge`/`RecoveryPlanPanel` UI) computes `allPendingFromOfficialBrokerExcel` only from THIS BATCH's still-pending candidates (`remainingBuysAndSells`). ACAMD's rows had already been committed (in this session, via an auto-skipped exact-duplicate re-extraction of the same 3,000-share buy) — `remainingBuysAndSells.length === 0`, so the flag's `.length > 0 &&` guard made it vacuously false, and a genuinely closed (net-zero), fully-Excel-sourced position fell straight into `checkTickerMatch`'s pre-existing `closed-position`/no-corroboration branch, which asks for a screenshot.

**Why the three prior fixes (PRs #81–83) didn't cover it**: all three consistently patched the *pending-candidate* gate across `ImportPage.tsx`, `verificationEngine.ts`, and `reconciliation.ts`/`PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`. The one check that looks at a ticker's FULL committed history (`isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced`, added in PR #83) was only wired into `reconciliation.ts`/`PortfolioDetailPage.tsx` (the ongoing holdings page) — never into `ImportPage.tsx`'s own, separate `checkTickerMatch` call, which still only reasoned about this-session pending rows plus a bare share-count number from the provenance-blind legacy `Trade` entity.

**Fix**: `ImportPage.tsx` now fetches `repos.rawTransactions.getAll()` (same pattern as its existing `existingTrades`/`existingVerifications` fetches) and reuses `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` (already exported from `reconciliation.ts`) as a fallback — but only once nothing is left pending for that ticker (`remainingBuysAndSells.length === 0`), never as a blanket override while a fresh row from a DIFFERENT source is still sitting in the batch. Caught and fixed this exact boundary case myself before shipping: a naive "OR the historical check in unconditionally" version would have let a ticker's *unrelated* Excel-sourced past silently bypass verification for a brand-new, still-unverified screenshot-sourced buy — a new regression test (`ImportPage.brokerExcelNewRowStillVerifies.test.tsx`) locks in that this never happens.

- 2 new tests: `ImportPage.brokerExcelClosedPosition.test.tsx` (reproduces the exact ACAMD shape — closed position, zero remaining pending, full Excel-sourced history — verified to fail without the fix by temporarily reverting `ImportPage.tsx` and re-running) and `ImportPage.brokerExcelNewRowStillVerifies.test.tsx` (the boundary case above). 912 tests total. `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean.

### Second real bug found via user report (CLHO): the fix was in the write path, not the read path

User traced a second reproducible case after the ACAMD fix, with explicit instructions not to patch the specific ticker but to audit the full Import → Verify → Allocate → Commit → Closed lifecycle for where `official-broker-excel` provenance gets lost.

**Root cause, in the business logic, not the UI**: `TradeService.ts`'s `ensureSellFacts` — the fact-writer `recordSell` (called by `SellAllocationForm`, both ImportPage's own sell-allocation modal and PortfolioDetailPage's PendingExecution "Allocate sell" flow) always calls after every sell allocation — hardcoded `source: "manual"` on the `SellExecution` RawTransaction fact it writes, unconditionally, for every sell regardless of what document it actually came from. Since the Buy and Sell candidates are both already recorded correctly at *extraction* time (`recordImportedRawTransactions`, both tagged `official-broker-excel`), allocating the Sell wrote a **second**, wrongly-`manual`-sourced `SellExecution` fact describing the same real sell — `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced`'s "every live fact is Excel-sourced" check failed the instant that second fact existed, sending the now-closed ticker straight back into the legacy `closed-position`/no-corroboration path.

**Why the ACAMD fix didn't catch this**: that fix (and its regression test) only exercised the *read* side — `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` and `ImportPage.tsx`'s historical fallback — using hand-crafted RawTransaction facts, never actually driving a sell through the real `recordSell`/`ensureSellFacts` write path. The invariant was being violated at write time, which a read-side-only fix and test could never have caught.

**Why the fix can't just mirror `ensureBuyFact`'s dedupe-by-value approach**: `ensureSellFacts`'s own doc comment records that an *earlier* version tried exactly that (skip writing when a live fact matches by ticker/date/shares/price) and caused real data loss — two genuinely different same-day same-price sells silently merged into one, orphaning the second sell's allocations. Any fix had to avoid reintroducing that.

- **`TradeService.ts`**: `RecordSellInput` gained an optional `source?: RawTransactionSource` field (same pattern as its existing `transactionNumber`); `ensureSellFacts` now writes `source: input.source ?? "manual"` instead of hardcoding `"manual"` — no value-matching involved, so the coincidental-collision regression the doc comment warns about can't recur.
- **`SellAllocationForm.tsx`**: `initial` prop gained a `source` field, forwarded straight into `recordSell`'s input.
- **`ImportPage.tsx`**: passes `sellCandidate.candidate.source` through when opening the allocation modal. `PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`'s own `SellAllocationForm` usage (the `PendingExecution` "Allocate sell" flow) was deliberately left unchanged — `PendingExecution` carries no document-type field to thread through, and no `official-broker-excel` candidate ever reaches that path anymore (partial fills from this parser stopped setting `needsConfirmation` two sprints ago).
- 2 new tests in `TradeService.test.ts` (914 total): the fix (a sell recorded with `source: "official-broker-excel"` stamps that source on the fact, not "manual") and the invariant it must preserve (a sell recorded with no source still defaults to "manual" — a genuinely user-typed sell). Verified the new test actually fails without the fix by reverting the three source files and re-running before restoring them. `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean.

### Full architectural audit: every code path that could lose official-broker-excel provenance

User explicitly rejected another ticker-specific patch (after CLHO) and asked for a full audit of every code path capable of writing or resolving a Buy/Sell RawTransaction fact, since any ticker passing through a buggy path is affected regardless of name. No live browser/IndexedDB access exists in this session, so "scan the database" was reframed as "scan every fact-writing/fact-resolving code path" — the correct generalization, since a bug in a shared path affects every ticker that ever passes through it.

**Two systemic root causes found, both fixed with universal (non-ticker-specific) mechanisms:**
