1. **Provenance loss on sell allocation, properly this time.** The prior CLHO fix (threading an explicit `source` parameter through `RecordSellInput`/`SellAllocationForm`/`ImportPage.tsx`) worked but wasn't architectural enough — it required every future caller of `TradeService.recordSell` to remember to pass `source`, which `PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`'s own `SellAllocationForm` usage (the `PendingExecution` "Allocate sell" flow) never did. New `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact` (`rawTransactionFolds.ts`) makes `ensureSellFacts` ADOPT an already-existing, unclaimed `SellExecution` fact matching the sell's value (ticker/date/shares/price) — the one `recordImportedRawTransactions` already wrote at extraction time, correctly sourced — instead of depending on the caller to know/pass the right source at all. "Unclaimed" (no live `SellAllocationDecision` already points at it) is what makes this safe against the exact collision an earlier, cruder version of this same idea caused (two genuinely different same-value sells silently merging) — each sell's own decision claims its fact the moment it's recorded, so a second same-value sell correctly falls through to minting its own. The explicit `source` threading from the prior fix is kept as a fallback layer (used only when no adoptable fact exists at all), not removed.
2. **Provenance loss on ticker rename — found by the audit, never reported.** `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` read a fact's `payload.ticker` directly, but a fact's ticker is immutable — `TradeService.renameTickerEverywhere` (the "fix a misread ticker" feature) writes a separate `Correction` fact rather than editing in place (already correctly handled by `commitEngine.ts`'s existing, private `resolveCurrentTicker` fold, used elsewhere in the codebase but never here). Any Excel-sourced ticker ever renamed would have silently stopped being recognized as Excel-sourced under its new name. Fixed by extracting `resolveCurrentTicker` out of `commitEngine.ts` into the shared `rawTransactionFolds.ts` leaf module (avoiding a `reconciliation.ts` → `commitEngine.ts` → `verificationEngine.ts` → `reconciliation.ts` circular import) and using it in the provenance check.

**Audited and confirmed already safe, no change needed**: `ensureBuyFact`'s existing canonical-key + `otherTradeIds` dedup (Buy side never had this bug — it already adopts an extraction-time fact correctly); `ledgerProjection.ts`'s legacy-to-RawTransaction backfill path (already uses a proven count-based dedup, correctly labeled `"backfill"` — a real, distinct, non-Excel provenance for pre-migration data, not a bug); every other `createRawTransaction` call site in the codebase (`PortfolioAssignment`/`Retraction`/`Correction`/`CashAdjustment`/etc. — none of these write a `BuyExecution`/`SellExecution` fact, so none are in scope for this check at all).

**Audited and deliberately left out of scope, explicitly flagged rather than silently ignored**: `lotManager.ts`'s `recordSellTransaction` (TradesPage/TickerDetailPage's Lot Manager) also hardcodes `source: "manual"` unconditionally. Applying the same adoption mechanism there would be unsafe — Lot Manager's "record the execution now, allocate later" design means a sell can sit unallocated (and therefore unclaimed) for a while by construction, so "unclaimed" there would incorrectly mean "still pending" rather than "available to adopt," risking exactly the collision the fix elsewhere prevents. This is a real, separate gap but architecturally different from the Import → Verify → Allocate → Complete lifecycle actually reported, and isn't reachable from the Official Broker Excel importer's own review flow at all.

- **Files modified**: `rawTransactionFolds.ts` (new `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact`, moved-in `resolveCurrentTicker`), `TradeService.ts` (`ensureSellFacts` rewritten around the adoption mechanism), `commitEngine.ts` (removed its now-duplicate private `resolveCurrentTicker`), `reconciliation.ts` (`isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` folds through ticker corrections).
- 3 new tests (917 total): `TradeService.test.ts` — adopts a pre-existing candidate fact end-to-end even when the caller passes no `source` at all, and two coincidentally-identical-value sells never merge; `reconciliation.test.ts` — a renamed ticker is still recognized correctly under its new name (and no longer under its old one). Verified each new test fails without its corresponding fix by reverting and re-running before restoring. `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean (confirms no circular import was introduced by the `rawTransactionFolds.ts` extraction).
- **No ticker-specific logic introduced anywhere** — every change operates on generic value/claim/correction folds over the fact log, never a ticker name or ticker-specific branch.

### One-time data repair: the code fix alone doesn't heal data written before it

Direct, sharp follow-up question: do the previous architectural fixes retroactively repair data already written under the old buggy `ensureSellFacts`, or only future writes? Answer, confirmed by tracing the exact mechanics: **only future writes**. A sell already allocated before the fix left two live facts behind — the correctly-sourced extraction-time fact (permanently orphaned, unclaimed) and the wrongly-`"manual"`-sourced one the ledger's `SellAllocationDecision` actually references. `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` checks every live fact for a ticker, so the orphaned correct twin sitting there doesn't help — the ticker stays broken until something rewrites the decision. The code fix changes what happens on the *next* `recordSell` call; it has no way to reach back and fix a sell that was already recorded.

- **New `provenanceRepair.ts`**: `dryRunProvenanceRepair`/`applyProvenanceRepair`, same dry-run-first convention as the existing `ledgerRebuild.ts`/`RebuildLedgerPanel`. Detection is deliberately narrow and precise — only ever flags a `SellAllocationDecision` whose currently-referenced fact has `source: "manual"` (the old bug's exact, known signature, never any other value) where a different, still-unclaimed, non-`"manual"`-sourced twin exists for the identical value (reusing `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact` from the code fix itself). This can't touch a genuinely manual sell (Lot Manager, hand-typed) — those never have an unclaimed differently-sourced twin sitting around unless the same execution really was also recorded from an authoritative document, which is exactly the case worth fixing. The repair itself: retract the wrong fact and its stale decision, write a replacement decision with the *exact same* lot allocations pointing at the correct fact instead — which lots closed and how many shares never changes, only which fact the ledger resolves to. `applyProvenanceRepair` re-verifies each finding is still live immediately before acting (skips, never double-acts, if something else already changed the data between dry-run and apply).
- **New `ProvenanceRepairPanel.tsx`**, wired into `DataPage.tsx` alongside the existing Rebuild panel: Run Check → review the list → an explicit `confirm()` naming exactly how many sells are about to be repaired → Repair. Nothing is written until the user explicitly acts.
- 6 new tests (923 total) in `provenanceRepair.test.ts`: detects the exact corrupted-CLHO-shape fixture; correctly finds nothing for a genuinely manual sell with no twin; correctly finds nothing when the referenced fact is already correct; end-to-end repair (retractions land, replacement decision references the right fact and carries the same allocations, ticker becomes fully Excel-sourced afterward); never touches an unrelated ticker's facts; skips a finding whose underlying facts already changed since the dry-run (simulated via a concurrent retraction).
- **Verified live**: ran the dev server, navigated to `/data`, confirmed the new panel renders correctly (matching the existing Rebuild panel's styling) and "Run Check" works with zero console errors, correctly reporting "No affected sells found" against this session's empty database.
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite green.
- **Not done**: this migration exists in the app now but hasn't been run against any real user data — no such data is reachable from this session. The user needs to open the app, go to Data, and run it themselves once.

### Third real bug found via user report ("same problem, same conditions"): the ticker-resolution fix from the audit above wasn't applied consistently within its own PR

User reported the exact same "Closed — needs corroborating evidence" symptom recurring again, without naming a ticker — a direct test of whether the prior "full architectural audit" entry actually closed the gap. It hadn't, fully.

**Root cause**: `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact` (`rawTransactionFolds.ts`), written in the very same PR as the `resolveCurrentTicker` ticker-correction fold it depends on, read the candidate fact's `t.ticker` field **directly** instead of resolving it through `resolveCurrentTicker` — the identical bug class that same PR had just fixed in `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced`, but never applied to this sibling function. Net effect: any ticker whose extraction-time Sell candidate fact was written under a ticker string later corrected (e.g. an OCR misread fixed via `TradeService.renameTickerEverywhere`) would fail to be recognized as "already existing" during allocation — `ensureSellFacts` would fall through, mint a fresh `"manual"`-sourced fact for the resolved name, and orphan the correctly-sourced one, reproducing the exact bug the prior fix was supposed to eliminate for good.

The prior entry's audit claim that "`ensureBuyFact`'s existing canonical-key + `otherTradeIds` dedup ... Buy side never had this bug" was re-checked and was **wrong** — `ensureBuyFact`'s `liveMatch` lookup had the identical raw-`t.ticker`-read defect (it was just never exercised by the two reported tickers, so it hadn't yet surfaced as a symptom).

**Fix, applied to every fact-adoption/resolution site that reads a candidate's ticker, not just the one that happened to reproduce**:
1. `rawTransactionFolds.ts` — `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact` now resolves each candidate's ticker via `resolveCurrentTicker` before comparing, instead of reading `t.ticker` directly.
2. `TradeService.ts` — `ensureBuyFact`'s `liveMatch` lookup does the same.
3. `provenanceRepair.ts` — `dryRunProvenanceRepair` resolved `currentFact.ticker` directly as the search key it hands to `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact`; a wrongly-sourced fact written under a since-renamed ticker would search for its correct twin under the OLD name and never find it. Now resolves through `resolveCurrentTicker` first.

- **Files modified**: `rawTransactionFolds.ts`, `TradeService.ts`, `provenanceRepair.ts`.
- 6 new tests (928 total): `rawTransactionFolds.test.ts` (new file) — `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact` finds a candidate under its current, corrected ticker and no longer under the old one; `TradeService.test.ts` — `ensureBuyFact` end-to-end adopts a pre-existing Buy fact extracted under a ticker later renamed via a Correction; `provenanceRepair.test.ts` — `dryRunProvenanceRepair` finds the wrongly-sourced fact even when the whole corrupted fixture was written under a since-renamed ticker. Verified every new test fails without its corresponding fix (`git stash push` on the three fixed source files only, re-ran, confirmed all three failed, `git stash pop` to restore) before shipping.
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (928 tests) green.
- **No ticker-specific logic introduced anywhere** — all three fixes are the same generic "resolve through `resolveCurrentTicker` before comparing" change already established by the prior audit, applied to the two sibling call sites that were missed.
- **Lesson for future audits in this codebase**: when a shared helper (`resolveCurrentTicker`) is introduced to fix one call site, grep for every other place reading the same immutable field directly (`t.ticker`, `currentFact.ticker`, etc.) in the same change, not just the one call site the reported bug happened to touch — a sibling function written in the same PR is not automatically safe just because it looks similar.

### Reset All Data audit: `pendingExecutions` was never in the purge table list

User suspected "Reset All Data" (`DataPage.tsx` → `purgeAllData`) wasn't actually clearing every persistence layer, evidenced by a ticker's shares reappearing as "already recorded on the ledger" after a reset. Full inventory of every persistence location the app uses (all ten Dexie tables in `db.ts`, `localStorage` keys — `portfolio-os:import-session`, `portfolio-os:tracking-start-date`, `portfolio-os:language` — and a check for `sessionStorage`/Cache API/service-worker usage, of which there is none in this codebase).

**Confirmed defect**: `purge.ts`'s `allTables()` helper — the table list both `purgeAllData` and `purgeTickerData` clear/scope their transaction to — listed 10 tables but the schema (`db.ts`, version 4) has 11: `db.pendingExecutions` (unconfirmed partial-fill Buy/Sell executions held outside the Trade/TradeAllocation ledger, see `pendingExecutions.ts`) was missing from the list entirely. Neither "Reset All Data" nor per-ticker "Reset" ever deleted a single `PendingExecution` row, directly contradicting `purgeAllData`'s own doc comment ("erases everything... indistinguishable from a fresh install") and `purgeTickerData`'s ("leaving the app looking like the ticker was never imported").

**Traced, but ruled out, as the literal cause of the reported number**: the exact "{{existing}} already recorded on the ledger" ImportPage string (`importPage.mismatchArithmetic` et al. in `translations.ts`) is sourced from `matchStatus.existingRemainingShares`, computed live in `ImportPage.tsx` from `repos.trades.getAll()` → `db.trades`. `db.trades` *was* already in `allTables()` and is unconditionally `.clear()`'d — confirmed by both static tracing (`DexieTradeRepository.getAll()` is a direct `toArray()` passthrough, no caching layer) and by the existing `purgeAllData` test, which already asserted `db.trades.count()` is 0 afterward. So a surviving `db.trades` row is not the mechanism.

**What the `pendingExecutions` gap *does* cause, concretely reproduced**: `PortfolioDetailPage.tsx` reads `repos.pendingExecutions.getByPortfolio(id)` and renders any non-`"executed"` row as a live "Pending Execution" card. A per-ticker "Reset" (`purgeTickerData`, which — unlike "Reset All Data" — deliberately leaves the portfolio itself intact) previously left that ticker's own unconfirmed `PendingExecution` rows behind in the very same, still-existing portfolio; re-importing the same ticker afterward would resurface the stale card, looking exactly like "this ticker already has activity" even though the ticker's trades/facts had genuinely been erased. "Reset All Data" also leaked every `PendingExecution` row as permanently orphaned IndexedDB garbage (pointing at a deleted `portfolioId`) — invisible today only because portfolio ids are randomly generated and never reused, not because the data was actually gone.

**Fix**: added `db.pendingExecutions` to `allTables()` (so `purgeAllData` clears it and `purgeTickerData`'s transaction is correctly scoped to it too); `purgeTickerData` now also collects and `bulkDelete`s every `PendingExecution` row matching the ticker, the same pattern already used for every other per-ticker table.

- **Files modified**: `purge.ts` only.
- 2 new assertions in the existing `purge.test.ts` fixtures (seeded one `PendingExecution` per ticker): `purgeTickerData` — the reset ticker's pending execution is gone, the untouched ticker's survives; `purgeAllData` — `db.pendingExecutions.count()` is 0 afterward. Verified both fail without the fix (`git stash` on `purge.ts` only, re-ran, confirmed both failed with the stale row still present, restored).
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (928 tests) green.
- **Not fully closed**: any `PendingExecution` row already orphaned by a *past* "Reset All Data" (before this fix) has no `portfolioId` left to be found by — it's unreachable through the app's own UI today (nothing queries `pendingExecutions` unscoped by portfolio) and is not user-financial-data-visible, so no data-repair migration was written for it; it's inert IndexedDB bloat, not a correctness bug once cleaned going forward. If this needs literal disk reclaiming for a specific affected user, the `pendingExecutions` table can be inspected directly via the browser's DevTools IndexedDB panel.

### Architectural inconsistency found: an open official-broker-excel position could still trip a "needs corroboration"-shaped banner

User pressed on a direct contradiction: the broker-record trust policy (PRs #81–89) says Official Broker Excel is the Single Source of Truth for a ticker's current position — yet asked whether an open Excel-sourced position could still enter the "Needs broker screenshot" workflow. It could, through a path none of the prior ACAMD/CLHO/audit fixes touched.

**Root cause**: `constraintValidation.ts`'s Constraint Validation Layer — introduced in an earlier sprint as an independent "Global Inventory Check" sitting *above* `checkTickerMatch`, deliberately separating "do the facts add up" from "why might they not" — recomputed its own calculated-vs-Holdings comparison (`evaluateInventoryConstraint`) directly from `verifiedUnits` (a "My Position" screenshot's unit count), with **no awareness of `checkTickerMatch`'s own `reason`/trust-tier decision at all**. `checkTickerMatch` already special-cases `"broker-excel-verified"` — a disagreeing screenshot is surfaced only as a non-blocking `secondaryMismatch`, never treated as a real discrepancy — but that special case lived entirely inside `checkTickerMatch`; `evaluateInventoryConstraint` re-derived the identical comparison from scratch and had no way to know a `verifiedUnits` value it was handed came from a screenshot the trust policy had already ruled non-authoritative for that specific ticker. So: an Excel-sourced OPEN position with no screenshot at all was fine (no Holdings value to compare against). An Excel-sourced OPEN position *with* a genuinely agreeing screenshot was also fine. But an Excel-sourced OPEN position with a **disagreeing** screenshot — exactly the scenario the trust policy exists to resolve — tripped a rose "Contradiction" banner (`ImportPage`'s `ConstraintReportPanel`) with diagnosis hypotheses like "an extra or duplicate Buy transaction is likely already on the ledger," functionally reintroducing the exact "needs corroborating evidence" framing the policy was supposed to eliminate. `matched` itself stayed `true` (Confirm still worked — `checkTickerMatch`'s own decision was never overridden), but the banner visibly told the user their authoritative Excel data was in question.

**Why the prior fixes (PRs #83, #86) didn't cover this**: those touched `checkTickerMatch`, `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced`, `reconcilePositions`, and the fact-adoption path — every place that decides *whether* a ticker is Excel-verified. None of them touched `constraintValidation.ts`, a structurally separate layer that was built to consume `checkTickerMatch`'s output as inert "facts" (per its own doc comment) but in practice re-derived one of the same judgments (calculated vs. Holdings) independently, without importing the judgment itself.

**Also audited**: `ledgerRebuild.ts`'s `diffHoldings` (the "Rebuild Ledger" dry-run tool on the Data page) performs the exact same calculated-vs-Holdings comparison via the same `buildInventoryFacts`/`evaluateInventoryConstraint` pair, but reconstructs its inputs purely from `Upload.candidates` — it never calls `checkTickerMatch` and `CanonicalTrade` (its own merged-row type) doesn't currently retain a `source` field at all. **Deliberately left unfixed and explicitly flagged, not silently ignored**: giving it the same exemption would require threading `source`/trust-tier through `canonicalizeTradeEntries`' row-merging logic (which today collapses several candidates, possibly of different sources, into one `CanonicalTrade` with no "which source wins" rule defined) — a real, separate piece of work, not a one-line consequence of this fix. A ticker's `Import` and `Data → Rebuild Ledger` experiences can therefore still disagree until that's done.

**Fix**: `InventoryFacts` gained a `brokerExcelVerified: boolean` field, set by `buildInventoryFacts` from `status.reason === "broker-excel-verified"` (the same field `checkTickerMatch`/`TickerStatus` already carry — both call sites, `ImportPage.tsx` and `verificationEngine.ts`'s `buildConstraintReport`, needed zero changes; `tsc` confirmed their existing argument shapes already satisfy the widened type). `evaluateInventoryConstraint` now exempts `brokerExcelVerified` tickers from the Holdings comparison entirely, the same way it already exempts a closed position — checked *before* the `holdingsRemaining` check, not only when undefined, since the whole point is to stop a *present*, disagreeing screenshot from being treated as grounds for distrust.

- **Files modified**: `constraintValidation.ts` only.
- 1 new test in `constraintValidation.test.ts`: a `checkTickerMatch`-real (not hand-built) `"broker-excel-verified"` status with a disagreeing `verifiedUnits` produces zero contradictions. Verified it fails without the fix (`git stash` on `constraintValidation.ts` only, re-ran, confirmed failure, restored).
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (929 tests) green.
- **No ticker-specific logic introduced** — the exemption is keyed purely on `checkTickerMatch`'s own generic `reason` field, identical in shape to the existing `closed` exemption.

### Rebuild Ledger pipeline migrated onto the same trust-policy implementation as Import

User rejected the previous entry's "deliberately left unfixed" close on `ledgerRebuild.ts` outright: two pipelines producing different business decisions for the same input is exactly the "two independent implementations of one policy" defect this whole thread of fixes has been about, not a lower-priority follow-up. Required: one shared trust-policy implementation, provenance preserved through Rebuild's own canonicalization, and Rebuild's Holdings/verification decision provably identical to Import's for the same ticker/source.

**What was actually wrong**: `CanonicalTrade` (Rebuild's own canonical-execution row, built from `Upload.candidates`) never recorded which document type each execution was read from. `diffHoldings` therefore had no provenance to make a trust decision with at all, and fell back to a raw calculated-vs-Holdings comparison — the same naive comparison the *previous* entry fixed inside `constraintValidation.ts`, but Rebuild never even reached that fixed code path with real trust-tier information; it always passed a bare `{ netShares, verifiedUnits }` with no `reason`, so `evaluateInventoryConstraint`'s `brokerExcelVerified` exemption was structurally unreachable from Rebuild. An Official-Broker-Excel ticker with a disagreeing verification screenshot would show "Verified" via Import but a "Holdings Mismatch" via Data → Rebuild Ledger for the exact same underlying facts.

**Fix — provenance preserved, decision shared, nothing duplicated**:
1. `CanonicalTrade` gained a `source: ParsedTradeCandidate["source"]` field, set directly from the surviving entry's own candidate (`e.candidate.source`) inside `canonicalizeTradeEntries`. Confirmed safe against the existing cross-source-merge machinery: `completeCandidateFieldsFromSiblings` only ever borrows `fees`/`taxes`/`time`/`transactionNumber` from a sibling, never `source` itself, and `suggestDuplicatePendingCandidateKeysToDelete` already has a deterministic "which one survives" rule (an invoice-sourced read always wins the survivor slot over a same-signature sibling) — so `.source` on a canonical row is always well-defined and reproducible, never an arbitrary/ambiguous merge.
2. `diffHoldings` no longer builds `InventoryFacts` directly from a hand-rolled `{ netShares, verifiedUnits }`. It now groups canonical Buy/Sell rows by ticker, derives `allPendingFromOfficialBrokerExcel`/`allPendingFromInvoice` from `.source` (the exact same boolean shape Import's own `checkTickerMatch` callers already compute), and calls **`checkTickerMatch` itself** — the identical function `ImportPage.tsx` and `verificationEngine.ts` call — before building `InventoryFacts` from its result. There is now exactly one function in this codebase that decides "does this ticker need a Holdings screenshot," and both pipelines call it.
3. Verified this produces identical decisions for identical inputs: an Official-Broker-Excel-sourced ticker with a disagreeing screenshot is no longer flagged by Rebuild, matching Import exactly; a genuinely non-Excel-sourced ticker with a real disagreement is still flagged by both, unchanged; an invoice-sourced ticker is exempted only when no screenshot exists at all (never against a disagreeing one) — the same asymmetry `checkTickerMatch` already enforces for Import, now reached by Rebuild for the first time too.

**Deliberately not extended to `allPendingSelfVerified`/`allPendingOrderConfirmed`** (cross-source corroboration and Orders-timeline confirmation): those require pairing signals (`findCrossSourceVerifiedKeys`, order-evidence matching against `ParsedOrderEvidence`) that Rebuild's Upload-based world doesn't currently wire into `CanonicalTrade` at all. Extending to these would be additional, separate plumbing, not a consequence of provenance now existing on `CanonicalTrade` — flagged here rather than silently left out again. Only `official-broker-excel` and `invoice` are exempted from Rebuild's Holdings check today, matching exactly what provenance Rebuild now actually carries.

- **Files modified**: `ledgerRebuild.ts` only (no other file needed to change — `constraintValidation.ts`'s `brokerExcelVerified` exemption from the previous entry already does the actual work once handed a real `reason`).
- 4 new tests in `ledgerRebuild.test.ts`: an Official-Broker-Excel-sourced ticker with a disagreeing screenshot produces zero Holdings mismatches; a non-Excel-sourced ticker with a genuine disagreement is still flagged (proves the fix doesn't over-suppress); an invoice-sourced ticker with no screenshot at all is exempted; a cross-source merge (statement + invoice, same execution) preserves the invoice donor's source on the surviving canonical row, per the same survivor rule `suggestDuplicatePendingCandidateKeysToDelete` already implements. Verified all four fail without the fix (`git stash` on `ledgerRebuild.ts` only, re-ran, confirmed failure, restored) — the two that don't touch the new `source` field (companyName-mismatch, price-mismatch etc.) were unaffected, confirming no regression in the untouched diff logic.
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean (no circular import from `ledgerRebuild.ts` importing `checkTickerMatch` — `importVerification.ts` remains a dependency-free leaf module); full suite (933 tests) green.
- **One authoritative provenance model, one verification model**: `CanonicalTrade.source` is Rebuild's own provenance field (the RawTransaction-based pipeline already has its own, `RawTransaction.source` — these are deliberately two DIFFERENT data models, since Rebuild operates over `Upload` and Import/RawTransaction operate over the fact log; unifying the *data* layer is a separate, larger migration, not what was asked here), but there is now exactly one function — `checkTickerMatch` — that turns provenance into a trust decision, called by both.

### Full architectural audit: every verification workflow that could still classify an official-broker-excel ticker as needing external corroboration

User rejected ticker-by-ticker investigation entirely and demanded a business-rule audit: enumerate every code path capable of producing a "needs broker screenshot"/"needs corroborating evidence"/"Orders History required" verdict for a ticker whose complete history is official-broker-excel-sourced, and replace every independent decision with the one shared trust-policy function. Full inventory below, one row per code path found by grepping for the UI strings themselves (`matchNeedsScreenshot`, `matchClosedNeedsEvidence`, `recoveryPlanTitle`, `colVerification`, `quantityMismatch`, etc.) and tracing each backward to its source, not by searching for any ticker name.

| # | Source file / function | Trigger condition | Bypass mechanism | Missing data | Category | Status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | `constraintValidation.ts` `evaluateInventoryConstraint` | Open position, `verifiedUnits` disagrees with calculated remaining | Recomputed calculated-vs-Holdings independently of `checkTickerMatch`'s `reason` | The ticker's trust-tier (`reason`) was never threaded into `InventoryFacts` | Reconciliation / read-side | **Fixed (prior PR #90)** |
| 2 | `ledgerRebuild.ts` `diffHoldings` | Same as #1, reached via Data → Rebuild Ledger instead of Import | `CanonicalTrade` carried no provenance at all; fell back to a raw comparison | `.source` on each canonical row | Rebuild | **Fixed (prior PR #91)** |
| 3 | `ImportPage.tsx` `tickerMatchStatuses` (via `initialDataLoaded`) | A ticker with nothing pending this session (fully committed, e.g. ACAMD/CLHO shape), rendered while `existingRawTransactionsRaw`'s own `useLiveQuery` hasn't resolved yet but four *other* independent `useLiveQuery` reads already have | `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` was fed the default-empty `[]` a not-yet-loaded query reads as, since `existingRawTransactionsRaw` was missing from the `initialDataLoaded` readiness gate | `existingRawTransactionsRaw !== undefined` in the readiness check | **UI / read-side race** — real decision logic (`checkTickerMatch`) was already correct; it was fed transiently-incomplete data | **Fixed this entry** |
| 4 | `reconciliation.ts` `reconcilePositions` | Any future caller that omits the `rawTransactions` argument | `rawTransactions: RawTransaction[] = []` was an optional, defaulted parameter — an omitted argument silently reads as "no ticker is Excel-sourced" with no compiler or runtime signal | Nothing missing today (`PortfolioDetailPage.tsx`, the only current caller, already passes it correctly) — the defect was that the *type signature* permitted a future caller not to | **Latent architectural risk**, not a live bug | **Hardened this entry** (parameter made required) |
| 5 | `completenessEngine.ts` `classify`/`recoveryPlan` | Any ticker | N/A — already maps `"broker-excel-verified"` → `"Complete"`, `recoveryPlan` returns `undefined` for anything not `"Incomplete"` | — | Read-side | **Audited, already correct** |
| 6 | `verificationEngine.ts` `computeVerification` (per-ticker `tickerReason` and per-transaction `verdict`) | Any ticker/transaction | N/A — both derive from `checkTickerMatch`'s own `matched`/`reason`, and `entries` is built from the FULL live RawTransaction history in scope, not a restricted "this batch only" set | — | Read-side | **Audited, already correct** |
| 7 | `PortfolioDetailPage.tsx` reconciliation table (`quantityMismatch`/`quantityShortfall`/`verificationStale`) | Any ticker | N/A — `reconcilePositions` already skips generating a row at all for a fully-Excel-sourced ticker (row #1's fix), and the one caller passes `rawTransactions` correctly | — | Reconciliation / UI | **Audited, already correct** |
| 8 | `pendingExecutions.ts` (STES "Needs Confirmation" invoice workflow) | A partial-fill Buy candidate with `needsConfirmation: true` | N/A — `ThndrOrdersWorkbookParser.ts` never sets `needsConfirmation` on an official-broker-excel candidate by design; this workflow is structurally unreachable for Excel-sourced rows | — | Write-side | **Audited, already correct** |
| 9 | `evidenceGraph.ts`/`evidenceIntelligence.ts`/`canonicalTransaction.ts` | Any ticker | N/A — all three call `verifyTicker`/`verifyAllDetailed` (the shared engine), and none is imported by any presentation-layer file today | — | Dormant (no UI entry point) | **Audited, not reachable** |
| 10 | `systemValidation.ts` | Any ticker | N/A — not imported by any presentation-layer file | — | Dormant (no UI entry point) | **Audited, not reachable** |
| 11 | `TickerDetailPage.tsx`/`TradesPage.tsx`/`DashboardPage.tsx`/other pages | — | N/A — none of these pages read verification/reconciliation state at all | — | UI | **Audited, no corroboration workflow exists here** |

**Root cause of #3 (the one live bug)**: `ImportPage.tsx` reads `portfolios`/`trades`/`allocations`/`verifications`/`timeline`/`rawTransactions` via six independent `useLiveQuery` calls, each resolving on its own schedule. `initialDataLoaded` — the readiness gate already used to disable the Confirm button and gate a couple of auto-skip effects — never included `existingRawTransactionsRaw`, the one query `tickerMatchStatuses`' historical-fallback branch (`isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced`, added by the ACAMD fix, PR #84) actually depends on. A ticker with nothing pending this session (already fully committed) depends *entirely* on that one query; while it's still resolving but every other query has already settled, the ticker read as `"closed-position"`/`"no-verification"` — exactly the reported symptom — purely from being fed a transiently-empty array, not from any flaw in `checkTickerMatch` itself. This is why the fix in PR #84 "worked" in every manual test (data had already settled by the time a human looked) yet the bug kept recurring for the same user under real load-timing conditions.

**Fix, scoped precisely to the actual gap**:
1. `initialDataLoaded` now includes `existingRawTransactionsRaw !== undefined`.
2. `tickerMatchStatuses` skips adding a map entry for a ticker whose verdict depends on the historical fallback (`remainingBuysAndSells.length === 0`) while that one query is still `undefined` — rather than computing a wrong verdict from a default-empty read. A ticker with real pending rows this batch never touches this path at all (its verdict never depends on `existingRawTransactions`), so it's completely unaffected — confirmed by the existing Statement-Aggregate end-to-end test, which explicitly relies on a different ticker's badges rendering *before* all ledger data has settled.
3. `MatchBadge` now renders a neutral "Checking…" chip for an absent map entry, replacing the old fallback that silently reused the "Needs broker screenshot" copy for both "genuinely no verification" and "no verdict yet" — the exact conflation that made the race user-visible as a false corroboration demand instead of an honest loading state.

An earlier, broader attempt at this fix (hiding the entire ticker-card list behind `initialDataLoaded`) was tried and rejected: it broke a real, deliberate product behavior (a different ticker's cross-source-confirmation badges are meant to render progressively, independent of ledger-data readiness) — caught by the existing `ImportPage.aggregateStatement.test.tsx` failing. The shipped fix is narrower, scoped only to the one ticker-classification path that actually depends on the slow query.

- **Files modified**: `ImportPage.tsx` (`initialDataLoaded`, `tickerMatchStatuses`, `MatchBadge`), `translations.ts` (new `importPage.matchChecking` key, en + ar), `reconciliation.ts` (`rawTransactions` parameter hardening), `reconciliation.test.ts` (updated call sites).
- 1 new test file, `ImportPage.brokerExcelLoadRace.test.tsx`: renders ImportPage with `rawTransactions.getAll()` deliberately held pending while every other query resolves, and asserts the ACAMD-shaped ticker never shows "Closed — needs corroborating evidence" during that window, settling to "Fully matched" once the query resolves. Verified this test fails without the fix (`git stash` on `ImportPage.tsx` only, re-ran, confirmed the exact bad badge rendered, restored) — a genuine, non-manual-timing-dependent reproduction of the real recurring symptom, unlike every prior fix in this file's history which could only be confirmed by inspection or by the app happening to settle before a human looked.
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (934 tests) green.
- **No ticker-specific logic introduced anywhere.**
- **Acceptance criteria verified**: open/closed position (row #3's fix and rows #1/#2's prior fixes cover both), pending/committed state (the historical-fallback branch this entry hardens IS the "committed, nothing pending" case), re-import/duplicate detection (unaffected — never depends on the slow query at all once real pending rows exist), allocation (covered by the prior `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact`/`ensureBuyFact` fixes), ledger rebuild (row #2), portfolio reconciliation (row #7), inventory validation (row #1), every UI entry point (rows #9–11 confirm no other page has a corroboration workflow to bypass at all).

### A NEW race, in the same file, found after the prior one was fixed: the auto-skip-duplicate effect vs. its own in-flight commit

User reported the exact same symptom again (ARCC — a still-open, single-Buy Excel-sourced ticker; CLHO — a fully-closed one) immediately after confirming, i.e. after the load-race fix above had already shipped. Investigated by actually reproducing the real user flow end-to-end in a real browser against real IndexedDB (a synthetic "Your Orders" workbook, `npm run dev` + Playwright), not by static reading — every one of the 11 rows in the prior "full architectural audit" table was individually re-checked first and all still held, so this had to be a genuinely new path.

**Root cause, found by instrumenting the real run**: `ImportPage`'s "auto-skip an exact ledger duplicate" `useEffect` (the one keyed off `existingTrades`/`existingAllocations` — introduced to close the "already-fully-recorded ticker stuck on Mismatch forever" deadlock, see the reconciliation-investigation entry earlier in this log) races the very commit it is watching. `commitTickerGroup`'s `addBuyCandidate` → `recordBuy` saves the `Trade` several `await`s (portfolio save, timeline save) before it ever calls `ensureBuyFact` and before the caller updates `addedKeys`. Dexie's real `useLiveQuery` observes that intermediate `Trade` write immediately — genuine IndexedDB reactivity a hand-mocked, non-Dexie `repos` object can't reproduce, which is exactly why every prior regression test for this file's race bugs (including this sprint's new one) had to be re-pointed at real Dexie repositories backed by `fake-indexeddb` rather than the usual plain-object `vi.mock`. In that window, the candidate looks like "not yet added, and now duplicates an existing trade" — the trade its OWN commit just wrote — so the effect marks it skipped and retracts its RawTransaction fact. `ensureBuyFact` then finds no live fact left to adopt and mints a brand-new one hardcoded to `source: "manual"`, permanently destroying the ticker's official-broker-excel provenance the instant it's confirmed. The identical shape exists on the Sell side (`SellAllocationForm`'s submission → `recordSell`, used by both `ImportPage`'s own "Allocate Sell" and `PortfolioDetailPage`), which is why CLHO (closes via a Sell) reproduced too, not just ARCC (Buy-only).

**Why the prior audit's 11-row table didn't catch this**: every row there asked "does some code path re-derive the trust decision independently of `checkTickerMatch`" — the actual defect here is upstream of that question entirely: it corrupts the *input data* (`RawTransaction.source`) that `checkTickerMatch`/`isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` correctly read afterward. `checkTickerMatch` itself was never wrong in this run — it faithfully reported "no-verification"/"closed-position" for a ticker whose fact log had, moments earlier, actually lost its Excel provenance to a write-time race. A read-side audit structurally cannot find a write-side data-corruption bug.

**Fix**: excluded `inFlightKeys` (the module-level `Set` `commitTickerGroup`'s own three loops already use as a reentrancy guard) from the auto-skip-duplicate effect's candidate pool, plus the statement-aggregate auto-skip effect right below it for the same reason. `inFlightKeys` only covers `commitTickerGroup`'s three loops, not `SellAllocationForm`'s modal-driven submission, so the exact-duplicate effect also excludes `sellCandidate?.key` for as long as that modal is open (safe: nothing else can add that key while its own allocation modal is up).

- **Files modified**: `ImportPage.tsx` only (both auto-skip `useEffect`s).
- 1 new test file, `ImportPage.inFlightDuplicateRace.test.tsx`: wires up **real** Dexie repositories (`fake-indexeddb`, already a global test dependency via `src/infrastructure/db/test-setup.ts`) behind `@presentation/lib/data` instead of the usual hand-mocked plain-object `repos`, seeds one official-broker-excel BUY candidate for ARCC (with its extraction-time RawTransaction fact already on file, matching what `recordImportedRawTransactions` writes in the real app), clicks the real "Confirm ARCC" button, and asserts it settles to "Fully matched" with zero "Needs broker screenshot"/"Closes this gap" text and exactly one live `BuyExecution` fact still sourced `official-broker-excel`. Verified this test fails without the fix (temporarily removed the `inFlightKeys`/`sellCandidate` exclusion, re-ran, confirmed the exact bad badge path and a second `source: "manual"` fact, restored) — and separately reproduced/fixed the same scenario against the real running dev server end-to-end with Playwright (screenshots: ARCC and CLHO both reach "Fully matched" after Confirm + Allocate Sell, zero gap badges; the Portfolio Detail Holdings table shows no Verification-mismatch column for ARCC at all; the underlying fact log stays 100% `official-broker-excel` for every row).
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (935 tests) green.
- **No ticker-specific logic introduced** — the exclusion is keyed purely on the same generic `inFlightKeys`/`sellCandidate` state every other reentrancy guard in this file already uses.
- **Lesson for future audits in this file**: a "does the decision function get bypassed" audit (like the 11-row table above) is necessary but not sufficient — this codebase's two-phase Import workflow reads reactive Dexie state (`existingTrades`/`existingAllocations`) inside `useEffect`s that run *during* the very commit they're meant to police, and any such effect needs the same `inFlightKeys`-style reentrancy guard `commitTickerGroup` already established, not just a correct filter over already-settled state. Grep for every `useEffect` in `ImportPage.tsx` keyed off `existingTrades`/`existingAllocations`/`existingRawTransactions` before declaring this class of bug closed again.

### A THIRD, independent race in the same investigation: two Buys of the same ticker in one batch, found while stress-testing generality

User explicitly required proof this class of fix isn't ticker-specific — pushed back on the ARCC/CLHO-only verification and asked for confirmation across every ticker shape. Stress-tested the fix above against tickers the original report never mentioned: a single-Buy-then-Sell close (a second ticker, unrelated symbol), and — the one that broke — a ticker with **two separate Buy candidates in the same import batch** (a very ordinary real shape: buying the same stock twice). Confirming it produced an actually-corrupted ledger, not just a bad badge: a duplicate `Trade` row for the second Buy (double-counting real shares — 2000 shown instead of 1500) alongside the same lost-provenance symptom.

**Root cause, found the same way (real browser + real IndexedDB + call-site instrumentation)**: `ensureBuyFact`/`ensureSellFacts` (`TradeService.ts`), once they adopt or create a fact, called the TICKER-WIDE `assignPortfolio` — "assign every still-unassigned live fact for this ticker" — instead of assigning just the one fact they were handling. `commitTickerGroup` processes a ticker's Buys sequentially (one `recordBuy` at a time, guarded by `inFlightKeys`), but the FIRST Buy's own `assignPortfolio` call, fired from deep inside `ensureBuyFact`, swept up the SECOND Buy's still-unprocessed fact too — it looked exactly like a genuine assignment gap from `assignPortfolio`'s own ticker-wide vantage point, and `inFlightKeys` (a presentation-layer, `ImportPage.tsx`-only concept) has no reach into `commitEngine.ts`/`TradeService.ts` to stop it. Assigning a fact reactively fires `appendAndMaybeCommit`'s own `shouldCommit`/`commitTicker` trigger — a SEPARATE commit pathway from `recordBuy` — which materialized a legacy Trade for the second Buy straight from the raw fact via `projectLegacyTicker`, BEFORE that Buy's own `recordBuy` call had even started. That phantom Trade then raced the second Buy's genuine `recordBuy` moments later: two Trade rows for one real execution, and the genuine candidate's own fact got auto-skipped by `ImportPage.tsx`'s (now otherwise-fixed) duplicate-effect as an apparent "exact duplicate" of the phantom Trade it should never have had to compete with. Confirmed this is unrelated to (and pre-dates) the previous entry's own fix — moving `commitTickerGroup`'s blanket `assignPortfolio` call to run after its own loops (tried first) made zero difference, since `ensureBuyFact`'s OWN internal call was the actual trigger, a completely different call site in a different layer.

**Why the prior two fixes/audits didn't catch this**: both were scoped to `ImportPage.tsx`'s own React effects — genuine fixes for genuine bugs, but neither touched `commitEngine.ts`/`TradeService.ts`, where this one actually lives. The 11-row audit table's own framing ("does some code path re-derive the trust decision independently of `checkTickerMatch`") doesn't cover this either, for the same reason the second entry's defect evaded it: this is a write-time data race between two independent commit pathways (the legacy `recordBuy` flow and the new architecture's reactive `commitTicker` trigger), not a read-side policy bypass.

**Fix**: added `assignPortfolioToFact` (`commitEngine.ts`) — a single-target counterpart to the ticker-wide `assignPortfolio`, assigning exactly one fact (idempotent: no-ops if already assigned or retracted) — and switched both `ensureBuyFact` and `ensureSellFacts`' adopt-branch calls to it. `assignPortfolio` itself is untouched and still used exactly where a ticker-wide sweep is actually correct: `setTickerPortfolio`'s explicit dropdown pick, and `commitTickerGroup`'s own end-of-function catch-all (for dividends/verifications, which never self-assign).

- **Files modified**: `commitEngine.ts` (new `assignPortfolioToFact`), `TradeService.ts` (`ensureBuyFact`/`ensureSellFacts` switched to it).
- 1 new test file, `ImportPage.multiBuySameTickerRace.test.tsx`: same real-Dexie harness as the previous entry's test, seeds TWO official-broker-excel Buy candidates for one ticker (ORWE, 1000 + 500 shares) with both extraction-time facts already on file, clicks the real "Confirm ORWE" button, and asserts exactly 2 live `BuyExecution` facts (both still `official-broker-excel`) and exactly 2 Trade rows totaling 1500 shares — never a phantom third row. Verified this test fails without the fix (temporarily reverted `ensureBuyFact`'s call back to the ticker-wide `assignPortfolio`, re-ran, confirmed 3 Trade rows instead of 2, restored) — and separately reproduced/fixed the same scenario end-to-end against the real running dev server with Playwright, including a combined 4-ticker batch (a single-Buy open position, a Buy+Sell closed position, a two-Buy open position, and a second Buy+Sell closed position, all four different symbols) that reaches "Fully matched" for every ticker with zero gap badges and a fact log 100% `official-broker-excel`.
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (936 tests) green.
- **No ticker-specific logic introduced** — `assignPortfolioToFact` is keyed purely on a fact id, and both call sites already had that id (`liveMatch.id`/`sellExecutionId`) in scope before this fix; nothing ticker-specific was added anywhere.
- **Generality now covered across every shape actually tested**: single Buy/open, Buy+Sell/closed, multiple Buys/same ticker/same batch/open — all four combinations across four distinct tickers in one batch, plus the original ARCC/CLHO pair, all verified gap-free in both the automated suite and a live browser run. A ticker with multiple Sells in one batch was not separately stress-tested (the fix is symmetric — `ensureSellFacts` got the identical `assignPortfolioToFact` swap — but this specific shape wasn't driven end-to-end); flagged rather than silently assumed.

### A FOURTH shape in the same recurring bug family: an exact-duplicate Excel upload upgrading a LOWER-authority existing fact, not adopting/racing an equal one

User reported the exact same "Needs broker screenshot" symptom yet again — ABUK, a still-open position (27 shares, `Opening 27 + Buy 0 − Sell 0`) — after every fix above had already shipped, insisting the whole point of uploading the broker's official Excel export is that it should never need any further confirmation. Unlike the three prior entries (all races between two `official-broker-excel`-sourced writes, or between a write and the read watching it), ABUK's shape is different: its 27 shares were recorded manually (`source: "manual"`) *before* any document ever confirmed them, and the newly-uploaded Excel row is an exact duplicate (same ticker/date/shares/price) of that pre-existing manual trade — no race involved, reproducible on every run.

**Root cause**: the exact-duplicate auto-skip effect (`ImportPage.tsx`, the one this log's "reconciliation root-cause" and "in-flight race" entries above already touched) treats every exact duplicate identically — it always retracts the **newly-extracted** candidate's own RawTransaction fact via `retractRawTransactionKeys`, regardless of which fact actually carries the better evidence. For the ACAMD/ARCC/ORWE shapes above, the pre-existing fact was already `official-broker-excel` too, so retracting the new (redundant) one was harmless. For ABUK, the pre-existing fact is `manual` (Evidence Authority rank 0 — see `evidenceAuthority.ts`) and the newly-uploaded one is `official-broker-excel` (rank 5) — retracting the new one instead of the old one throws away the higher-authority document and leaves `manual` as the ticker's only surviving evidence, so `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` (and every reason chain that depends on it) never sees the Excel confirmation at all. The broker-record trust policy says an official Excel row "is authoritative... no 'My Position' screenshot... is ever requested for a transaction sourced from here" (`RawTransaction.ts`'s own doc comment on `"official-broker-excel"`) — silently deleting that row on sight is the opposite of that policy.

**Fix**: added `findLiveExecutionFact` (`rawTransactionFolds.ts`) — a plain ticker/date/shares/price lookup for the live Buy or Sell fact already describing one execution, with no "claimed" semantics (unlike the existing `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact`, which exists for a genuinely different question). The auto-skip effect now uses it, Buy-side only: when the new candidate's source outranks the existing fact's source (`higherAuthority`, `evidenceAuthority.ts`), it retracts the OLD fact and leaves the new one live — upgrading the ticker's provenance — instead of always retracting the new one. Sells are deliberately left on the prior behavior: a Sell's fact can already be claimed by a live `SellAllocationDecision`, and re-pointing that decision at a different fact is `provenanceRepair.ts`'s dedicated dry-run/apply job (built for the analogous old `ensureSellFacts` bug), not something to do unconditionally inside a live effect. `candidateSource` (`importRecording.ts`, the same `candidate.source ?? "statement"` fallback the fact-writer itself already uses) was exported instead of re-implemented, so the authority comparison reads the exact same source a real import would have written.

- **Files modified**: `rawTransactionFolds.ts` (new `findLiveExecutionFact`), `importRecording.ts` (`candidateSource` exported, unchanged behavior), `ImportPage.tsx` (the exact-duplicate auto-skip effect only).
- 1 new test file, `ImportPage.brokerExcelProvenanceUpgrade.test.tsx`: seeds a still-open ABUK trade (27 shares) backed by a `manual`-sourced fact, plus a pending `official-broker-excel` Buy candidate that exactly duplicates it (its own extraction-time fact already on file, matching real import ordering), and asserts the ticker settles to "Fully matched" with no "Needs broker screenshot"/"Closes this gap" text — and, more precisely, that the Retraction fact written targets the OLD manual fact's id, never the new Excel one.
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (937 tests) green.
- **No ticker-specific logic introduced** — the swap is keyed purely on `evidenceAuthority.ts`'s existing source ranking, already used elsewhere for the identical "which document's fields win" question.
- **Deliberately not generalized to Sells this sprint** — flagged rather than silently assumed; the analogous Sell-side shape (a duplicate Excel row for a manually-recorded sell) would need `provenanceRepair.ts`'s decision-re-pointing logic wired into a live effect, a larger change than this fix's scope.

### Closing the ABUK class of bug for good: Sells, plus two more real bugs only a live browser run could catch

User explicitly rejected any answer short of a real, screenshot-verified demonstration that this whole bug family is closed for every ticker shape, not just ABUK's — including "after allocating sell shares," the exact gap the prior entry flagged and deliberately deferred. Investigated by actually running the app (`npm run dev` + a scripted Playwright session against a real Chromium instance, real IndexedDB — not vitest's hand-mocked `repos`), seeding a portfolio with a manually-recorded open Buy (ABUK) and a manually-recorded Buy+Sell (HRHO), then uploading a synthetic official-broker-excel workbook that exactly duplicates both, plus a third, brand-new ticker (COMI) sourced entirely from the Excel with no prior history — the combination the unit-test suite alone could never exercise end-to-end.

**Bug 1 — Sells never got the upgrade.** Exactly as flagged: HRHO's Sell duplicate still read "Needs broker screenshot" after the Buy-side fix, because the auto-skip effect's authority-swap only checked `e.candidate.side !== "BUY"`. Fixed by adding `upgradeSellExecutionFact` (`provenanceRepair.ts`) — a live, single-swap counterpart to `applyProvenanceRepair`'s batch dry-run/apply flow: retract the old (lower-authority) `SellExecution` fact, and if a live `SellAllocationDecision` references it, retract that too and replace it with an identical one pointing at the new fact — never leaving a decision referencing a dead fact, the same swap the batch tool already performs for its own narrower ("manual"-source-only) historical bug.

**Bug 2 — the new fact never inherited the old fact's portfolio assignment, and `projectLegacyTicker` deleted the real Trade as "stale".** Found only by inspecting the actual `trades` IndexedDB table after the fix above — the Import page's own badges looked perfect ("Fully matched") while ABUK's and HRHO's real Holdings rows had silently vanished. Root cause: `commitEngine.appendAndMaybeCommit`'s Retraction branch re-triggers `commitTicker` for the retracted fact's (portfolio, ticker) the moment it's written; `relevantTradeTransactions` filters by `resolveCurrentPortfolioId`, and the newly-uploaded Excel fact (written by Import with no `portfolioId` at all — Import never assigns one, see `importRecording.ts`) had never been assigned to any portfolio, since being auto-skipped as a duplicate bypasses the normal Confirm-time `assignPortfolio` call entirely. So the retraction's own commit saw ZERO relevant transactions for that ticker, and `projectLegacyTicker` (`ledgerProjection.ts`) correctly-by-its-own-rules deleted the "stale" Trade row that no longer had any live fact backing it — a real, reproduced case of the evidence layer upgrading cleanly while the actual ledger silently lost the position. Fixed by exporting `resolveCurrentPortfolioId` (`commitEngine.ts`, previously private) and calling `assignPortfolioToFact(repos, newFactId, oldPortfolioId)` — awaited — BEFORE retracting the old fact, for both the Buy and Sell upgrade paths, so the surviving fact always carries the old one's portfolio assignment by the time the retraction's own commit runs.

**Why the existing regression test didn't catch bug 2 the same way**: `ImportPage.brokerExcelProvenanceUpgrade.test.tsx`'s hand-crafted single-ticker setup happens to also go through `setTickerPortfolio`'s own ticker-wide `assignPortfolio` sweep in a way that masks the gap in that harness's timing — the bug was only reliably reproducible under real browser/Dexie scheduling with multiple tickers in flight together, exactly why this investigation insisted on a live run instead of trusting the unit suite alone. The test was still strengthened (now also asserts the real `trades` table row survives with the correct `remainingShares`) as a permanent guard, even though it isn't a fully deterministic reproduction of this specific race in isolation.

**End-to-end verification performed** (screenshots taken, not just asserted): created portfolio "SMC" with a manual ABUK Buy (27 sh) and a manual HRHO Buy+Sell (100 sh, 40 sold via Lot Manager's Auto Allocate FIFO); uploaded a synthetic "Your Orders" workbook (built with the `xlsx` package, verified against `parseThndrOrdersWorkbook` first) containing exact-duplicate Buy rows for both, an exact-duplicate Sell row for HRHO, and a brand-new COMI Buy+Sell. Confirmed: (1) immediately after upload, before any manual action, ABUK and HRHO both collapse straight into "Fully matched" — "ABUK fully matched — 1 transaction", "HRHO fully matched — 2 transactions" — with zero "Needs broker screenshot"/"Closes this gap" text; (2) after confirming COMI's Buy and using the new "Smart Allocate" button for its Sell, all three tickers read "Every ticker has been fully matched and distributed — nothing left to confirm here."; (3) the Portfolio Detail Holdings table shows all three real positions (ABUK 27, HRHO 60, COMI 30 remaining) with correct cost basis/market value and no Verification-column warning; (4) the real `trades` IndexedDB table has exactly 3 rows with correct `remainingShares`; (5) Dashboard totals reconcile with cash spent/received across all five executions.

**Bug 3, found the same way, unrelated to the provenance-upgrade work — a fresh race in the just-shipped "Smart Allocate" button** (PR #94, `ImportPage.tsx`'s `smartAllocateSell`): clicking it for a genuinely NEW sell (COMI, nothing pre-existing) intermittently reproduced the exact ARCC/CLHO in-flight-commit race this file's history already fixed twice for `commitTickerGroup`'s three loops and `SellAllocationForm`'s submission — `recordSell` saves the TradeAllocation several awaits before `addedKeys` updates, and the exact-duplicate auto-skip effect's own `existingAllocations` dependency can see that in-flight write and mark the very candidate mid-commit as an apparent "duplicate" of the allocation its own call just created. `smartAllocateSell` was the one commit path never given the `inFlightKeys` reentrancy guard `commitTickerGroup`'s loops and `SellAllocationForm` already have. Fixed by adding the identical `inFlightKeys.add(entry.key)` / `finally { inFlightKeys.delete(entry.key) }` wrap already used everywhere else.

- **Files modified**: `provenanceRepair.ts` (new `upgradeSellExecutionFact`), `commitEngine.ts` (`resolveCurrentPortfolioId` exported, doc comment explaining why), `ImportPage.tsx` (auto-skip effect now assigns-then-retracts and handles both Buy/Sell; `smartAllocateSell` gained the `inFlightKeys` guard), `ImportPage.brokerExcelProvenanceUpgrade.test.tsx` (now also asserts the real Trade row survives with correct shares).
- `tsc --noEmit`/`arch:check` clean; full suite (937 tests) green.
- **No ticker-specific logic introduced anywhere** — every fix is keyed on generic mechanisms (`evidenceAuthority.ts`'s ranking, `resolveCurrentPortfolioId`'s fold, the same `inFlightKeys` Set every other reentrancy guard in this file already uses) and was verified across four distinct tickers (ABUK: Buy-only upgrade; HRHO: Buy+Sell upgrade; COMI: brand-new ticker, Buy confirm + Smart Allocate) in one combined batch, not one at a time.
- **Scope check against the user's demand** ("no confirmations/gaps/warnings after allocating sell shares, for every ticker, not one specific ticker"): verified for manually-recorded-then-Excel-confirmed Buys, manually-recorded-then-Excel-confirmed Sells (including the allocation-decision re-pointing), brand-new Excel-only tickers with a Sell requiring genuine allocation (both the manual "Allocate Sell" dialog's underlying engine and the new "Smart Allocate" one-click FIFO path), and the Portfolio Detail/Dashboard read surfaces downstream of Import. Not separately stress-tested: a ticker whose Sell duplicate would need re-pointing a decision that itself closes MULTIPLE lots (the single-lot HRHO shape was what reproduced and verified the fix); flagged rather than silently assumed covered.

### User re-reported the same symptom against their real broker Excel — found a real, deeper concurrency bug, only partially closed

User uploaded their real "Your Orders" export (766 candidates, ~150+ tickers, several thousand raw rows) and reported ACAMD ("Closed — needs corroborating evidence") and ADIB ("Needs broker screenshot") still failing after the fixes above shipped. Reproduced with their **actual file** (not synthetic data) against a real running dev server + real IndexedDB.

**First checked and ruled out**: the exact ABUK/HRHO shape (a pre-existing manually-recorded Buy/Sell duplicated by an exact-matching Excel row) for both ACAMD and ADIB specifically — both resolved correctly end-to-end (per-ticker Confirm + Smart Allocate), matching the prior fix's own verification. `purgeAllData` (Data page "Reset all") was also audited: it clears all 11 Dexie tables unconditionally, so no registered data can survive it; "Clear all" (Import page) only clears `uploads` + the local import session, which is fine once Reset all already emptied `rawTransactions`/`trades`.

**What actually reproduces it**: confirming *many* tickers close together — the batch "Confirm — Distribute to Portfolios" button commits every matched ticker via `Promise.all` (commitEngine's own single-ticket commit path never changed), and/or clicking "Smart Allocate" on several rows for the same ticker within a few seconds of each other. Under this load, `DexieCommittedLedgerRepository.commitTicker`'s `bulkDelete`+`bulkAdd` on `ledgerCache`/`allocationsCache` throws a Dexie `BulkError` — reproducible even *without* any of this session's own fixes involved (`ensureBuyFact failed ... BulkError` fires for plain, pre-existing Buy commits too, so this predates the provenance-upgrade work; it's just far more likely to surface once a real file with 150+ tickers is confirmed in one batch).

**Consequence, before this entry's fix**: `commitEngine.commitTicker` awaited `committedLedger.commitTicker(...)` with no error isolation (unlike the `ensureLegacyFactsExist`/`projectLegacyTicker` calls right next to it, both already try/caught). A thrown `BulkError` there aborted the *entire* calling operation — `recordSell`, `recordBuy`, `retractRawTransaction`, `assignPortfolioToFact` all sit above `commitTicker` with no catch of their own — which (a) skipped `projectLegacyTicker` for that call even though `events`/`allocations` were already computed and don't depend on the cache write succeeding, and (b) for `smartAllocateSell` specifically, meant the row's own `addedKeys` update never ran, permanently stranding it on "Smart Allocate" forever with no visible error.

**Fixed**: wrapped `committedLedger.commitTicker(...)` in the same non-fatal try/catch its two neighbors already have, so a transient cache-write failure no longer aborts the caller or skips the legacy projection.

**Not fully fixed, disclosed rather than papered over**: re-running the full reproduction after this fix, the specific stuck-forever symptom for two of ADIB's own Sell rows persisted, and the ticker's own "Opening" share count in the Constraint Check panel briefly computed an impossible negative value under the same heavy-concurrency conditions. This means the isolation fix above is necessary but not sufficient — there is a **real, unresolved data-race** somewhere in the commit pipeline when many `commitTicker`/`recordSell`/`recordBuy` calls for overlapping tickers run close together (most likely: no serialization at all between concurrent commits for the *same* ticker, so a later commit's own reads — `repos.trades.getByPortfolio` for FIFO lot selection, `relevantTradeTransactions` for verdict computation — can race an earlier commit's writes that haven't finished landing yet). Properly fixing this needs a real concurrency-control mechanism (e.g., a per-(portfolio, ticker) serialization queue around every commit-triggering write), which is a materially larger, riskier change for a financial ledger than this session had room to design and test properly — deliberately not attempted half-tested.

- **Files modified**: `commitEngine.ts` (`commitTicker`'s `committedLedger.commitTicker` call wrapped in non-fatal try/catch).
- Full suite (937 tests) still green, `tsc`/`arch:check` clean — this specific change has no unit-test coverage of its own yet (the race it partially mitigates only manifests under real concurrent load a mocked-repos unit test can't produce; the existing real-Dexie regression tests in this file don't drive enough concurrent tickers to hit it either).
- **Recommended interim workaround for real, large files** (communicated to the user): avoid the single big "Confirm — Distribute to Portfolios" click across 100+ tickers at once; confirm and allocate tickers a few at a time, giving each action a couple of seconds to visibly settle (row reads "Added", no console errors) before starting the next, until the deeper concurrency fix ships.
- **Next recommended sprint**: design and implement per-(portfolio, ticker) commit serialization in `commitEngine.ts` (queue concurrent `commitTicker` calls for the same key rather than letting them race), then re-run this exact reproduction (the user's real file, batch-confirmed) to confirm the stuck-row and impossible-share-count symptoms are actually gone, not just less frequent.

### User re-reported the SAME symptom again for ACAMD, this time explicitly WITHOUT batch-confirming — two real, independent bugs found and fixed, unrelated to the concurrency issue above

User pushed back on the concurrency explanation above with a precise counter-example: uploaded the real Excel, deliberately did **not** click the batch "Confirm — Distribute to Portfolios" button, selected only ACAMD, and clicked "Smart Allocate" once — and still got "Closed — needs corroborating evidence" for ACAMD (portfolio "Old School" — the same ticker/portfolio name as an existing regression test for this exact bug class). This ruled out the concurrency theory as the explanation for this specific report (a single click on one ticker can't race itself) and forced a fresh root-cause search, again against the user's real file in a real browser + real IndexedDB.

**Bug 1 — `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` only recognized a literal source match, not "at least as authoritative."** The historical-fallback check (added in an earlier sprint above) required every live Buy/Sell fact for a closed ticker to have `source === "official-broker-excel"` exactly. A ticker whose surviving Buy fact came from an **Invoice** (evidenceAuthority.ts rank 6 — strictly *above* the Excel export's rank 5) still fell through to the same "closed-position, no corroboration" dead-end this function exists to prevent, purely because "invoice" isn't the literal string "official-broker-excel" — even though an Invoice is objectively more trustworthy. Proven with a direct unit test (`checkTickerMatch`/`isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` given an invoice-sourced closed 3000-share ACAMD position) before any fix, then fixed by comparing `authorityRank(source) >= authorityRank("official-broker-excel")` instead of an exact string match. Regression tests added in `reconciliation.test.ts`.

**Bug 2 — a real, more broadly-impactful duplicate-detection failure: 12-hour vs. 24-hour execution-time string mismatch.** `duplicateDetection.ts`'s `timesConflict` compared `Trade.executionTime`/`TradeAllocation.executionTime` (always 24-hour `"HH:MM"`, from the Record Buy/Sell form's `<input type="time">`) against a parsed candidate's `time` (always 12-hour with an AM/PM suffix, e.g. `"12:51PM"` — both `ThndrParser` and `ThndrOrdersWorkbookParser` use this format) as **raw strings**. `"12:51PM" !== "12:51"` even though they're the same real moment, so `timesConflict` always reported a conflict for any manually-recorded historical trade that happened to have a time filled in — the auto-skip/provenance-upgrade effect in ImportPage.tsx never even attempted to match it, leaving the old manual (low-authority) fact and the new Excel (high-authority) fact **both live side by side**: double-counted shares in Holdings, and a permanently-blocked `isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` (a manual-sourced fact never gets excluded). Reproduced end-to-end: manually recorded ACAMD's real 3000-share buy via the Trades page (24-hour time "12:51"), uploaded the real broker Excel, clicked Smart Allocate once on ACAMD's sell only — result was "Closed — needs corroborating evidence" and the old manual fact stayed live (`retracted: false`) forever. Fixed by parsing both time formats to minutes-since-midnight before comparing (falls back to raw string equality only for an unrecognized format). Re-ran the identical reproduction after the fix: the manual fact is now correctly retracted, and ACAMD shows "fully matched — 2 transactions." Regression test added in `duplicateDetection.test.ts`.

- **Files modified**: `reconciliation.ts` (`isTickerFullyOfficialBrokerExcelSourced` now rank-based), `reconciliation.test.ts`, `duplicateDetection.ts` (`timesConflict` now format-aware), `duplicateDetection.test.ts`.
- Full suite (940 tests) green, `tsc --noEmit` and `arch:check` both clean.
- **Verified with a screenshot** against the user's real uploaded file, in a real browser with real IndexedDB, using their literal reported workflow (no batch confirm, single ticker, single Smart Allocate click): ACAMD moved from "Closed — needs corroborating evidence" to "Fully matched — 2 transactions."
- Both bugs are independent of the concurrency issue two entries above — that data race (many tickers/commits at once) remains a real, separate, still-open item; this entry does not close it.
- **Next recommended sprint**: still the per-(portfolio, ticker) commit serialization item above. Additionally worth a follow-up audit: search for any other place in the codebase that compares two execution-time strings directly (`orderEvidence.ts` has its own, separate `timesConflict` implementation, not touched by this fix — both sides there currently come from parser output rather than manual entry, so it wasn't reproduced as broken, but it's the same class of risk if that ever changes).

### User reported two more real bugs against ABUK/ADIB in the SAME real file: a false "Duplicate" badge on two genuinely distinct same-day Buys, and a silently-swallowed Smart Allocate/Allocate Sell failure

Both found and fixed via the same real-browser-plus-real-IndexedDB methodology, using the user's real Excel again.

**Bug 1 — `canonicalKey` (ticker/side/date/shares/price, deliberately time-blind for OTHER purposes) was also used, unguarded, everywhere a fact/trade gets matched "by value," causing wrong cross-linking whenever two genuinely distinct real executions share every field except execution time** (a common pattern: splitting a large order into smaller fills at an identical limit price, minutes apart). Reproduced with ABUK's real data: two separate 49-share buys at E£42.40 on 01 Feb 2023, one at 10:32AM and one at 10:34AM. Confirming ABUK spawned a **phantom third Trade row** (id equal to the plain canonical key itself, e.g. `"ABUK|BUY|2023-02-01|49|42.4"`, instead of a real generated id) alongside the two legitimate ones, and the Import UI showed a false "Duplicate" badge on one of the two real rows.

Root cause: `disambiguateCollidingKeys` (ledgerRebuild.ts) already exists specifically to solve "two real trades share a value" for the Ledger Engine's own `eventId`s, but three OTHER places independently re-implemented "find the fact/trade matching this value" without ever checking execution time as a tiebreaker, picking whichever same-value candidate happened to come first in array order instead:
- `TradeService.ensureBuyFact`'s `liveMatch` search
- `ledgerProjection.ts`'s `resolveExistingTradeForLot` fallback (value-key) matching
- `rawTransactionFolds.ts`'s `findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact` and `findLiveExecutionFact`

Fixed by exporting `duplicateDetection.ts`'s (already time-format-aware, from the entry above) `timesConflict` and using it as a tiebreaker in all four spots: when more than one same-value candidate exists, prefer the one whose own execution time doesn't conflict with the caller's, falling back to the first candidate (unchanged prior behavior) only when time can't disambiguate. Proven with a regression test in `TradeService.test.ts` that seeds the two facts in the OPPOSITE order from the one under test (so an order-dependent, unfixed search would still fail it), plus re-ran the exact ABUK reproduction end-to-end after the fix: both rows now show a clean "Added" with no phantom trade and no false "Duplicate" badge (screenshot captured).

**Bug 2 — a Sell row's Smart Allocate/Allocate Sell failure was completely invisible.** `smartAllocateSell`/`onAllocateSell` catch their own errors into `rowErrors[entry.key]` (via `setRowError`), exactly like the Buy side — but `CandidateRow` (the component Sell rows render through, unlike `AutoCommitRow` for Buys) never had an `error` prop at all, so nothing was ever rendered. A failing Smart Allocate click looked exactly like a placebo button: the click fires, something throws internally, and the row just silently resets with zero feedback — matching the user's own description exactly. Root-caused directly by reading `CandidateRow`'s prop list (missing `error`) and its call site (never passing `rowErrors[entry.key]`) — a real, evidenced gap, not a guess. Fixed by adding the `error` prop and rendering it identically to `AutoCommitRow`'s own pattern.

Note: reproducing the user's EXACT ADIB "Smart Allocate does nothing" failure with a fresh, single upload did NOT reproduce a thrown error — Smart Allocate succeeded cleanly there. This means the specific underlying cause of the user's own real, evidently-broken ADIB row is still unconfirmed (most likely something particular to the accumulated state of their actual account after many earlier test iterations this session, rather than a fresh-upload scenario) — but the error will now be visible on-screen the next time it happens, closing the "silent no-op" complaint regardless of which underlying cause triggers it.

- **Files modified**: `duplicateDetection.ts` (`timesConflict` exported), `TradeService.ts` (`ensureBuyFact`, `ensureSellFacts`'s call site), `TradeService.test.ts` (new regression test), `ledgerProjection.ts` (`resolveExistingTradeForLot`), `rawTransactionFolds.ts` (`findUnclaimedSellExecutionFact`, `findLiveExecutionFact`), `provenanceRepair.ts` (call site threading `executionTime` through), `ImportPage.tsx` (`CandidateRow`'s new `error` prop + render, auto-skip effect threading `time` through to `findLiveExecutionFact`).
- Full suite (941 tests) green, `tsc --noEmit` and `arch:check` both clean.
- **Verified with a screenshot** against the user's real file: both ABUK 49-share rows show "Added" with no false "Duplicate" badge.
- **Next recommended sprint**: if the ADIB "Smart Allocate does nothing" complaint recurs now that the error is actually visible, the on-screen message will name the real cause directly — no further guessing needed. Also worth a dedicated pass auditing every OTHER "match by ticker/date/shares/price" call site in the codebase for the same time-blind gap, now that this exact bug class has shown up in two unrelated modules.

### Follow-up: the ADIB "Smart Allocate does nothing" complaint DID recur, plus an ABUK share-count mismatch — both diagnosed as pre-existing corrupted DATA, not a new code bug

User re-reported two more real symptoms against the same real file: ABUK stuck at "Needs broker screenshot" with 76 shares recorded on the ledger when the true correct current holding is 27, and ADIB's last remaining Sell group failing Smart Allocate with "need 46, only 42 open."

**Diagnosis, confirmed with real numbers**: parsed the user's actual Excel directly — ABUK's real data is 38 Buy rows totaling 1,855 shares and 8 Sell rows totaling 1,828 shares, net = **27**, exactly matching the user's own stated correct figure. So the Excel itself is not misread, and 76 is not a parsing error — it's leftover **DATA corruption from before this session's fixes shipped** (the two bugs above, and the still-open commit-concurrency issue from the earlier entry) that already wrote bad `Trade`/`TradeAllocation` rows into the user's real "Old School" portfolio. Code fixes only change what happens on *future* commits — they cannot retroactively repair rows already written wrong.

**Checked whether the existing "Rebuild Ledger" tool (ledgerRebuild.ts) already self-heals this now that `timesConflict` is fixed**: reproduced the exact corrupted state (temporarily reverted the fix commit, re-ran the real ABUK import, confirmed a phantom-shaped Trade id reappeared, restored the fix) and ran a dry run against it. Result: `diffBuys` (which now benefits from the time-aware `findDuplicateBuyMatch`) correctly paired every existing Trade — including the oddly-id'd one — to its own distinct canonical entry, reporting **zero** trades to remove or modify. This makes sense once the data is understood: the "phantom-id" Trade this bug class produces still holds perfectly valid share/price/time data for a real execution, so from a pure ledger-vs-documents diff it's indistinguishable from a normal row. Rebuild Ledger is therefore not the right tool for this — the actual damage (if any) sits in stale `remainingShares`/allocation state from a sell that got applied under the old buggy matching, which Rebuild Ledger's diff never touches (`diffTradeFields` doesn't compare `remainingShares` at all).

**Verified remediation, end-to-end, with the fix live**: used the existing per-ticker "Reset" control (the trash icon next to the ticker name in Import — `purgeTickerData`, already shipped) to fully wipe ABUK, then re-uploaded the same real Excel and re-confirmed it. Result: 38 Buy trades, 1,855 shares — exactly right, no phantom, no false "Duplicate." Then allocated all 8 Sells via Smart Allocate **one at a time, waiting for each to settle** before the next: final remaining share count landed at exactly **27** — matching the user's own stated correct figure precisely.

**A real methodological trap, caught and disclosed rather than hidden**: an earlier attempt at this same verification clicked through the 8 Sells back-to-back without waiting, and hit a **false** "Not enough open shares" error partway through — not a new bug, but the SAME already-disclosed, not-yet-fixed commit-concurrency race from two entries above, self-inflicted by rapid-fire clicking in the test itself. Confirmed by re-running the identical sequence slowly: it completes cleanly every time. This means the interim workaround already given to the user (process one action at a time, wait for "Added" before the next) is not just about the big batch button — it applies to Sell allocation too, until the per-ticker commit serialization fix ships.

- **No code change in this entry** — this was a data/diagnosis investigation, not a bug fix. Nothing to test/deploy.
- **Recommended action communicated to the user**: for any ticker whose share count still looks wrong from before the fixes shipped, use the ticker's "Reset" (trash icon) in Import, re-upload the same broker Excel, re-confirm its Buys, then allocate its Sells one at a time — waiting for each row to show "Added" (no error text underneath) before starting the next — rather than clicking through several Smart Allocate buttons in quick succession.
- **Next recommended sprint**: still the per-(portfolio, ticker) commit serialization item from two entries above — this incident is further, independent evidence that it's the real remaining gap, this time surfacing on the Sell/allocation side rather than the Buy/fact side. Once that ships, the "reset + carefully re-import" workaround should no longer be necessary even for large, many-sell tickers.
